801 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Newman


DOCKET NO. A-1374-98T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


325 N.J. Super. 556; 740 A.2d 153; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 358


September 28, 1999, Submitted  
November 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cumberland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from criminal conviction and 10-year term of imprisonment in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cumberland County, following defendant's plea of guilty, and imposition of an 8 1/2 -year parole ineligibility term with a 3-year term of parole supervision pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-7.2.


OVERVIEW: Following charges of felony murder, robbery and burglary, defendant pleaded guilty to the amended offense of reckless manslaughter. The trial court imposed a 10-year prison term, and an 8 1/2 -year parole ineligibility term with a 3-year term of parole supervision, pursuant to the No Early Release Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-7.2. On appeal, defendant argued that the Act's absence of a degree of culpability required courts to insert "knowingly" as the degree of culpability required to apply the Act, and second-degree reckless manslaughter was not a "violent crime" within the Act's intendment. The court affirmed, holding first that the plain language of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-2c(3), creating the need to impute the "knowingly" culpability standard, only applied to statutes defining offenses. Second, the plain language of the Act, defining a violent crime as one in which the actor caused death, clearly applied to reckless manslaughter.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed, because the plain language of the act, creating the need to impute the "knowingly" culpability standard, only applied to statutes defining offenses, and clearly applied to reckless manslaughter. The parole ineligibility did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

 

802 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


City of Camden v. Whitman


A-7096-97T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


325 N.J. Super. 236; 738 A.2d 969; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 340


September 14, 1999, Submitted  
October 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Local Finance Board, Department of Community Affairs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: City of Camden appealed from the Local Finance Board, New Jersey Department of Community Affairs seeking a declaratory judgment that a provision of the New Jersey General Appropriations Act for 1998-1999, L. 1998, c. 45, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The City of Camden sought a declaratory judgment that a provision of the New Jersey General Appropriations Act for 1998-1999, L. 1998, c. 45 was unconstitutional. The Act authorized the Local Finance Board (Board) to create a financial review board to approve, implement and enforce a financial plan for the City of Camden. The City contended the authorization to create the financial review board violated the New Jersey Constitution's mandates that legislative acts have a single object and that the Legislature could not pass special laws regulating the internal affairs of municipalities. The court held that the issues raised were moot. Not only had the time for effective supervision of the 1998-99 fiscal year long passed, but Camden had agreed to continue fiscal supervision by its financial review board as part of its new distressed city aid from the state.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed as moot due to passing of time for effective supervision of appellant city's 1998-99 fiscal year and it had agreed to continue fiscal supervision by its financial review board.

 

803 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


New Jersey Shore Builders Ass'n v. Township of South Brunswick


A-5114-97T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


325 N.J. Super. 412; 739 A.2d 956; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 330


September 13, 1999, Argued  
October 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 8, 1999. As Amended October 27, 1999. Second Correction December 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County which granted summary judgment to plaintiff associations who challenged appellant's water detention basin maintenance ordinance as exceeding appellant's authority under the state's Municipal Land Use Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-53.


OVERVIEW: Three associations of developers challenged appellant's ordinance requiring maintenance of water detention basins, contending the ordinance exceeded appellant's municipal authority under the Municipal Land Use Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-53, and was unconstitutional. Appellant moved for summary judgment, contending plaintiffs lacked standing, in addition to untimely filing. The trial judge disqualified himself due to a conflict of interest, sent the standing issue to another judge, then subsequently heard the substantive issues, declaring the ordinance unlawful on its face. Appellant appealed. The court reversed and remanded because a disqualification required the judge step aside from all issues in the case; the court was not relieved of its duty to make findings if a standing issue was suspect, and the trial court's decision on the substantive issue was inadequate for the court's review and must be addressed on remand.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded because disqualification required the judge step aside from all issues in case; the court was not relieved of its duty to make findings if standing issue was suspect, and decision on substantive issue was inadequate for review and must be addressed on remand.

State v. Johnson


A-773-98T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


325 N.J. Super. 78; 737 A.2d 1140; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 326


September 14, 1999, Argued  
October 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 7, 1999.
Certification denied by State v. Johnson, 163 N.J. 12, 746 A.2d 458, 2000 N.J. LEXIS 113 (2000)
Modified by, Affirmed by State v. Johnson, 166 N.J. 523, 766 A.2d 1126, 2001 N.J. LEXIS 179 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Johnson, 2009 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 903 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, resulting in guilty verdict of first-degree robbery, second-degree possession of a firearm with intent to use it unlawfully against a person, and third-degree possession of a firearm without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of first-degree robbery and second-degree possession of firearm with intent to use it unlawfully against a person, was sentenced under the No Early Release Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-7.2d, which mandated a parole ineligibility term of 85 percent of the base term be imposed on individuals convicted of violent crimes. Defendant appealed, contending his rights were violated because his peremptory challenges were not allowed and his sentence violated constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment. The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded for re-sentencing on the second-degree conviction. The court held that a defendant could not make race-based juror challenges. The court refused to consider the constitutional issue since it was not raised at trial. Finally, the court remanded the second-degree conviction for re-sentencing because defendant's conviction of a purely possessive crime did not meet statutory definition of violent criminal.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The defendant could not make race-based juror challenges and the court refused to consider the constitutional issue since it was not raised at trial. Since defendant's conviction of a purely possessive crime did not meet statutory definition of violent crime, the court remanded for re-sentencing.

Pollution Control Financing Authority of Warren County v. County of Somerset


A-5679-97T1 AND A-5927-97T1 (Consolidated)


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


324 N.J. Super. 391; 735 A.2d 633; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 302


April 20, 1999, Argued  
August 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Warren County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Warren County, which incorporated prior orders for summary judgment and an order denying reconsideration. These orders were entered in favor of defendants relieving them from any further obligation to deliver solid waste to the incinerator or to pay for failing to deliver it.


OVERVIEW: By an agreement made pursuant to state waste regulations, defendants, county and hauler, promised to deliver a set amount of waste to plaintiff's incinerator and to pay for the processing of that amount of waste, whether delivered or not. After federal cases held that such regulations and agreements were unconstitutional as per se discrimination, the defendants ceased deliveries and payments. In the subsequent suit, the trial court granted summary judgment for defendants, declaring the contract was unenforceable as a matter of law. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that there were material facts in dispute, that the court misinterpreted or misapplied the governing law, and that the defendant hauler, who was not an original signatory to the agreement but was party to a settlement agreement, was still liable. The court held that, since the agreement was retroactively void and unenforceable, and the settlement agreement was vacated, the defendants could not be liable.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed as to enforceability of contract between plaintiffs and defendants; remanded to determine equitable allocation of financial burden, and to join another county as a party.

 

806 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Revocation of Access of Block 1901, Lot No. 1, Borough of Paramus, Bergen County Parkway 17 Associates


A-2073-98T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


324 N.J. Super. 322; 735 A.2d 594; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 295


April 19, 1999, Argued  
August 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 19, 1999. Approved for Publication August 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Department of Transportation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Transportation which revoked its existing highway access permit concerning passage between its property and the southbound lane of a state highway.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, landowner, appealed a decision of the Commissioner of the Department of Transportation, which revoked petitioner's existing highway access permit concerning passage between its property and a state highway. The Department of Transportation (DOT) purported to act under authority of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 27:7-94, which authorizes such a revocation provided that suitable "alternative access" is available. The DOT claimed the existing access did not meet current access standards and that it provided suitable alternative access. Petitioner claimed, however, that the proposed alternative access was unsuitable and did not comply with statutory standards. The court applied the five elements which N.J. Stat. Ann. § 27:7-94c(1) incorporates that must be satisfied in order for a proposed new access plan to constitute "reasonable alternative access," and concluded that with respect to each of those five elements, there was ample evidence to support the conclusion that the DOT had met its burden.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; while petitioner's alternative plan of access should have been considered, refusal to do so was not prejudicial error.

Roman Check Cashing, Inc. v. New Jersey Dept. of Banking and Ins.


A-0351-98T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


324 N.J. Super. 58; 734 A.2d 346; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 296


June 11, 1999, Argued  
August 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State of New Jersey Department of Banking and Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision of the State of New Jersey Department of Banking and Insurance that denied plaintiff a license operate a check cashing facility.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was denied a license to be a check cashing facility because it was located too close to another check cashing facility. The court reversed the denial and remanded. The court held N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:15-A-41c, the statute proscribing the geographic limitations separating check cashing facilities, was invalid. The court held the statute was not rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. The court held distance requirements did not relate to the economic health or stability of the check cashing business.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of plaintiff's license and remanded because the statute proscribing distance requirements for check cashing facilities was invalid.

 

808 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Green Party of New Jersey v. Hartz Mountain Industries, Inc.


A-938-98T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


324 N.J. Super. 192; 735 A.2d 9; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 286


June 1, 1999, Argued  
August 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 3, 1999. As Corrected November 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a shopping mall, appealed an order of the New Jersey Chancery Division court that entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs in an action concerning defendant's restrictions on leaflet distributing at the mall.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, non-profit political activists, filed suit after defendant, a shopping mall, restricted plaintiffs use of the mall for distributing leaflets. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs. The court reversed. The court held defendant could establish objectively reasonable regulations regarding the time, place, and manner of plaintiffs' use of the mall. The court held defendant's regulation limiting the use of the mall by each organization to one day or a few consecutive days was reasonable. The court also held defendant's requirement that each organization have an insurance policy and sign a hold harmless agreement was proper. The court held defendant had a right to protect itself against liability that was imposed on defendant due to defendant's position of operating a public mall.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs because defendant's regulations, limiting the use of the mall by leaflet distributors, were reasonable.

 

809 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


WHS Realty Co. v. Town of Morristown


A-3502-97T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


323 N.J. Super. 553; 733 A.2d 1206; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 278


May 24, 1999, Argued  
July 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, conducted a plenary hearing to determine that defendants' garbage collection ordinance violated plaintiff's equal protection rights because the classification scheme bore no rational relationship to any legitimate state interest. However, the trial court found plaintiff failed to establish a prima facie case for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant town passed a garbage collection ordinance providing free collection service to all residential dwellings of three or less units as well as certain condominium developments. As a multi-family dwelling of four or more units, plaintiff's apartment complex did not receive such service. Claiming the ordinance violated its constitutional rights to due process and equal protection, plaintiff sought the same garbage collection service provided to all other residents as well as compensatory damages and attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988. After plenary hearing, the trial court reaffirmed a prior determination that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest. However, the trial court denied plaintiff's demand for damages under § 1983 and counsel fees under § 1988, and parties appealed. Finding plaintiff proved the classification lacked any rational basis, the court struck the ordinance. Moreover, defendants' good faith in enacting and enforcing ordinance was no defense to plaintiff's § 1983 claim for damages. Thus, the court remanded to determine if plaintiff had a viable claim for damages and counsel fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that defendants' garbage collection ordinance violated plaintiff's equal protection rights because the classification scheme was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest, but reversed its holding that plaintiff failed to state a prima facie civil rights claim for deprivation of constitutional rights and therefore remanded for a hearing on damages and counsel fees under federal law.

 

810 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


City of Ocean City v. Maffucci


A-5224-97T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


326 N.J. Super. 1; 740 A.2d 630; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 391


April 13, 1999, Submitted  
July 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which held that appellees, condominium owners, were entitled to severance damages for the city's easement. Appellant objected to the court's finding that the easement blocked appellees' view of the ocean and constituted a considerable loss of privacy.


OVERVIEW: Appellees owned beachfront condominiums with an ocean view. Appellant city attempted to purchase an easement from appellees, and they refused. After a hearing on the matter, commissioners appointed to appraise the value of the easement taken by appellant city issued a report and valued the easement at $ 1. A court proceeding ensued and the trial court held in favor of appellees. The trial court held that the easement completely blocked appellants' view of the ocean and that appellees were entitled to severance damages based on this obstructed view. The city appealed and the court reviewed all expert testimony. The court concluded that although appellees' expert did not state the specific date of the taking, his evidence was temporally relevant to that date, and was stated with sufficient particularity to support a compensable loss of beach view and access by appellees. The court affirmed the trial court's award, holding that there was evidence to support the conclusion that appellees lost their ocean view, beach access, and privacy.


OUTCOME: Appellant city was not granted relief on review, and the court sustained the decision of the trial court, which held that appellees, condominium owners, were entitled to severance damages for the city's easement. After a review of the record, the court held that appellant's easement blocked appellees' view of the ocean and constituted a considerable loss of privacy to appellees.

 

811 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warriner


A-6430-97T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


322 N.J. Super. 401; 731 A.2d 86; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 228


June 2, 1999, Argued  
June 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 29, 1999.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Warriner, 2006 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 170 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed a decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, ruling that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:25-17 to -33, outlawing assault weapons, was unconstitutionally vague. Defendant cross-appealed the denial of his application to the Pretrial Intervention Program.


OVERVIEW: As a result of a domestic violence restraining order, defendant was required to turn over all of his weapons to the police. One of the weapons was an assault rifle with a barrel labeled "Universal M1 autoloading carbine." The trial court found that N.J. Stat. Ann. §2C:39-1w(1) listing "M1 carbine type" as an assault weapon was unconstitutionally vague, both facially and as applied. On appeal, the court ruled that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied as the stamp on the rifle gave sufficient notice to defendant that the gun had the basic design proscribed by the statute. On the cross-appeal, defendant challenged the decision by the prosecutor to deny his application for admission to the Pretrial Intervention (PTI) program. In affirming the decision the court held that judicial review of prosecutorial decisions on diversion into PTI was available to check only the most egregious examples of injustice and unfairness. The court found no unfairness as rejection was based on the large number of weapons and the illegal rifle possessed by defendant and the potential for violence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision finding the statute outlawing M1 type carbine weapons as unconstitutionally vague as applied based upon the labeling on defendant's assault rifle. The court affirmed the decision denying defendant entry into the Pretrial Intervention program based upon his potential for violence.

 

812 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Binkowski v. State


A-3963-97T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


322 N.J. Super. 359; 731 A.2d 64; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 221


February 17, 1999, Argued  
June 24, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 24, 1999. As Amended July 14, 1999. Second Correction August 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hunting protestors appealed from the judgment of the Hudson County Superior Court (New Jersey) dismissing their complaint for declaratory relief and ruling that the Hunter Harassment Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:7A-1 et seq., was not facially overbroad, vague, or impermissibly content-based, in violation of plaintiffs rights under U.S. Const. amend. I, and did not violate their equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff hunting protestors brought a declaratory judgment action challenging the facial constitutionality of the Hunter Harassment Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:7A-1 et seq., claiming, inter alia, that it violated hunting opponents' rights to free speech and equal protection, under U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. Upon cross-motions for summary judgment, the complaint was dismissed and plaintiffs appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that the statute was not a impermissible content-based restriction of anti-hunting speech; rather, by its terms, it plainly regulated conduct that was not sufficiently expressive to constitute speech. The statute aimed only to proscribe the hindering of a person engaged in the lawful taking of wildlife by hunting and it was not intended to favor pro-hunting advocates to the exclusion of the anti-hunting viewpoint. The terms of the statute were not vague, unclear, or imprecise and there was no real and substantial deterrent effect on legitimate expression. Moreover, the statute was not overbroad; it applied only in limited areas and only where the actor had the wrongful intent to interfere with the lawful taking of wildlife.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the challenge to the statute was affirmed because the statute did not regulate speech, but prohibited the non-expressive conduct of physically interfering with hunters with the intent of interfering with the lawful taking of wildlife; it was not substantially overbroad and its terms were sufficiently clear and precise; and it did not impermissibly endorse the viewpoint of hunters at the expense of protesters.

 

813 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aguiar


DOCKET NO. A-2569-97T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


322 N.J. Super. 175; 730 A.2d 463; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 214


June 3, 1999, Submitted  
June 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 17, 1999. As Corrected June 28, 1999. Second Correction July 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, of aggravated manslaughter and possession of a handgun without a permit. He petitioned for post-conviction relief, asserting that the prosecutor had concealed evidence of the victim's prior criminal conviction for murder.


OVERVIEW: After an unsuccessful appeal of his conviction for manslaughter and possession of a handgun without a permit, defendant learned that his victim had a prior murder conviction. He petitioned for post-conviction relief, and contended that the prosecutor had concealed the conviction; he asserted alternatively that if the prosecution had provided the defense with the evidence, his trial attorney was derelict in failing to use it to bolster defendant's claim of self-defense. At trial the prosecution characterized the victim as a nonviolent, peaceful individual, and the defense unsuccessfully attempted to prove that the victim had a violent and aggressive personality. The victim's conviction for a violent crime was admissible to show that he was the aggressor in the context of a claim of self-defense; and thus the victim's prior murder conviction was potentially admissible to establish his violent character and his conduct on the date of the killing. Therefore, the matter was remanded for consideration of defendant's alternative claims of unconstitutional concealment of exculpatory evidence by the prosecution or ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: An order denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was reversed and the matter was remanded, where evidence of the victim's prior murder conviction was either concealed by the prosecution or defendant's counsel failed to use the conviction to bolster defendant's claim of self-defense, and defendant was convicted of manslaughter. The victim's conviction was potentially admissible to show he had a violent and aggressive personality.

 

814 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


American Trucking Associations, Inc. v. State


NO. A-6334-97T3F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


324 N.J. Super. 1; 734 A.2d 314; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 207


January 21, 1999, Argued  
June 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1999..
Appeal granted by American Trucking Ass'ns v. State, 162 N.J. 124, 741 A.2d 93, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1203 (1999)
Appeal granted by American Trucking Ass'ns v. State, 162 N.J. 124, 741 A.2d 93, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1204 (1999)
Remanded by American Trucking Ass'ns v. State, 164 N.J. 183, 752 A.2d 1286, 2000 N.J. LEXIS 792 (2000)
Reversed by, Remanded by Am. Trucking Ass'ns v. State, 180 N.J. 377, 852 A.2d 142, 2004 N.J. LEXIS 910 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Tax Court.
American Trucking Ass'ns v. Department of Envtl. Protection, 154 N.J. 604, 713 A.2d 497, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 630 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case came to the court on remand by the Supreme Court (New Jersey), which granted a motion by defendant, New Jersey, for leave to appeal a tax court order granting partial summary judgment to plaintiffs, a trucking association and others, in a class action. The tax court ruled that hazardous waste transporter registration fees, authorized under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:1E-18, violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a tax court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a trucking association and others, in a class action suit, and remanded to the tax court. The tax court had ruled that the hazardous waste transporter registration fees adopted by defendant, New Jersey, to register and track vehicles engaged in the collection or delivery of hazardous waste in the state constituted a burden upon interstate commerce under a dormant Commerce Clause analysis. The court rejected as premature, and probably unnecessary, the tax court's grant of summary judgment. The court found that state courts had jurisdiction to make separate and varying rulings as to the commerce impact of the hazardous waste hauling fees of their respective states. But a final judgment, and particularly summary judgment, should not issue in New Jersey absent critical input from the United States Department of Transportation (USDOT). The USDOT had been charged by Congress with administration of the Hazardous Materials Transportation Act, 49 U.S.C.S. §§ 5101-5127, to promote uniformity and to ensure fairness of hazardous waste hauling fees imposed by the respective states.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a grant of summary judgment and remanded the matter to a tax court because a final judgment should not issue in the state without input from the United States Department of Transportation, which was charged with promoting uniformity and ensuring the fairness of hazardous waste hauling fees imposed by the respective states.

 

815 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Bell Atlantic Network Services, Inc. v. P.M. Video Corp.


A-6440-96T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


322 N.J. Super. 74; 730 A.2d 406; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 201


March 30, 1999, Argued  
June 11, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 11, 1999. As Amended July 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, judgment disallowing projected lost profits and vacating punitive damage award. Plaintiff alleged error in allowing defendant telephone company to argue they had not committed fraud and by prohibiting jury from considering projected lost profits. Defendants cross-appealed alleging judicial estoppel barred a fraud claim and insufficient evidence for punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: In plaintiff's suit against defendants, telephone company and its employee, for fraudulent inducement to enter into a contract, plaintiff sought to recover compensatory damages, projected lost profits, and punitive damages. Compensatory damages were awarded. Consideration of projected lost profits was disallowed, because plaintiff's proof was too speculative to permit consideration by a jury. Evidence was sufficient to show that repeated acts of defendant employee were accompanied by wanton and willful disregard of plaintiff's right to profit from its proprietary information and from efforts of its employees. Therefore, punitive damages were warranted. At the first trial, the punitive damage award was so disproportionate to the amount of actual harm as to shock the court's conscience. Thus, granting a new trial to determine punitive damages was not a miscarriage of justice. The second trial was rendered unfair because of confusion as to what was to be tried. The defendant argued improper points for a trial on punitive damages only. Therefore, plaintiff was entitled to a new trial, if it so chose, but that trial would have to address plaintiff's right to punitive damages.


OUTCOME: Judgment for compensatory and punitive damages to plaintiff was affirmed, but the cause was remanded to permit plaintiff to exercise its right to a new trial on punitive damages should it so choose. Evidence was sufficient to show fraud by defendant employee in his repeated acts with wanton and willful disregard of plaintiff's right to profits. The trial on punitive damages was rendered unfair because of confusion as to what was to be tried.

 

816 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Damiano


A-5116-96T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


322 N.J. Super. 22; 730 A.2d 376; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 197


March 9, 1999, Argued  
June 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Sussex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a trial by jury, defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Sussex County, of 44 theft and sales tax crimes of the second, third, and fourth degree, all arising out of his operation of an automobile dealership. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a financially distress Chrysler dealership. He was inexperienced in operating a car dealership and was undercapitalized and suffered immediate cash flow problems. Before defendant left and ceased doing business, he failed to pay off the liens and to obtain properly executed certificates of title with evidence of satisfaction of the debt for several buyers of new or used cars each traded in cars that had outstanding liens held by financial institutions. There were also problems with extended warranties. A jury convicted defendant of theft and sales tax crimes. The court reversed and remanded. For criminal liability to attach to the acts or course of conduct of a businessman, who was on the brink of insolvency, there must be criminal intent and culpability as defined by the criminal statutes. The court found that the jury was not appraised of the distinction between civil and criminal concepts and, therefore, had insufficient guidance in the determinations required of it. The court then detailed the deficiencies in the instructions as to each set of related charges against defendant. It also discussed certain erroneous and prejudicial evidentiary rulings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of convictions was reversed and the case remanded for the dismissal of six counts of the indictment and for retrial of all remaining counts. There was substantial error in the charge to the jury, coupled with erroneous evidential rulings.

In re Charter School Appeal of Greater Brunswick Charter School


A-4557-97T1F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


332 N.J. Super. 409; 753 A.2d 1155; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 464


April 14, 1999, Submitted  
May 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 28, 2000. As Amended July 18, 2000. Second Correction August 30, 2000.
Certification granted by In re Greater Brunswick Charter Sch. (Highland Park Bd. of Educ.), 162 N.J. 482, 744 A.2d 1205, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1692 (1999)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by In re Grant of the Charter Sch. Application of the Greater Brunswick Charter Sch., 164 N.J. 314, 753 A.2d 686, 2000 N.J. LEXIS 664 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district board sought review of the decision of the state board of education (New Jersey), which affirmed approval of respondent charter school's application to begin operations under the Charter School Program Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:36A et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondent charter school applied to begin operations under the Charter School Program Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:36A et seq. Appellant school district board objected. Reviewers found defects in the application, but they were never cured. The charter school submitted addenda to the application. The New Jersey Commissioner of Education (commissioner) approved the application. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed because the reviewers did not find that the entire curriculum was inadequate, the commissioner's decision was not based on non-objective criteria, the commissioner had authority to ask respondent for addenda, that the charter school's head did not have principal's certification did not void the charter, any adverse impacts on appellant's financial health were in the nature of disagreements with the legislature's educational policy and had no judicial remedy, and appellant did not establish that the Act was unconstitutional for failing to compel consideration of race in the application process.


OUTCOME: Affirmation of approval of respondent charter school's application was affirmed because the approval was not based on non-objective criteria, the education commissioner had authority to ask for application addenda, adverse impacts on appellant school district board's financial health had no judicial remedy, and the charter school act was constitutional.

A-2572-97T5, A-3856-97T5, A-4052-97T5

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiffs appealed an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, which, pursuant N.J. Ct. R. 1:13-4(a), transferred to another jurisdiction the coordinated action of defendant county and plaintiff utilities authority to assure repayment of a certain debt.


OVERVIEW: These consolidated appeals addressed the coordinated actions of defendant county and plaintiff utilities authority to assure repayment of debt issued by plaintiff. The ability of plaintiff to meet its debt obligations was jeopardized by the invalidation of the state imposed solid waste management plan and the consequent drop in plaintiff's revenue. A suit was filed that sought to declare defendant's refunding bond deficiency agreement with plaintiff unconstitutional. Plaintiffs appealed after the trial court transferred the entirely of the consolidated cases pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 1:13-4(a). The court found that such transfer was proper. Stat. Ann. § 40:14B-1 to -69. Finally, the court concluded that the deficiency agreement, by which defendants agreed to guarantee the payment of unsecured revenue bonds issued by plaintiffs, was a constitutional use of public funds for a private purpose. Accordingly, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order, which transferred defendant county and plaintiff utilities authority's coordinated action to another jurisdiction, was proper. Accordingly, the order was affirmed.

State v. Oliver


A-7124-96T3, A-7268-96T1, A-7303-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


320 N.J. Super. 405; 727 A.2d 491; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 127


March 16, 1999, Argued  
April 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 13, 1999.
Certification denied by State v. Oliver, 161 N.J. 332, 736 A.2d 525, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1039 (1999)
Certification denied by State v. Morgan, 161 N.J. 332, 736 A.2d 525, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1040 (1999)
Certification denied by State v. Schmidt, 161 N.J. 332, 736 A.2d 525, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1041 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for creating a physically dangerous condition and obstructing the administration of law in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:33-2a(2) and 2C:29-1a, and violating municipal ordinances permitting the closing of beaches and prohibiting bathing under certain conditions from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey).


OVERVIEW: After a tropical storm, authorities closed the beach. Despite the closure, defendants went surfboarding and were subsequently convicted of creating a physically dangerous condition, obstructing the administration of law, violating an ordinance permitting the closure of beaches, and violating an ordinance prohibiting bathing under certain conditions. Defendants appealed, and the court affirmed. The court disagreed with defendants' contention that the municipal court lacked jurisdiction to hear their case. The municipal court was granted territorial and subject matter jurisdiction over cases arising with regard to premises or property located partly in and partly outside the municipality. The court further held that the municipal ordinances under which defendants were convicted were not unconstitutionally vague. An ordinance was facially vague only if there was no conduct that it proscribed with sufficient certainty. An ordinance was vague as applied if it did not clearly prohibit the conduct on which the particular charges were based. Neither form of vagueness was found here.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions for creating a physically dangerous condition, obstructing the administration of law, violating ordinance allowing closure of beaches, and violating ordinance prohibiting bathing under certain conditions were affirmed. Municipal court had both territorial and subject matter jurisdiction over their trial. Municipal ordinances were not unconstitutionally vague on their face or as applied.

Camden County Energy Recovery Associates, L.P. v. New Jersey Dept. of Environmental Protection


A-3-98T3

Appeal granted by Camden County Energy Recovery Assocs. v. New Jersey Dep't of Envtl. Protection, 161 N.J. 328, 736 A.2d 522, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1176 (1999)
Appeal granted by Camden County Energy Recovery Assocs. v. New Jersey Dep't of Envtl. Protection, 161 N.J. 329, 736 A.2d 522, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1177 (1999)
Appeal granted by Camden County Energy Recovery Assocs. v. New Jersey Dep't of Envtl. Protection, 161 N.J. 329, 736 A.2d 523, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1180 (1999)
Affirmed by Camden County Energy Recovery Assocs., L.P. v. N.J. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 170 N.J. 246, 786 A.2d 105, 2001 N.J. LEXIS 1508 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey that reserved a decision for the state's motion to dismiss all claims against it for failure to state claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff received a franchise for the disposal of solid waste from a county located within defendant state. Construction of the facility was financed through bonds issued by the county pollution control financing authority (PCFA). As a result of a district court decision striking down the defendant's waste control policy, resource recovery facilities were no longer guaranteed to receive a certain quantity of waste. Plaintiff brought suit to restrain the PCFA from opening new bids for the operation of the facility. PCFA and the county asserted cross claims against defendant seeking indemnification for any loss they might incur. The trial court reserved defendant's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed the decision. Plaintiff argued that a contractual relationship between itself and the defendant was created when plaintiff was granted the franchise. The court disagreed and held that, although the defendant's policy was constitutionally flawed, it did not create an enforceable contractual right for the litigants. Moreover, the court reasoned that the parties must approach the legislative and executive branches of government to obtain relief.


OUTCOME: The reversed the decision of the trial court to reserve defendant state's motion to dismiss. The court held that a motion to dismiss was proper because the defendant was not contractually bound to any of the litigants.

In re Grant of Charter School Application of Englewood on Palisades Charter School


A-4697-97T1, A-4825-97T1, A-4973-97T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


320 N.J. Super. 174; 727 A.2d 15; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 103

March 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 29, 1999. As Corrected April 16, 1999. As Amended May 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school districts challenged decisions from the State Board of Education (New Jersey) that granted approval of three charter applications. Appellants challenged various aspects of the Charter School Program Act of 1995, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:36A-1 to -18, and its application in practice.


OVERVIEW: The State Board of Education granted charters to three respondent schools. Appellant school districts challenged the decision, various aspects of the Charter School Program Act of 1995, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:36A-1 to -18, and its application in practice. Appellants further argued that the Charter School Program Act was unconstitutional because it breached the equal protection rights of parents and students in the existing school districts, to the advantage of the charter schools. The court rejected this argument and affirmed the decision below.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the charters below, finding none of the challenges advanced by appellant school districts persuasive. The court found that while the decisions of the Commissioner and State Board of Education could have been more expansive, they were adequately comprehensive and sufficiently detailed to warrant the court's deference.

Brown v. Township of Old Bridge


A-0522-97T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


319 N.J. Super. 476; 725 A.2d 1154; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 93


February 10, 1999, Argued  
March 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 19, 1999.
Certification denied by Brown v. Township of Old Bridge, 162 N.J. 131, 741 A.2d 99, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 1234 (1999)
Related proceeding at Frank v. Township of Old Bridge, 2007 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2118 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.
Brown v. Township of Old Bridge, 144 N.J. 587, 677 A.2d 759, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 799 (1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County (New Jersey), that reversed an award of disability retirement benefits given to plaintiff in a suit to enforce a resolution passed by defendant township.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee worked as a police officer for defendant township until disability forced him to retire. In a resolution passed by defendant, plaintiff was given his full salary, disability benefits, accrued vacation and sick time, and health benefits. After defendant failed to pay disability benefits, plaintiff filed suit. Plaintiff was awarded disability benefits at trial. On appeal, the court held that the resolution was unenforceable and that the award was nevertheless excessive. On the appeal here, the court affirmed. The collective bargaining agreement which permitted receipt of disability benefits in excess of the statutory maximum level was unenforceable because statutes covering public employee benefits could not be contravened by negotiated agreement. Further, application of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-154, which limited the compensation for permanent disability was not unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff. The statute did not violate the Contracts Clause because it did not substantially impair a contractual relationship. The statute also did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it was rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversing award of disability benefits to plaintiff employee was affirmed because the collective bargaining agreement giving plaintiff benefits in excess of the statutory maximum was unenforceable. Statute limiting disability retirement compensation was not unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause or the Contracts Clause.

In re Markel Ins. Companies


A-1460-97T2, A-1889-97T5, A-1890-97T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


319 N.J. Super. 23; 724 A.2d 848; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 61


January 25, 1999, Argued  
March 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Banking and Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the decision of the Department of Banking and Insurance (New Jersey), which determined that a special purpose apportionment authorized under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:1C-19 - 17:1C-32, which applied to appellants as surplus lines insurers, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent commissioner issued notices of assessment against appellant surplus lines insurers (SLI) pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:1C-19 - 17:1C-32. Appellants claimed they had insufficient connections with New Jersey to qualify as insurers doing business in New Jersey and that, therefore, application of the act was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the decision upholding the constitutionality of the act. SLI insured risks, adjusted claims, and were amenable to suit in New Jersey. Those factors indicated a presence in New Jersey related to the business of insurance. The taxation of SLI did not violate their right to substantive due process. SLI ability to insure risks in New Jersey and the Department of Banking and Insurance's expenses in the discharge of oversight responsibilities satisfied the constitutional test for due process limits on a state's power to tax out of state corporations. New Jersey's purpose for the tax, to obtain reimbursement for the cost of regulatory oversight of SLI, was a legitimate state interest and did not violate equal protection. The department was not constrained by the Commerce Clause in regulating out of state insurers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision that a statute imposing a special purpose apportionment on surplus line insurers was constitutional. The court found that surplus line insurers had sufficient connections with New Jersey to warrant application of the statute because they insured risks within the state. For the same reason, the court held that the statute did not violate appellants' right to substantive due process.

Barreiro v. Morais


A-229-97T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


318 N.J. Super. 461; 723 A.2d 1244; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 48


November 17, 1998, Argued  
February 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 23, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, that dismissed with prejudice their medical malpractice complaint for failure to comply with the Affidavit of Merit Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:53A-27.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' son died after being treated by defendants, a hospital and several of its doctors. Plaintiffs engaged the services of counsel, who requested the medical records on the son. Plaintiff's counsel did not receive the medical records until after some delay by defendants. The records proved indecipherable and a requested translation was not received until after more delay. Defendants later moved to dismiss for plaintiff's failure to comply with the Affidavit of Merit Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:53A-27, which was granted with prejudice because plaintiffs did not file an affidavit by an expert stating their claim was meritorious within the applicable time period. On appeal, the court found that the circumstances of the case, particularly the delay by defendants in providing decipherable records, were so extraordinary that a dismissal without prejudice before the statute of limitations ran would have been necessary, because plaintiffs did not have the opportunity to present evidence on the issue of such extraordinary circumstances. This was pursuant to a decision by the state's high court decided after the trial court's opinion. The order was vacated and the case remanded.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of plaintiffs' medical malpractice complaint with prejudice for their failure to comply with the Affidavit of Merit Statute was vacated. The court found that a dismissal without prejudice would have been necessary, in light of a decision of the state's high court decided after the trial court's opinion, due to the extraordinary circumstances of the case. The matter was remanded to allow plaintiffs to present evidence on that issue.

Village of Ridgefield Park v. New York, Susquehanna and Western Ry. Corp.


A-3817-97T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


318 N.J. Super. 385; 724 A.2d 267; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 37


December 2, 1998, Argued  
February 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality, having seen its public nuisance lawsuit against respondent railroad corporation dismissed on summary judgment by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, on the grounds that federal preemption barred review, sought reversal of that order.


OVERVIEW: Appellant municipality filed suit against respondent railroad corporation, seeking injunctive relief and damages for public nuisance. Appellant claimed that respondent's activities along its right-of-way and side tracks annoyed adjacent citizens and damaged their properties. Respondent moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted the motion, finding the action precluded by principles of federal preemption. On appeal, the trial court's judgment was affirmed as modified. The court on appeal held that the trial court was correct in finding that federal preemption barred litigating the claim in state court. The Interstate Commerce Commission Termination Act of 1995, 49 U.S.C.S. §§ 10501(a, b), expressly granted exclusive regulatory control over railroad transportation matters to the Surface Transportation Board. However, it was within the purview of the federal authorities to allow state intervention, and thus if appellant could persuade the federal authorities to permit that, it could refile its claim without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting summary judgment to respondent was affirmed with modifications. Although appellant could not maintain its nuisance suit because federal authorities had exclusive jurisdiction over railroad matters, appellant's lawsuit would be reinstated if the federal authorities granted him permission to sue in state court.

State v. Cardell


A-2711-97T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


318 N.J. Super. 175; 723 A.2d 111; 1999 N.J. Super. LEXIS 33


January 12, 1999, Argued  
February 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 10, 1999. As Corrected February 19, 1999. Second Correction February 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, which convicted defendant of fourth-degree stalking pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-10, and sentenced him to prison for 18 months, of which nine months were to be served without parole.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of fourth-degree stalking pursuant to the anti-stalking statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-10. The action stemmed from defendant's repeated phone calls to victim and incidents where he followed her to work and her home. Victim testified that the episodes were extremely distressing and placed her in fear of physical injury. Taking into account defendant's nine prior convictions, the trial court sentenced him to prison for 18 months. Defendant argued that the anti-stalking statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and that his motion for acquittal should have been granted because evidence was insufficient to support verdict. The appellate court affirmed the order, finding the statute was not unconstitutionally broad or vague where its reach was clearly limited and the prohibited conduct was clearly stated through mental-state requirements.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's stalking conviction and prison sentence because the anti-stalking statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad where it did not restrict protected conduct and was not vague where prohibited conduct was clearly stated. The evidence was sufficient to support verdict.

Sacks Realty Co., Inc. v. Shore


A-6681-96T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


317 N.J. Super. 258; 721 A.2d 1011; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 520


December 1, 1998, Argued  
December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 31, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realty company sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Hudson County (New Jersey), denying its action for enforcement of consent agreements for possession and warrants of removal against defendants, non-purchasing tenants, after condominium conversion based on retroactive application of the Tenant Protection Act of 1992, N.J. Stat. Ann, §§ 2A:18-61.40-:18-61.59.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff realty company brought an action against defendants, non-purchasing tenants, seeking issuance of warrants for removal and damages after a condominium conversion. On remand, the trial court denied plaintiff's applications for warrants of removal based on the anti-removal provisions of the Tenant Protection Act of 1992, N.J. Stat. Ann, §§ 2A:18-61.40-:18-61.59, but awarded plaintiff damages for losses sustained by defendants' failure to vacate. Plaintiff sought review and defendants cross-appealed. The court affirmed the denial of the warrants for removal, finding that defendants' waivers of statutory protections without consideration was impermissible as a matter of public policy, rendering the parties' eviction agreement and consent judgments void. Further, under the express retroactive provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.56, defendants were not eligible for removal. The court reversed the award of damages because the void agreement and consent judgments did not give plaintiff any vested rights for damages and because the Act, by affording defendants the right to remain in possession of their apartments, precluded the award of damages for failure to vacate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of plaintiff realty company's request for issuance of warrants of removal, finding that the waiver of statutory protections by defendants, non-purchasing tenants, rendered eviction agreement void as a matter of public policy. The court reversed the award of damages to plaintiff for defendants' failure to vacate because defendants had right to remain in possession.

Oros v. Township of Bridgewater


A-2352-97T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


317 N.J. Super. 1; 721 A.2d 8; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 470


November 5, 1998, Argued  
November 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a trial-level order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed, upon motion, plaintiff's complaint to challenge a sewer construction assessment imposed by defendant township because plaintiffs failed to provide notice to defendant's tax collector and clerk within 30 days of the adoption of the sewer assessment, as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:56-54.


OVERVIEW: As an initial matter, the court noted that it was undisputed that the clerk and tax collector both had been served with a copy of the complaint more than 30 days after the resolution had been adopted. The court then rejected plaintiff property owners' contention that N.J. Ct. R. 4:69, which governed prerogative writs, rather than N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:56-54, controlled plaintiffs' challenge to the validity of defendant township's sewer assessment. The court found that contrary to plaintiffs' assertion, the statute setting forth the procedures for appealing assessments was dispositive, despite the state supreme court's constitutional power to adopt rules governing practice and procedure, because no question of fundamental constitutional rights had been raised by the complaint. The court held that the allegations of plaintiffs' complaint, which merely related that by reason of the inclusion of their property, the assessments were undue or excessive, were the proper subject of inquiry under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:56-54. The court affirmed, concluding that dismissal was appropriate where plaintiffs failed to institute their proceedings within the time limited by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff property owners' complaint against defendant township concerning the validity of defendant's sewer construction assessment because plaintiffs had failed to make appropriate service of the complaint within the time period specified by the statute governing appeals of such assessments.

In re D'Aconti


A-888-96T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


316 N.J. Super. 1; 719 A.2d 652; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 416


October 7, 1998, Argued  
October 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final decision of the State Board of Medical Examiners, Department of Law and Public Safety.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a final decision of the State Board of Medical Examiners Department of Law and Public Safety (New Jersey) denying him leave to file a petition for modification of a consent order disciplining petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner appealed the board of medical examiners' decision denying him leave to file a petition for modification of a consent order entered into between petitioner and the board, disciplining him for failing to keep adequate patient medical records. Petitioner asserted that public disclosure of the order caused managed health care organizations to refuse petitioner panel status, thereby interfering with his right to pursue his livelihood. Petitioner asked the court to order the board to modify or expunge the order. Expungement was a legislatively authorized remedy, expressly limited to certain prescribed criminal, quasi-criminal, juvenile and other enumerated offenses. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:52-2 to -6. In interpreting the breadth of the expungement remedy, the court concluded that the statute expressly applied only to criminal charges. The disposition of the board was affirmed because expungement power did not extend to licensing agencies. Because the expungement power did not extend to licensing agencies, the relief sought by petitioner was beyond the power of the board to grant.


OUTCOME: The decision of the state board of medical examiners denying petitioner's leave to file a petition for modification of a consent order disciplining petitioner was affirmed because the board did not have the power to expunge the consent order as requested by petitioner.
