State v. Lazarchick


A-3082-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


314 N.J. Super. 500; 715 A.2d 365; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 387


March 25, 1998, Argued  
September 3, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant policeman appealed judgment of the Superior Court, Union County (New Jersey), which convicted him de novo of assault and harassment, and refused to review the trial court's order requiring forfeiture of defendant's employment under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:51-2a. Defendant argued that the trial judge erred procedurally and the lower court erred in refusing review of application of the forfeiture statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant policeman was convicted of assault and harassment on a juvenile while on duty, and he appealed to the lower court, which convicted him again on de novo review and refused review of the trial court's order that defendant forfeit his employment under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:51-2a. Defendant appealed the lower court's judgment and argued that the trial court erred in admitting hearsay testimony and in consolidating his prosecution of complainant with complainant's prosecution of him and that the lower court erred in refusing review of the forfeiture order. The court affirmed and ruled that the testimony recounting complainant's report of defendant's assault was admissible as an excited utterance, that defendant consented to the consolidation, and that the consolidated trial was not fundamentally unfair. The court also ruled that forfeiture of office was a mandatory requirement separate from the sentence, designed to effect an important public purpose apart from punishment for an offense, and that, under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:51-2e, the court became involved in determining whether waiver was appropriate only after the attorney general or the county prosecutor requested it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment convicting defendant policeman of assault and sustaining the trial court's order that defendant forfeit his employment. The court ruled that the trial court's evidentiary rulings were proper, that the trial was not fundamentally unfair, and that forfeiture of employment was mandatory and not subject to judicial discretion in the absence of a prosecutorial request for waiver.

 

832 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sharpless


A-5869-95T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


314 N.J. Super. 440; 715 A.2d 333; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 355


December 15, 1997, Submitted  
August 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, that convicted him of possession of heroin and tampering with evidence. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his suppression motion based upon an illegal search and erred in denying his motion to dismiss the charges of evidence tampering.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for and convicted of possession of heroin and tampering with evidence. He appealed the judgment of conviction, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his suppression motion where the search was unlawful and erred in failing to dismiss the charges of evidence tampering. In affirming defendant's conviction of drug possession, the court concluded that the search was unlawful where the police had an objectively reasonable basis to travel to the location where an unknown informant indicated that they would find an armed person and to stop and frisk defendant when his appearance matched the description provided by the informant. Defendant's failure to promptly respond to officer's command to take his hand out of his pocket provided a reasonable basis for the police officers to direct him to get down on the ground so that they could conduct a search for weapons without undue danger to themselves. In reversing defendant's conviction of tampering with evidence, however, the court concluded that the act of discarding contraband upon the approach of police did not constitute evidence tampering.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of drug possession was affirmed, for information that a person matching defendant's description was armed provided justification for the police to stop and frisk defendant to search for a weapon. The judgment convicting defendant of evidence tampering was reversed, however, as the act of discarding of drugs upon the approach of police officers did not constitute tampering with evidence.

 

833 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. Department of Human Services


A-466-97T1F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


314 N.J. Super. 11; 713 A.2d 1056; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 336


January 27, 1998, Argued  
July 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 8, 1998. As Corrected July 14, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Department of Human Services, Division of Family Development.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a decision of the Camden County Board of Social Services (New Jersey) that limited plaintiff's cash assistance benefits pursuant to the Work First New Jersey Program, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 44:10-46, based on a residency requirement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff received AFDC benefits in New Jersey until she moved to New York and later to Puerto Rico. Plaintiff then returned to New Jersey and reapplied for public assistance. Defendant, the Camden County Board of Social Services, awarded plaintiff limited cash assistance benefits pursuant to the Work First New Jersey Program, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 44:10-46. The statute created a two-tier welfare system, whereby a person seeking welfare benefits who had moved to New Jersey from a state that offered a lower level of cash assistance, received lower benefits than a person who had lived in the state for 12 consecutive months. The court vacated and remanded holding that § 44:10-46 violated both the federal and state constitutional guarantees of equal protection of the law. The conservation of taxpayer dollars was not a sufficient state interest to sustain the durational residency requirement.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded plaintiff's reduced public assistance award holding that the conservation of taxpayer dollars was not a sufficient state interest to sustain the durational residency requirement of the Work First statute, which violated constitutional guarantees of equal protection.

 

834 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Dunn v. State, Dept. of Human Services


A-3434-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


312 N.J. Super. 321; 711 A.2d 944; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 274


February 10, 1998, Argued  
June 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property seller appealed from a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which denied him damages incurred during the 21 month period between conclusion of the trial and the court's rendering of the decision. Both defendant property sellers challenged the denial of counsel fees given that defendant programs company received counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: Defendant programs company contracted to purchase property from defendant property sellers which they planned to convert into group home for emotionally disturbed teenagers. After initially approving the plan, plaintiff city and intervenor neighbors and parents sought to terminate the project. Defendant property seller and programs company countered alleging violations of the Fair Housing Amendments Act (FHAA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 3601 et seq., and the Law Against Discrimination (LAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 to -42. The trial court found FHAA and LAD violations, awarded declaratory and injunctive relief and damages to defendant property seller. Defendant property seller appealed contending improper refusal to consider the damages he incurred during period between trial conclusion and the court's decision. Both defendant property sellers challenged the denial of counsel fees which defendant program company was awarded. The court concluded that defendant property seller was entitled to damages he sustained not only to the time of trial but also to the time of the court's decision. The court remanded for consideration of proofs and to fix damages accruing subsequent to the trial date.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to defendant property seller not receiving counsel fees. On remand, the trial court was to hold a hearing to determine damages from the time of trial to the time of decision, and counsel fees. The court also concluded defendant property seller was entitled to the damages sustained to the time of the court's decision because the trial judge's delay in rendering a decision did not toll the damage claim.

 

835 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Cherrits v. Ridgewood


A-5078-96T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


311 N.J. Super. 517; 710 A.2d 586; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 264


April 7, 1998, Argued  
May 29, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff demonstrator appealed an entry of summary judgment by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, in favor of defendant municipality in plaintiff's action brought pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1985(3).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff demonstrator brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1985(3) against defendant municipality based on his arrest at a Republican political rally. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of defendant. On appeal, the court affirmed. Plaintiff offered no proof to support allegations that defendant had a municipal policy to suppress the beliefs of Democrats. His allegations that the police chief created policy on how to handle criminal complaints also failed. The power to effect arrests resided in the county prosecutor and neither the police chief nor defendant had the final policymaking authority with respect to such procedures. Whether the police chief willfully or negligently misapplied county policy was an issue that related to his individual liability, not defendant's. Plaintiff's failure to train theory likewise failed, because plaintiff failed to point to one incident in which Democrats were the targets of official misconduct. There was no need to analyze the particulars of plaintiff's § 1985(3) claim, because plaintiff's failure to demonstrate a municipal policy in the first instance barred his recovery under both § 1983 and § 1985(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendant municipality in plaintiff demonstrator's civil rights actions. Defendant did not have final policymaking authority as to effecting arrests, and thus plaintiff could not show that defendant's policy was the moving force of any constitutional violation. Plaintiff could not prove failure to train because he could not point to any incidents of official misconduct against Democrats.

 

836 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Branin Transport, Inc.


A-2635-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


312 N.J. Super. 38; 711 A.2d 331; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 234


May 13, 1998, Argued  
May 22, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 22, 1998.
As Corrected June 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Judgment of the Division of Workers' Compensation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the judgment of the Division of Workers' Compensation (New Jersey), which applied amended N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13 retroactively to award appellee widow dependency benefits for husband's death while employed by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee widow's husband was killed in the course of his employment with appellant employer, and she was awarded widow-dependency benefits, as provided in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13, that ceased when her earnings exceeded the benefits. After N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13 was amended, appellant filed a notice of motion against appellee for dependency benefits payment, noting the elimination of the earned income credit. The hearing judge held that appellee was entitled to receive dependency benefits and appellant sought review. The court affirmed, because appellant had a vested right to the dependency benefits, and applying the amendment to existing claims constituted, at most, secondary retroactivity, because it only applied to the future receipt of benefits as a result of the elimination of the credit. The court concluded that appellee had only a contingent right to the credit that did not vest until appellee's income was actually obtained from employment on each occasion when the statute was in effect, therefore no constitutional infirmity existed in the secondarily retroactive application of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the workers' compensation division that applied amended N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13 retroactively to award appellee widow dependency benefits for husband's death while employed by appellant employer was affirmed, as appellee had vested right in the benefits and secondarily retroactive application of the amendment to provide future receipt of benefits as a result of the elimination of the credit was constitutional.

 

837 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Morris School Dist. Bd. of Educ.


A-6013-96T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


310 N.J. Super. 332; 708 A.2d 762; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 179; 158 L.R.R.M. 2116


March 25, 1998, Argued  
April 22, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Public Employment Relations Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review from a scope of negotiation determination by the Public Employment Relations Commission (New Jersey), which decided that a proposed cap on payments for unused paid sick leave was an illegal inducement to early retirement and, thus, non-negotiable, and that respondent union did not knowingly bargain away accrued sick leave compensation by consenting in advance to be bound by the recommendations of a factfinder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school board and respondent union were at an impasse in contract negotiations and were referred to a factfinder to make a recommendation. Respondent agreed to be bound to the decision. The factfinder proposed a retroactive cap on accumulated unused sick leave payable on retirement to employees. The issue of accumulated sick leave payments was not at issue in negotiations. The Public Employment Relations Commission (commission) decided that a proposed cap was an illegal inducement to early retirement and was non-negotiable. The commission further determined that respondent did not knowingly bargain away accrued sick leave compensation by consenting in advance to be bound by the recommendations of a factfinder. The court affirmed the decision of the commission because appellant and respondent could not divest employees of accumulated sick leave compensation without a knowing and intentional waiver by the employees affected. The court also held that respondent did not bargain away the sick leave by consenting to the factfinder's decision in advance where the retroactive cap was first conceived by the factfinder and had never been proposed by either of the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision prohibiting a cap on the payment of accrued sick leave of employees upon retirement because appellant school board and respondent union could not adopt a policy that divested employees of accumulated sick leave compensation absent a knowing and intentional waiver by the persons adversely affected.

 

838 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


A-5359-95T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


310 N.J. Super. 92; 707 A.2d 1387; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 166


March 10, 1998, Argued  
April 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, which convicted defendant pursuant to the former version of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(b)(2) of second-degree possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and related drug charges. The trial court imposed an extended term of 20 years with a 10-year period of parole ineligibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested following a surveillance operation where he was suspected of possessing cocaine for distribution. Defendant was convicted of second-degree possession with the intent to distribute one-half ounce or more of cocaine, pursuant to the prior version of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(b)(2) and other drug-related crimes. The trial court imposed an extended term of 20 years with a 10-year period of parole ineligibility. The appellate court affirmed the conviction but remanded for resentencing. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(b)(2) was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute clearly stated that the weight included adulterants and dilutants, not just the weight of the cocaine itself. The trial court did not state its reasons for resentencing defendant to 20 years when the presumptive sentence for a third-degree extended sentence was 15 years under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-1(f)(1)(b) nor did it state its reasons for the parole ineligibility. Because of the trial court's inadequate explanation for its sentences, the cause was remanded.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for second-degree possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and related drug charges was affirmed. The cocaine possession statute was not unconstitutionally vague. However, the cause was remanded for resentencing because the trial did not adequately explain its reasoning for sentencing defendant to 20 years of imprisonment with ten years of parole ineligibility.

City of Newark v. Essex County Bd. of Taxation


A-5713-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


309 N.J. Super. 476; 707 A.2d 493; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 153


November 12, 1997, Argued; January 21, 1998, Reargued  
April 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, awarding summary judgment to defendant, a board of taxation, in plaintiff's action seeking to compel defendant to calculate the tax bills for properties whose abatements had expired.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city filed an action against defendant, a board of taxation, seeking to compel defendant to calculate the tax bills for 77 properties whose abatements had expired in accordance with N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.140, and to have defendant treat those properties as other than taxable in calculating school, county, and municipal taxes. Defendant filed a cross-motion for summary judgment, arguing that plaintiff's interpretation of § 54:4-3.140 violated the New Jersey Constitution by extending abatements beyond five years. The trial court awarded summary judgment to defendant. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding that plaintiff's interpretation of § 54:4-3.140 was not unconstitutional. The transitional scheme to assure that the abatement program was a success and to move in the direction of uniformity by encouraging revaluation was within the power of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The order awarding summary judgment to defendant, a board of taxation, in plaintiff city's action to compel defendant to calculate the tax bills for properties whose abatements had expired was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that the trial court erred in finding that plaintiff's interpretation of an abatement statute was unconstitutional.

Bryant v. City of Atlantic City


A-3438-96T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


309 N.J. Super. 596; 707 A.2d 1072; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 155


March 25, 1998, Argued  
April 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 10, 1998.
As Corrected April 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a group of residents, taxpayers, and interested associations, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, awarding summary judgment to defendants, a city, a mayor, a city council, and a resort corporation, in an action challenging a redevelopment agreement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a group of residents, taxpayers, and interested associations, filed an action against defendants, a city, a mayor, a city council, and a resort corporation, alleging that improper actions were taken in connection with a redevelopment area. Defendants moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not err in failing to conclude that defendant city unconstitutionally donated public land to defendant resort corporation. The court further found that certain contingencies in the redevelopment agreement did not make it illusory. Finally, the court found no merit to plaintiffs' contentions that the trial judge inappropriately applied the relevant standard in granting summary judgment to defendants. However, the court did modify the redevelopment agreement, finding that one of its sections violated a statute. In all other respects, the trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order awarding summary judgment to defendants, a city, a mayor, a city council, and a resort corporation, was affirmed as modified because plaintiffs, a group of residents, taxpayers, and interested associations, failed to demonstrate that the trial judge inappropriately applied the relevant standard in awarding summary judgment to defendants.

State v. Purnell


A-3137-95T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


310 N.J. Super. 407; 708 A.2d 1196; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 118


January 27, 1998, Argued  
March 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 20, 1998. As Revised April 8, 1998.
Certification denied by State v. Purnell, 156 N.J. 385, 718 A.2d 1214, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 651 (1998)
Certification granted by State v. Purnell, 156 N.J. 385, 718 A.2d 1214, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 1004 (1998)
Reversed by State v. Purnell, 161 N.J. 44, 735 A.2d 513, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 832 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.
State v. Purnell, 126 N.J. 518, 601 A.2d 175, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 13 (1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, convicting him of murder, hindering apprehension, possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose, and perjury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, hindering apprehension, possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose, and perjury. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, hindering apprehension, and possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose. However, the court reversed defendant's perjury conviction and remanded for a new trial on that charge. The court found that the conviction for perjury was obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional rights to have the jury find each element of the crime, in that the trial court, not the jury, determined that the allegedly perjured statement was material. The evidence with respect to the materiality element of the perjury charge was open to question.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of murder, hindering apprehension, and possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose was affirmed. However, the order convicting defendant of perjury was reversed and remanded for a new trial on the charge. The court found that the conviction for perjury was obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional right to have the jury find each element of the crime.

 

842 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lutz


A-5933-96T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


309 N.J. Super. 317; 707 A.2d 159; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 114


February 3, 1998, Argued  
March 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court, Ocean County (New Jersey), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol and careless driving. Defendant contended that the serum alcohol test used against him was unreliable and inadmissible. Further, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction for careless driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a collision with oncoming traffic and taken to a hospital. A police officer noticed alcohol on defendant's breath and asked him to take a blood alcohol test. Defendant agreed and the test indicated a serum alcohol level of 149 milligrams, the equivalent of a blood alcohol level of .128 percent. Based on the results of the test, defendant was found guilty of driving under the influence of alcohol and careless driving. On appeal, the law division tried the case de novo, again finding defendant guilty. Defendant sought additional review, contending that the results of the blood serum test were unreliable and inadmissible. However, the court found no basis for ruling that the serum test was inadmissible, given the ample evidence of the test's reliability. However, the court agreed that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of careless driving. The court held that due to the quasi-criminal nature of the proceedings, the state was required to prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Absent any specific evidence that defendant was actually careless, the court held that he could not be convicted of careless driving.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol was affirmed because the reliability of the results of a serum alcohol test were not sufficiently in doubt as to render them inadmissible. But, absent specific evidence of defendant's carelessness, the state could not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was guilty of careless driving; thus, that conviction was reversed.

 

843 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Dale v. Boy Scouts of America


A-2427-95T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


308 N.J. Super. 516; 706 A.2d 270; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 79


December 8, 1997, Argued  
March 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 2, 1998.
Certification granted Dale v. BSA, 156 N.J. 382, 718 A.2d 1210, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 914 (1998)
Certification granted Dale v. BSA, 156 N.J. 381, 718 A.2d 1210, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 915 (1998)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Dale v. BSA, 160 N.J. 562, 734 A.2d 1196, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 995 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff scoutmaster sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, that granted summary judgment to defendants, Boy Scouts of America and the local boy scout council, after plaintiff was expelled from his position as an assistant scoutmaster after publicly declaring he was a homosexual.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff scoutmaster was expelled from his position with defendant local boy scout council after publicly declaring his homosexual status. He was expelled from defendant Boy Scouts of America (BSA) because of its policy excluding avowed homosexuals from membership in its organization. Plaintiff filed a complaint in the superior court, alleging his expulsion violated the New Jersey laws against discrimination (LAD) as well as certain common law rights. Summary judgment was granted to defendants wherein the superior court stated plaintiff had no cause of action under the LAD because defendant BSA was not a place of public accommodation, was a distinctly private organization, and was, thus, excluded from the LAD. Upon review, the court held that the LAD rendered unlawful certain discriminations, and its goal was nothing less than the eradication of the cancer of discrimination. Further, defendant BSA, and its local councils were places of public accommodation dependent upon the broad-based participation of members of the general public and as such were not entitled to LAD exclusion. The judgment of the superior court was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's grant of summary judgment to defendants, Boy Scouts of America and the local council, because defendants were places of public accommodation and as such were not entitled to exclusions under the New Jersey Laws Against Discrimination. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Tamburelli Properties Ass'n v. Borough of Cresskill


A-1806-96T5, A-7342-95T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


308 N.J. Super. 326; 705 A.2d 1270; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 72


February 3, 1998, Argued  
February 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality sought review of an order from the Tax Court (New Jersey), which reduced the property tax assessment on a tract of land owned by respondent property owners.


OVERVIEW: After a trial, the tax court reduced the property tax assessment on certain land owned by respondent property owners. Appellant municipality sought review, contending that the underlying assessments were improperly calculated, and that the Freeze Act judgment was entered prematurely. Affirming the tax court's judgment, the court held that the discounted cash flow analysis using an absorption discount as one factor in the calculation of value was appropriate. The court further held that appellant's attempt to appeal this method of valuation after embracing it at trial violated the doctrine of judicial estoppel. The court concluded that there was no reason to believe that the legislature intended the Freeze Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:51A-8, to apply to a tax court determination that remained on appeal, but not to a county board of taxation determination that was on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's judgment reducing the property tax assessment on respondent property owner's land because calculating the property value based on use of the entire tract as a residential subdivision with value computed pursuant to a discounted cash flow analysis was appropriate.

 

845 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


A-6540-93T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


308 N.J. Super. 174; 705 A.2d 805; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 45


January 6, 1998, Submitted  
February 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 11, 1998. As Corrected March 11, 1998.
Certification denied by State v. Jones, 156 N.J. 380, 718 A.2d 1209, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 946 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Jones, 2013 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2974 (App.Div., Dec. 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey), which convicted him of murder and felony murder, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3a, first- and second-degree kidnapping, § 2C:13-1b(1)(2), conspiracy to commit robbery, § 2C:5-2, first-degree robbery, § 2C:15-1, possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose and unlawful possession of a weapon, § 2C:39, and first-degree aggravated sexual assault, § 2C:14-2a(3).


OVERVIEW: In a death penalty case, defendant and an accomplice kidnapped a young mother and her 4-year-old son, then raped and murdered the mother. Defendant was convicted of murder and felony murder, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3a, first- and second-degree kidnapping, § 2C:13-1b(1)(2), conspiracy to commit robbery, § 2C:5-2, first-degree robbery, § 2C:15-1, possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose and unlawful possession of a weapon, § 2C:39, and first-degree aggravated sexual assault, § 2C:14-2a(3). The court affirmed, holding that under § 2C:14-2a(3), proof of one or more of the predicate crimes was all that was necessary to establish the absence of "affirmative and freely given permission." The court also held that § 2C:14-2a required proof that a rape-murder victim be alive at the time the assaultive behavior began but not at the time of penetration. The court further held that in a capital murder case, felony murder must be submitted to the jury if rationally supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions because proof of the homicide established the sexual assault charge, the death of defendant's rape-murder victim prior to penetration did not necessarily preclude a rape conviction, and felony murder was required to be charged where it was rationally based on the evidence and was the basis for an alternative form of murder that was noncapital.

 

846 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rogers


A-2819-96T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


308 N.J. Super. 59; 705 A.2d 397; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 39


January 5, 1998, Submitted  
February 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant was convicted of unauthorized practice of law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:21-22b(2), by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County. Appellant asserted that this statute was unconstitutional by way of being void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant defendant was convicted of unauthorized practice of law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:21-22b(2), upon accepting money to help prepare an answer for a complaint. Appellant asserted that this statute was void for vagueness and therefore unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, noting that the rule was that if a law was so vague that persons of common intelligence must guess at its meaning, it would be considered void for vagueness. The court noted that the Supreme Court of New Jersey had defined the term "practice of law" and it therefore could not be considered facially vague, and also found that the statute clearly proscribed certain conduct and therefore was not vague as applied. The court found that the drafting of pleadings and other legal documents did constitute the practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, noting that the rule was that if a law was so vague that persons of common intelligence must guess at its meaning, it would be considered void for vagueness. The court found the statute prohibiting unauthorized "practice of law" was not facially vague or vague as applied, because this term was defined by the Supreme Court of New Jersey in some contexts and clearly proscribed certain conduct.

State in Interest of M.G.


A-4336-95T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


307 N.J. Super. 348; 704 A.2d 1025; 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 19


December 10, 1997, Argued  
January 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which adjudicated him delinquent for possessing an imitation controlled dangerous substance as criminalized by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-11. The trial court imposed five years of probation, monetary assessments, and a six-month driver's license suspension.


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer arranged to purchase LSD from a juvenile. After negotiating the sale, three juveniles were arrested, including appellant. After the arrest, a search of the car in which the juveniles were riding yielded two plastic-wrapped sheets of blotter paper, each perforated into 100 sections with each section imprinted with black and white smiley faces. It is undisputed that the sheets were styled and packaged in a traditional manner used to transfer LSD. Initially, the juveniles were charged with possession with intent to distribute and distribution. After the blotter paper sections tested negative for LSD, the state amended its complaint and charged appellant with possession of an imitation controlled substance as criminalized by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-11. The trial court concluded that the sheets of blotter paper fell within the intendment of the statute, and adjudicated appellant delinquent. In affirming the lower court, the court concluded that the statutory plain language criminalized the possession of a substance that was designed to replicate LSD.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order adjudicating appellant delinquent. The court ruled that the visual nature of the packaged sheets engendered circumstances designed to lead a reasonable person to believe that the sheets contained LSD. Those circumstances, compounded with the uniqueness of the drug, satisfied the court that appellant possessed an imitation substance criminalized by statute.

Township of Saddle Brook v. A.B. Family Center, Inc.

January 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 2, 1998.
Certification granted Township of Saddle Brook v. A.B. Family Ctr., 153 N.J. 217, 708 A.2d 67, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 286 (1998)
Certification denied by Township of Saddle Brook v. A.B. Family Ctr., 153 N.J. 217, 708 A.2d 68, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 285 (1998)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Township of Saddle Brook v. A.B. Family Ctr., 156 N.J. 587, 722 A.2d 530, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 14 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which rendered judgment in favor of respondents, corporation and developers, in appellant's action to enjoin respondent from selling adult oriented materials within the township.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, corporation and developer, attempted to open up a store selling adult materials after being denied a certificate of occupancy by appellant township. Appellant brought an action against respondent seeking injunctive relief. The court reversed and found that the trial court erred in declaring N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:34-7, which required a 1,000 foot buffer zone between sexually oriented businesses and churches, schools and similar places, an unconstitutional violation of respondents' right to free speech pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. I. The court noted that although there was no place within appellant's borders that would satisfy § 2C:34-7, there may have been ample alternative channels for communication in nearby communities. Because § 2C:34-7 was a state statute, there was no need to limit the inquiry to the appellant's borders. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence for the trial court to find that appellant endeavored to selectively enforce its zoning laws to prevent respondents from opening their store.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in favor of respondents, corporation and developers, in appellant township's action to enjoin respondent's from operating an adult oriented business and remanded for further proceedings because the inquiry into the constitutionality of the state law requiring a buffer zone around adult oriented businesses should have included alternative channels for communication in nearby communities.

Triano v. Division of State Lottery


A-4150-96T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


306 N.J. Super. 114; 703 A.2d 333; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 487


December 3, 1997, Argued  
December 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, which granted summary judgment for defendants, state agency and officials, on the ground that did not exhaust administrative remedies as they failed to seek a final determination from the executive director under the State Lottery Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:9-12, in there action for breach of agreement on lottery tickets.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimants, alleged winners in the bonus section of state lottery tickets, brought an action against defendants, state agency and officials, for breach of agreement and a claim against defendant state officials for negligent misrepresentation. Plaintiffs alleged that they were induced to purchase lottery tickets by an advertising brochure and that defendants failed to pay plaintiffs the amount indicated on the tickets. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment on the ground that plaintiffs failed to exhaust all administrative remedies prior to bring the action. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that plaintiffs did not exhaust administrative remedies prior to instituting the present action by filing a complaint with the executive director under the State Lottery Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:9-12. The court stated final decisions regarding the award of prizes rested with the executive director and plaintiffs were required to obtain a final determination by the director before they could appeal to the court under N.J. R. Civ. P. 2:2-3(a)(2). The court found the interests of justice did not require bypassing the administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants, state agency and officials, in plaintiff claimants' action for breach of agreement. Plaintiffs did not exhaust all administrative remedies available where they failed to file a complaint with the executive director prior to bringing their action because under the applicable statute, the executive director had the final determination regarding the award of prizes.

Mishlen v. Mishlen


A-2825-96T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


305 N.J. Super. 643; 702 A.2d 1384; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 473


November 5, 1997, Submitted  
December 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former wife sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which entered a dual judgment of divorce. Appellant complained that trial court erred by requiring that she not expose her children to her present boyfriend which restricted her freedom to remarry; by the amount and duration of rehabilitative alimony; and by failure to provide for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former wife sought review of portions of the dual judgment of divorce that was entered by the trial court following a six-day trial. Respondent husband was ordered to pay child support and rehabilitative alimony. Appellant was required to prevent the exposure of the children to her present boyfriend. Appellant complained that the restrictions regarding exposure of the children unnecessarily impinged on her right to marry. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the best interests of the children could be made paramount to other fundamental rights. The court stated that there were few rights more fundamental in society than those of parents to retain custody over and care for their children, and to rear their children, as they deemed appropriate. The court held that the trial judge's award of rehabilitative alimony was appropriate in the case involving a relatively short marriage and a young divorcee. The court also noted that if appellant's attainment of economic self-sufficiency did not occur despite her good faith efforts, appellant could have applied for an extension.


OUTCOME: The dual degree of divorce issued by the trial court, which placed restrictions of appellant former wife regarding exposing the children of the marriage to her present boyfriend, was affirmed. The court held that best interests of the children could be made more paramount to other fundamental rights.

Matter of A. Fiore & Sons, Inc.


A-3079-95T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


305 N.J. Super. 192; 701 A.2d 1303; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 435


October 7, 1997, Argued  
November 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 5, 1997.
Certification denied by In re Allegations of Violations of Law & Admin. Code by A. Fiore & Sons, 153 N.J. 51, 707 A.2d 155, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 192 (1998)
Certification granted In re Allegations of Violations of Law & Admin. Code by A. Fiore & Cons, Inc. (Department of Envtl. Protection), 1998 N.J. LEXIS 1401 (N.J., Aug. 11, 1998)
Affirmed by In re Allegations of Violations of Law & Admin. Code by A. Fiore & Sons, Inc., 158 N.J. 105, 726 A.2d 1289, 1999 N.J. LEXIS 537 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a decision of the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, waste disposal business and owners, challenged a decision of the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection (New Jersey), finding that appellants failed to comply with state and local regulations regarding solid waste disposal, assessing a monetary penalty, revoking appellants' certificate, and permanently debarring appellant owners from participating in the solid waste disposal industry in New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, waste disposal business and owners, faced with conflicting state and local regulations, chose to utilize out-of-state solid waste disposal facilities, contravening state regulations. The Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection assessed a monetary penalty, revoked appellants' certificate, and permanently debarred appellant owners from participating in the solid waste disposal industry in New Jersey. Shortly thereafter, the federal courts determined that the state's system of flow control of waste violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I § 8, cl. 3. The court concluded that the newly-announced federal case law's interpretation of federal constitutional rules was to be applied retroactively. Accordingly, the court held that, unless the federal decision was reversed or severely modified, the orders prohibiting out-of-state shipment of solid waste were constitutionally defective and the penalties imposed for violating those orders were to be rescinded. The court remanded the matter with instructions to radically reassess the penalties imposed and advised that appellants' mitigating factors be taken into account with respect to local violations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order finding that appellants, waste disposal business and owners, failed to comply with state and local regulations regarding solid waste disposal because the recent federal decision holding that the state's waste laws violated the Commerce Clause was to be applied retroactively. The court remanded for reconsideration.

State v. Younger


A-635-95T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


305 N.J. Super. 250; 702 A.2d 477; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 408


October 7, 1997, Submitted  
October 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, for possession of heroin and possession of that heroin within 1,000 feet of a school, alleging that the lower court erred in denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a warrantless search.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of heroin and possession of that heroin within 1,000 feet of a school. He sought review of the conviction, claiming that the lower court erroneously denied appellant's motion to suppress drug evidence that a police officer found in a change purse while he was conducting a warrantless search for a handgun in appellant's room. On appeal, the court reversed appellant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the officer exceeded the scope of the consent of appellant's grandmother when he searched a change purse because the grandmother's consent was limited to a search for a handgun and the officer admitted that the change purse was too small to contain a handgun. The court also held that appellant's grandmother did not have authority to consent to the search of closed containers within the room in which appellant was staying because the authority of the grandmother as owner of the premises did not extend to possessions of appellant, as occupier, that were not in plain view.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for possession of heroin and possession of that heroin within 1,000 feet of a school was reversed and remanded for a new trial on the grounds that a police officer conducted a warrantless search of appellant's room and exceeded the scope of consent to search for a handgun, when he searched a small change purse that belonged to appellant.

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Gloucester County.

Admin. Code tit. 33, § 3.8 (a)-(b), rejecting plaintiffs' interpretation of Tenants' Property Tax Rebate Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-6.2 -13, but upholding its constitutionality.

The provisions did not require different property assessment or taxation than for property that fell outside the Act. The trial court correctly rejected plaintiffs', landlord association and apartment owners, equal protection challenge to the Act.

State v. Apprendi


A-1587-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


304 N.J. Super. 147; 698 A.2d 1265; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 365


February 4, 1997, Argued  
August 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cumberland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his extended term sentence from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Cumberland County, that was imposed pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-3(e) (the Hate Crime Statute). The defendant asserted that the statute was unconstitutional for vagueness and for violating due process by using a preponderance of the evidence standard. The defendant pled guilty to violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-4(a) and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-3(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's extended term sentence imposed pursuant to N .J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-3(e) (the Hate Crime Statute) was affirmed because as a sentencing factor it required as proof only preponderance of the evidence that the crime, proved beyond a reasonable doubt, was racially motivated. The court excised the words "at least in part, with ill will, hatred or bias toward" to cure the vagueness challenge as the legislature had done earlier. Defendant was arrested for twice firing a rifle into a neighbor's residence and at his door and windows. Statements made after his arrest raised the issue of whether his motivation was racial bias. He pled guilty to a firearm possession and an unlawful weapon possession and was sentenced to an extended term of 12 years on the firearm charge. The court found no constitutional impediment to a statutory requirement for an extended term upon the sentencing judge being satisfied by a preponderance of the evidence that the crime, either pled or proven beyond a reasonable doubt, was committed because of racial hatred.


OUTCOME: Defendant's extended term sentence imposed pursuant to the state's Hate Crime Statute was affirmed because as a sentencing factor it required as proof only preponderance of the evidence that the crime, proved beyond a reasonable doubt, was racially motivated. The court excised the words "at least in part, with ill will, hatred or bias toward" to cure the vagueness challenge.

State v. Gadsden


A-0504-94T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


303 N.J. Super. 491; 697 A.2d 187; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 354


November 14, 1996, Submitted  
August 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought relief from multiple convictions in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, on the grounds that evidence seized was taken from an illegal arrest and therefore should have been suppressed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought relief from a conviction of armed robbery, possession of a handgun for unlawful purposes, possession of a handgun without a permit, and possession of an imitation firearm for unlawful purposes. Defendant contended that all evidence seized during his arrest should have been suppressed because he was arrested by police outside of their jurisdiction in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A: 14-152 and that such actions by police constituted a violation of his state and federal constitutional rights against unreasonable searches and seizures. The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant and held that the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine applied only to evidence seized in violation of a suspect's constitutional rights. An arrest by police outside of their jurisdiction was not a violation of a law of constitutional dimension but was a procedural violation that did not affect defendant's constitutional rights regarding search and seizure. Moreover, police had probable cause to arrest defendant based on observation and did not infringe on defendant's state or federal constitutional rights against unreasonable search and seizure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant because although the police committed a statutory violation by arresting defendant outside of their jurisdiction, such a violation did not rise to the level of infringing on defendant's constitutional protections against illegal search and seizure.

Van Wingerden v. Lafayette Tp.


A-5208-95T3, A-5397-95T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


303 N.J. Super. 614; 697 A.2d 565; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 340


May 20, 1997, Submitted  
July 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, whose decision is reported at 15 N.J. Tax 475.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged the decision of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which upheld a tax assessment on plaintiff's greenhouse, in favor of defendant township.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged the decision by the tax court in favor of defendant township in issuing a tax assessment on plaintiff's greenhouse. The tax court found that plaintiff's greenhouse was real, not personal, property, that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-23.12 rendered the greenhouse exempt from real property taxation, and that the exemption statute violated the constitutional requirement that property be taxed under general laws authorized by N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 1, para. 1(a). Plaintiff and the attorney general filed a notice of appeal. On review, the court held that the statutory exemption did not violate the state constitution, but reversed and remanded the cause for reconsideration as to whether the greenhouse fell within the statutory exemption. The court held that plaintiff's greenhouse was readily dismantled, like personal property rather than real property, so that it did not violate the basic law of real property. The court also found defendant's argument compelling that the greenhouse was not exempt because a portion of the structure enclosed a space within its walls used as an office and remanded to consider whether plaintiff's greenhouse was statutorily exempt.


OUTCOME: Following plaintiff taxpayer's appeal of assessment on his greenhouse in favor of defendant township, the court held that the statutory exemption for greenhouses did not violate the state constitution, that plaintiff's greenhouse was personal and not real property because it was readily dismantled, and remanded the cause for reconsideration as to whether the greenhouse fell within the statutory exemption.

State v. Kane


A-4531-95T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


303 N.J. Super. 167; 696 A.2d 108; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 330


April 21, 1997, Argued  
July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, which affirmed his conviction for the offenses of disrupting a public meeting, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-8, and resisting arrest, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:29-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of disrupting a public meeting, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-8, and resisting arrest, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:29-2. The meeting was an official hearing before the committee on the budget of the United States House of Representatives. Defendant, unsuccessful at being recognized to speak before the meeting, attempted to attract the chairman's attention in a loud voice from the floor. Defendant was removed by police and struggled with them on the way. On appeal, the court reversed, and held that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant resisted arrest. Defendant's altercation with police took less than a 15 seconds. The court could not tell from the record, including video and audio tapes of the meeting, whether the police had announced to defendant their intention to arrest him. The court also held that defendant's brief shouts for recognition did not violate § 2C:33-8 because they did not substantially impair the assemblage, and that the police were not authorized to arrest him without direction from the congressman presiding over the meeting.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for disrupting a public meeting and resisting arrest. The state failed to prove that defendant resisted arrest because there was insufficient evidence from which to determine whether police had announced their intention to arrest defendant. Also, defendant's brief shouts for recognition did not violate the statute and police were not authorized to arrest him without direction from the meeting chair.

OVERVIEW: Appellant health maintenance organization, operated in New Jersey, and had applied for federal qualification as an health maintenance organization so that it could have offered a standard plan in compliance with federal law. Ann. § 17B:27A-12; N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11:20-2.1. State v. Saunders


A-0983-96T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


302 N.J. Super. 509; 695 A.2d 722; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 281


April 30, 1997, Submitted  
June 23, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which convicted him of third-degree stalking, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-10c, and sentenced him to a custodial term of five years.


OVERVIEW: After a prior court order precluded defendant from following the victim, he was convicted of third-degree stalking, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-10c, and sentenced to a custodial term of five years. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-10 was not unconstitutionally overbroad, because freedom of speech did not encompass a right to abuse or annoy the victim intentionally. Also, § 2C:12-10 was not impermissibly vague, because the specific intent required by § 2C:12-10 clearly indicated what type of conduct was prohibited. Also, he was repeatedly warned and finally ordered by the prior trial court to cease contact with the victim, and he must have known that his behavior would annoy the victim or put her in fear of injury. Further, the court concluded that his argument that his conviction was against the weight of the evidence was barred procedurally by N.J. Ct. R. 2:10-1, because he failed to move for a new trial below, and lacked substantive merit, because a trial court could only set aside a jury's verdict under N.J. Ct. R. 3:20-1 as against the weight of the evidence of a manifest denial of justice clearly and convincingly appeared.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of third-degree stalking, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad, because freedom of speech did not encompass a right to abuse or annoy the victim intentionally, and that the statute was not impermissibly vague, because the specific intent required in the stalking statute clearly indicated what type of conduct was prohibited.

Matter of Doe


A-4643-95T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


302 N.J. Super. 255; 695 A.2d 319; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 279


March 24, 1997, Argued  
June 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 20, 1997. Certiorari Denied April 27, 1998, Reported at: 523 U.S. 1096, 118 S. Ct. 1580, 140 L. Ed. 2d 795, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2855.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an individual and a corporation, challenged the orders of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, which required petitioner corporation to accord the state access to its documents, required both petitioners to answer investigative interrogatories issued pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:41-5a in an organized crime investigation, ordered fines for noncompliance with the prior order, and denied reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: In an organized crime investigation, the trial court required petitioner corporation to accord the state access to its documents, required petitioners, an individual and a corporation, to answer investigative interrogatories issued pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:41-5a regarding racketeering, ordered fines for noncompliance with the prior order, and denied reconsideration. On appeal, the court affirmed the issues addressed in the trial court's opinion on the basis of that opinion. The court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:41-5f provided the exclusive remedy for any disclosure by a state employee of petitioners' identities in connection with an organized crime investigation. The court held that a showing of probable cause was not required either by § 2C:41-5A, or the federal or state constitution for investigative interrogatories to be issued. The court held that by contending that the interrogatories should be set aside because petitioners were targets of a criminal investigation, petitioners conceded the existence of "an investigation," one of the § 2C:41-5a predicates for the issuance of the interrogatories which petitioners had argued was missing from the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders requiring petitioners, an individual and a corporation, to answer investigative interrogatories in an organized crime investigation, ordering fines for noncompliance with the order, and denying reconsideration. Probable cause was not required by statute or constitution for issuance of the investigatory interrogatories. Petitioners conceded the prerequisite investigation while arguing to set aside the interrogatories.

 

861 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. One 1990 Honda Accord, New Jersey Registration No. HRB-20D, VIN No. HGCB7659LA063293 and Four Hundred Twenty Dollars


A-6880-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


302 N.J. Super. 225; 695 A.2d 303; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 288


February 20, 1997, Submitted  
June 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 16, 1997.
As Corrected July 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which dismissed appellant's counterclaim against respondent state in respondent's forfeiture action and directed summary forfeiture of appellant's property. Appellant contended that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-3(f), which provided for non-jury determination of a forfeiture action, violated N.J. Const. art. I, para. 9 (1947).


OVERVIEW: Respondent state filed an in rem action seeking civil forfeiture of a vehicle owned by appellant claimant. Appellant filed a counterclaim asserting that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-3(f), which provided for non-jury determination of a forfeiture action, was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed appellant's counterclaim and ordered forfeiture of appellant's vehicle to the state. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. It held that an in rem forfeiture action under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-1 was subject to trial by jury pursuant to N.J. Const. art. I., para. 9 (1947). The court reasoned that such in rem forfeiture actions were causes of action triable by jury at common law and that the legislature could not deny the right to a jury trial in a cause of action triable by jury at common law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed appellant claimant's counterclaim and ordered appellant's vehicle forfeited to respondent state. It held that a state statute authorizing summary determination of in rem civil forfeiture actions violated the state constitution's guarantee of the right to jury trial in causes of action triable by jury at common law.

State v. Branch


A-4314-94T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


301 N.J. Super. 307; 693 A.2d 1272; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 255


May 14, 1997, Submitted  
June 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 5, 1997.
Certification granted by State v. Branch, 151 N.J. 470, 700 A.2d 881, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 1937 (1997)
Reversed by State v. Branch, 155 N.J. 317, 714 A.2d 918, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 626 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which found him guilty of murder, robbery, and numerous lesser crimes. The state filed a cross-appeal of the trial court's action in setting aside defendant's conviction for felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Police received information from a confidential informant about a person armed with a concealed weapon. Defendant who fit the description. When officers approached, defendant fled, and he was tackled and subdued. Police recovered a weapon implicated in a murder. Defendant was convicted of felony murder and lesser offenses. The trial court vacated the felony murder conviction. Defendant and the state appealed. The court affirmed the convictions and reinstated the felony murder conviction. Under the circumstances, the tackling of defendant was a reasonable use of force. Defendant was properly convicted of resisting arrest even though the police failed to utter the words that he was under arrest. The manslaughter instructions, while imperfect, were not erroneous when considered in their entirety. While the trial court failed to properly instruct the jury whether it could convict of felony murder when the predicate felony was bot charged, it was permissible to convict on the basis of the uncharged felony because the evidence supported the felony. The trial court erred in setting aside defendant's conviction for felony murder on the basis that the predicate felony had not been charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court insofar as it found defendant guilty of murder and other crimes and held that defendant failed to identify any prejudicial errors by the trial court. The court reversed the trial court's action in setting aside defendant's conviction for felony murder and held that the jury was able to convict of felony murder based upon an uncharged felony because there was evidence in the record to support it.

In re Certificate of Need Granted to the Harborage


A-681-95T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


300 N.J. Super. 363; 693 A.2d 133; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 208


March 25, 1997, Argued  
May 2, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 6, 1997. As Corrected May 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Deputy Commissioner of the Department of Health and Senior Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of the final administrative action of respondent Deputy Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health and Senior Services (department), awarding a certificate of need to respondent hospital for the establishment of a thirteen long-term ventilator care bed unit at its facility. Respondent department denied appellant's certificate of need application for a similar unit.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Deputy Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health and Senior Services (commissioner) awarded a certificate of need (CON) to respondent hospital for the establishment of a thirteen long-term ventilator care bed unit at its facility and denied appellant hospital's CON application. On appeal, the court affirmed respondent commissioner's final administrative action. Having established a need for ventilator beds under criteria set forth in N.J. Admin. Code tit. 8, § 33H-1.7(d), respondent commissioner properly applied the requirements of § 8 of the Health Care Facilities Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:2H-8. Respondent commissioner properly based her denial of appellant's CON application on appellant's failure to demonstrate adequate sources of present and future revenues. Moreover, appellant hospital had been cited for federal certification deficiencies, which mandated the denial of its CON application under N.J. Admin. Code tit. 8, § 33H-1.14(d). The court held that § 33H-1.14(d) was reasonably related to the legitimate legislative purpose of quality health care and was not arbitrary or discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant by respondent Deputy Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health and Senior Services of respondent hospital's certificate of need (CON) and denial of appellant hospital's CON. The denial was properly based on appellant's financial insecurity and federal certification deficiencies and the CON regulations were reasonably related to the legitimate legislative goal of quality health care.

Toys R Us, Inc. v. Director, New Jersey Div. of Taxation


A-817-95T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


300 N.J. Super. 163; 692 A.2d 111; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 199


December 17, 1996, Argued  
April 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retailer appealed the decision of the Tax Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant New Jersey Division of Taxation, which denied plaintiff's claim for a refund for a tax assessment paid by plaintiff that plaintiff subsequently discovered was no longer imposed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff retailer paid a tax assessment that arose as a result of an audit by defendant New Jersey Division of Taxation. Plaintiff later learned that defendant had changed its policy and no longer imposed sales and use taxes on labels. Plaintiff's claim for a refund was denied by defendant on the ground that the claim was filed too late. The Tax Court affirmed the denial by summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed. Plaintiff's claim was made approximately five months after the original assessment and more than three months after the revised assessment. The court held that if defendant had already made its change in policy, then the assessment was a mistake. The court agreed with defendant's construction of the various statutes of limitation, and in the absence of estoppel or other equitable considerations, plaintiff should have filed a claim for a refund within 30 days of the assessment or filed a complaint with the Tax Court within 90 days of the assessment. However, plaintiff should have had an opportunity to establish grounds for estoppel or equitable relief. Therefore, summary judgment was not proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to defendant New Jersey Division of Taxation on plaintiff retailer's claim for a refund of taxes that were erroneously imposed, because although plaintiff's claim was not filed within 30 days of the assessment, nor was a complaint filed with the Tax Court within 90 days of the assessment, plaintiff should have had an opportunity to establish grounds for estoppel or equitable relief.

Mourning v. Correctional Medical Services, (CMS) of St. Louis, Missouri


A-6574-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


300 N.J. Super. 213; 692 A.2d 529; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 193


March 26, 1997, Argued  
April 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoners sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which ruled in favor of respondent correctional medical services in appellants' action seeking injunctive relief and challenging the constitutionality of the prison inmate copayment statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 30:7E-1 to -6.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoners sought injunctive relief against respondent correctional medical services, challenging the constitutionality of the prison inmate copayment statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 30:7E-1 to -6, which imposed a $ 5 copayment on inmates for each inmate-initiated visit for medical, dental, emergency, and optometry services. The trial court concluded that appellants had not met the criteria for injunctive relief. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the fee program presumably provided adequate medical care at a nominal cost and that the statute did not deny medical services because of inability to pay. The court held that no reasonable jury could find that respondent's co-pay policy represented a cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The court concluded that the state had a legitimate interest in defraying the cost of health care provided to inmates incarcerated in state and county facilities and in reducing the alleged abuse of the sick-call policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief to appellant prisoners in their action against respondent correctional medical service, because the inmate copayment statute was constitutional, as the state had a legitimate interest in defraying the cost of inmate health care and respondent's co-pay policy was not a cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment.

County of Monmouth v. Communications Workers of America


A-3286-94T1, A-3479-94T1, A-3416-94T1, A-3480-94T1, A-3418-94T1, A-3483-94T1, A-3476-94T1, A-4698-94T1, A-3477-94T1, A-0371-95T1, A-3478-94T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


300 N.J. Super. 272; 692 A.2d 990; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 185


February 25, 1997, Argued  
April 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from eleven decisions and orders of the Public Employment Relations Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public employers appealed from separate decisions of the Public Employment Relations Commission (New Jersey), which ruled in favor of respondent unions and declined to restrain the binding arbitration of minor disciplinary actions against civil service employees.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner public employers and respondent unions had entered into collective negotiations agreements that included a provision for the binding arbitration of grievances. In each case, petitioners requested the Public Employment Relations Commission (PERC) to restrain the binding arbitration of a grievance in a minor disciplinary action involving a civil service employee. The cases were consolidated for appeal. The court held that the amended provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. 34:13A-5.3, which permitted binding arbitration as a procedure to resolve minor disciplinary actions involving employees, had a retroactive effect and was applicable to the instant employees. The court held that the amended provision applied to discipline of five days or less. The court held that procedural issues could also be referred to PERC. The court affirmed PERC's decision as to the Township of South Brunswick, holding that the case was not one of discipline. The dismissal of an employee by the County of Union was not within the civil service law. The court affirmed the decisions of PERC with the exception of those case involving non-police employees, which it reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all but three of the decisions of the Public Employment Relations Commission (PERC) with respect to the police employees, and reversed and remanded those decisions involving non-police employees, where PERC determined it had no jurisdiction. The court held that the amendment allowing arbitration for minor disciplinary actions was retroactive in effect.
