Pinkowski v. Township of Montclair


A-5435-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


299 N.J. Super. 557; 691 A.2d 837; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 161


March 10, 1997, Submitted  
April 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 9, 1997. As Corrected May 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land owners appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant township in plaintiffs' action for trespass, inverse condemnation, and negligence after finding a culvert on their property which prevented them from building on the lot.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff land owners brought an action against defendant township for trespass, inverse condemnation, and negligence after finding a culvert on their property which prevented them from building on the lot. Plaintiffs alleged that defendant was palpably unreasonable in constructing a culvert beneath their property without recording an easement, and that defendant should have had notice of the culvert's location when the previous owners requested subdivision approval and applied for a building permit. Defendant joined the surveyor as a third-party defendant. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant. The court held that defendant was granted immunity under the Torts Claims Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 59:2-5, 59:2-6, from plaintiffs' claim for damages from defendant's negligent issuance of subdivision approval and a building permit to the previous owner. The court held that the motion judge was correct in concluding that the construction of the culvert did not change the use of the property or the legal character of a brook on the property because the brook was part of the estate, not an easement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendant township, holding that defendant had been granted immunity from plaintiff land owners' claim for negligence in defendant's issuance of subdivision approval and a building permit, and that construction of a culvert did not change the use of the property or the legal character of a brook on the property because the brook was part of the estate rather than an easement.

Communications Workers of America, AFL-CIO v. New Jersey Dept. of Personnel


A-3195-95T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


299 N.J. Super. 166; 690 A.2d 695; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 142


February 10, 1997, Submitted  
March 31, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Department of Personnel.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civil service employers challenged the determination of respondent commissioner from the New Jersey Department of Personnel, which required appellants to adopt two pilot programs pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11A:2-11i.


OVERVIEW: Respondent commissioner determined that appellant civil service employers were to adopt two pilot programs concerning appellants' hiring processes. Appellants challenged the determination and contended that the programs violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11A:2-11i. The court reversed the determination. The court held that the pilot programs exceeded the scope of powers which could have lawfully been delegated under § 11A:2-11I, violated the plain language of § 11A:2-11I by administratively controverting and altering the express provisions of existing statutes, and that they should not have been adopted without complying with the rule-making requirements of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14B-4. The court found that the programs lacked definitive standards, and that it had been impossible to turn to the statutory scheme as a whole for guidance, because the programs flew in the face of the statutory scheme as was embodied in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11A:4-8 and § 11A:4-15. The court ruled that the grant and exercise of such a totally undirected and unstandardized agency power that deviated from existing legislation, which had been designed to constrain rule making, had been constitutionally insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination of respondent commissioner that had required appellant civil service employers to adopt two hiring programs, because the programs had not been lawfully delegated, lacked definitive standards, and deviated from legislation designed to constrain rulemaking; thus, they were considered constitutionally insufficient.

Rutgers Council of AAUP Chapters v. Rutgers State Univ.


A-5846-94T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


298 N.J. Super. 442; 689 A.2d 828; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 110; 73 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1038


February 20, 1997, Argued  
March 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Division of Pensions, New Jersey Department of the Treasury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, employees and their union, sought review of decision of the Division of Pensions, New Jersey Department of the Treasury, which denied health insurance coverage to employees' same-sex domestic partners and claimed the term "dependents" should be construed liberally and that it was a violation of the New Jersey Law Against Discrimination to deny benefits based on sexual orientation as well as a violation to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employees were denied health insurance coverage under the state health benefits plan for their same-sex domestic partners based on the failure to satisfy the statutory definition of "dependents" as spouses under New Jersey law. Appellants and their union sought review of the decision. The court affirmed in part, dismissed in part and remanded the case in part and held that the decision to deny same-sex domestic partners health insurance benefits did not violate the Law Against Discrimination (LAD) because the statutory exception to the LAD was part of the later enactment and intended to place programs such as the one appellant's are under, outside the scope of the LAD. The court further held there was not violation of equal protection because the statute was facially neutral and appellant's could not show a discriminatory intent behind the marital status classification. The court also held that there was no violation of the Executive Order that prohibited executive branch agencies from discriminating on the basis of sexual orientation because the state health benefits plan refers to marital status, not sexual orientation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination to deny appellant employee's same-sex domestic partners health insurance benefits under the state health benefits plan, dismissed appellant's complaint and appeal against the state, and remanded the case for further determinations against remaining respondent the university employer.

State v. Friedman


A-5803-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


304 N.J. Super. 1; 697 A.2d 947; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 336


February 10, 1997, Argued  
March 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant homeowners sought review of an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which affirmed their convictions for violations of plaintiff township's anti-noise ordinance in connection with eight separate occasions in which defendants' dog's barking awakened defendants' neighbor in the early morning hours.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant homeowners contended that, as it was applied to them, plaintiff township's anti-noise ordinance was unconstitutionally subjective and vague and that the trial judge's evidentiary rulings were erroneous because they had been based upon an unconstitutionally subjective and vague construction of the ordinance. The court, however, noted that although the challenged ordinance was defectively vague in its failure to provide any guidance as to what constituted a violation of its provisions, it was not facially unconstitutional. The court held that such general language was permissible so long as courts utilized a reasonableness standard when applying the ordinance. The court then found that a purely subjective standard of behavior had been utilized to determine whether dog's barking had constituted a disturbance of the peace, noting that such a standard was unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed, concluding that although the neighbor's testimony had been sufficient to establish the times when defendants' dog had barked, her testimony failed to establish that its barking constituted an objectively unreasonable noise as required by New Jersey law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had upheld defendant homeowners' convictions for purported violations of plaintiff township's anti-noise ordinance, finding that although testimony at trial established the timing and the frequency of defendants' dog's barking, there was insufficient testimony to establish that the barking constituted an objectively unreasonable noise.

James Const. Co. v. Board of Public Utilities


A-3623-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


298 N.J. Super. 355; 689 A.2d 784; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 99


January 22, 1997, Argued  
March 6, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 10, 1997.
As Amended April 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff and defendant construction companies appealed a judgment from the Morris County Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed a complaint that challenged the constitutionality of the Underground Facility Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 48:2-73 to -91.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and defendant construction companies sought review after the trial court dismissed a complaint challenging the constitutionality of the Underground Facility Protection Act (UFPA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 48:2-73 to -91. Specifically, the construction companies argued that the UFPA was unconstitutional because the state legislature had created its own procedure to indict violators and enacted a statute that allowed for the imposition of criminal penalties without affording an indictment and trial by jury. The court found that the construction companies' contentions addressed to the statute's constitutionality was without merit. The Board of Public Utilities' investigatory powers and hearings were not part of criminal proceedings and criminal sanctions could not flow therefrom. As no criminal proceeding was involved, and there was no administrative determination of guilt or innocence, the court concluded that the separation of power doctrine was not violated. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment, which dismissed a complaint that challenged the constitutionality of the Underground Facility Protection Act, was affirmed because plaintiff and defendant construction companies' contentions addressed to the statute's constitutionality were found to be without merit.

Hamilton Amusement Center, Inc. v. Poritz


A-3176-95T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


298 N.J. Super. 230; 689 A.2d 201; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 94


January 6, 1997, Argued  
February 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 5, 1997. As Corrected April 28, 1997.
Certification granted Hamilton Amusement Ctr. v. Poritz, 150 N.J. 24, 695 A.2d 667, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 524 (1997)
Affirmed by Hamilton Amusement Ctr. v. Verniero, 156 N.J. 254, 716 A.2d 1137, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 628 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which declared N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:34-7(c) unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 6, and awarded appellee businesses permanent injunctive relief from enforcement of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and permanent injunction in favor of appellee businesses because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:34-7(c) was neither an unconstitutional content-based restriction on free speech under U.S. Const. amend. I and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 6, nor unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the statute involved commercial speech, which did not trigger a strict scrutiny standard. The statute's purpose struck a balance between the right of sexually-oriented businesses to reasonably announce their presence to potential patrons, and the legislative perception that sexually-oriented signage on a large scale created distractions which interfered with traffic safety and the welfare of minors. The statute did not curb political or noncommercial speech. The court held that the protected commercial speech of sexually-oriented businesses was lawfully regulated because the statute directly advanced a substantial governmental interest and was appropriately tailored to that purpose. The court further held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's holding that the statute, which regulated the signage of appellee businesses was unconstitutional because the statute regulated commercial speech not subject to a strict scrutiny standard, the statute was supported by legitimate state interests, and was not unconstitutionally vague.

Communications Workers of America, AFL-CIO v. Whitman


A-6115-94T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


298 N.J. Super. 162; 689 A.2d 166; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 91

February 27, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 3, 1997.
Certification denied by Communications Workers of Am. v. Whitman, 152 N.J. 191, 704 A.2d 21, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 713 (1997)
Certification denied by Communications Workers of Am. v. Whitman, 152 N.J. 191, 704 A.2d 21, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 716 (1997)
Subsequent appeal at Communications Workers of Am.v Whitman, 335 N.J. Super. 283, 762 A.2d 284, 2000 N.J. Super. LEXIS 419 (N.J. Super. Ct. App. Div., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former state employees at motor vehicle agencies that were re-privatized pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14C-1-11, appealed from order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, that dismissed plaintiffs' complaint against defendant state officials. Plaintiffs claimed that re-privatization violated their First Amendment rights by discriminating against them on the basis of party affiliation.


OVERVIEW: Certain state-operated motor vehicle agencies were re-privatized pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14C-1-11. The agencies continued to operate using private agents as independent contractors, who were appointed by the Director pursuant to appointment power conferred by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-3. The court reversed the dismissal of the First Amendment claim, finding that plaintiffs' allegations that they were refused appointment due to their political beliefs was a cognizable First Amendment claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiffs', former state employees, U.S. Const. amend. I claims, holding that plaintiffs who alleged that they were refused appointment because of their political beliefs or political inaction stated a cognizable First Amendment claim, but affirmed the dismissal as to plaintiffs' claims of violation of public contract bidding statutes and denial of due process and equal protection.

State v. Burgess


A-7127-94T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


298 N.J. Super. 254; 689 A.2d 730; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 70


October 29, 1996, Submitted  
February 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 20, 1997. As Revised February 25, 1997. Second Revision March 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Ocean County, New Jersey, which denied his petition for post-conviction relief on his conviction under the drug-kingpin statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under the drug-kingpin statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-3. Subsequent to his conviction and unsuccessful direct appeal, case law required that the jury must be given specified definitions of "upper echelon member" and "organized drug trafficking network." The trial court dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief based on the trial court's failure to give the required jury charge. The court held that the definitional requirement was not a sudden and unanticipated repudiation of a long-standing practice, but was merely a clarification of the inherent ambiguity of the statute. The court held that the definitions were essential elements of the offense. The court found that retroactive application of the decision would not burden the administration of justice because retroactive application could only result in 10 new trials, including that of defendant. The court held that defendant was prejudiced by the improper jury charge and refused to speculate on what a properly instructed jury would have decided. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief because the jury was not charged as to essential definitions under the drug-kingpin statute, even thought this requirement was developed subsequent to defendant's conviction.

 

875 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Chez Sez VIII, Inc. v. Poritz


A-1729-95T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


297 N.J. Super. 331; 688 A.2d 119; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 55


January 6, 1997, Argued  
February 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 7, 1997. As Corrected March 26, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 20, 1997, Reported at: 522 U.S. 932, 118 S. Ct. 337, 139 L. Ed. 2d 262, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6324.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, that declared N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-12.2 unconstitutional as a content-based restriction on free speech and void for vagueness and that permanently enjoined the statute's enforcement against anyone, including appellees, owners of pornographic supply stores. The state contended that the statute was content neutral.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, owners of pornographic supply stores, brought a declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-12.2, which prohibited the provision by commercial establishments of booths that facilitated sexual activity. The state challenged the trial court's determination that the statute was an unconstitutional content-based restriction on free speech and was further void for vagueness. In reversing, the court concluded that the statute was a content neutral regulation, where its overall purpose was aimed at the secondary effects of speech. Under the time, place, and manner standard, the statute was valid where it was designed to serve a substantial government interest and did not unreasonably limit alternative avenues of communication. The statute did not seek to ban the viewing of sexually explicit material, but was intended to regulate sexual conduct as a health problem. Further, it was not void for vagueness, as it adequately proscribed conduct and instructed commercial establishments to refrain from facilitating such conduct on their premises.


OUTCOME: The superior court judgment declaring the challenged statute to be invalid as an unconstitutional content-based restriction on free speech and to be void for vagueness was reversed, as the statute was content-neutral where it was aimed not at speech itself but the secondary effects thereof. Further, the statute was not void for vagueness where it set forth the proscribed conduct and mandated that establishments refrain from its facilitating.

Ende v. Cohen


A-1270-96T1F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


296 N.J. Super. 350; 686 A.2d 1239; 1997 N.J. Super. LEXIS 16


December 18, 1996, Argued  
January 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 15, 1997. As Corrected January 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, university hospital, medical executive committee, and board of trustees, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which granted respondent physician's request for injunctive relief and disqualified appellants, medical executive committee and board of trustees, from taking any further action in a proceeding to deny renewal of respondent's hospital privileges.


OVERVIEW: Respondent physician was a member of the teaching staff at appellant university medical school. Appellant medical executive committee (MEC) voted to deny renewal of respondent's staff privileges at the university hospital. Respondent requested a full adversarial hearing by appellant MEC. Prior to the hearing, respondent brought an action alleging breach of contract, age and handicap discrimination, and various due process violations. The trial court granted respondent's request for injunctive relief and disqualified appellant MEC and appellant board of trustees from taking any further action regarding respondent's hospital privileges. The court reversed the order, holding that the mere fact that appellant MEC and appellant board of trustees investigated the matter and made preliminary decisions not to renew respondent's staff privileges did not render those bodies incompetent to adjudicate the issue in the context of an adversarial plenary hearing. The court rejected the assertion that the combination of investigative and adjudicative functions necessarily created an unconstitutional risk of bias in the administrative adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that granted respondent physician's request for injunctive relief and disqualified appellants, medical executive committee and board of trustees, from taking any further action in a proceeding to deny renewal of respondent's staff privileges. The court held that the combination of investigative and adjudicative functions did not create an unconstitutional risk of bias in the administrative adjudication.

Jackson v. Georgia-Pacific Corp.


A-3490-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


296 N.J. Super. 1; 685 A.2d 1329; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 466; 72 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1132


November 14, 1996, Argued  
December 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foreman appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey) following a jury determination that he had not proved that he was doing his job as was expected by defendant employer. Plaintiff employee had brought an action under the Law Against Discrimination (LAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 10:5-1 to 42, against defendant employer, alleging that his termination had been racially motivated.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff foreman was terminated by defendant employer following an incident when he waited four hours before sending an injured employee to the hospital. He brought an action including allegations under the Law Against Discrimination (LAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 10:5-1 to 42, that his termination was racially motivated. A jury ruled in defendant's favor. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that there was no evidence that an improper racial animus played a part in plaintiff's firing sufficient to shift the burden to defendant to explain that even so, it would still justifiably have fired plaintiff. The court held that plaintiff admitted that he had been warned with respect to his abusive treatment of his crew and to be more aware of safety, and that the plant manager told him he was being fired for failing to do so. The only evidence of defendant's reasons for firing plaintiff was the plant manager's testimony that he made the decision only after the injury incident because it was the last straw in a series of incidents that had occurred over an extended period of time and after repeated warnings from management and which reflected improper treatment of employees and their safety.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of defendant was affirmed because plaintiff failed to show that his termination was racially motivated. He was warned against actions such as that leading to his termination. Defendant's award of summary judgment on plaintiff's employee manual claim was affirmed because no reasonable employee could fail to understand that the manual was not intended to alter defendant's right to terminate its employees with or without cause.

Skaperdas v. Director, Div. of Taxation


A-4569-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


295 N.J. Super. 293; 685 A.2d 18; 16 N.J. Tax 454; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 428


October 17, 1996, Argued  
November 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Approved for Publication November 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, whose decision is partially reported at 14 N.J. Tax 103 (Tax 1994).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment from the Tax Court of New Jersey, finding plaintiffs were personally liable for the unpaid sales and use taxes of a corporation in which they were officers, directors, and shareholders.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged a tax court decision holding them personally liable for the unpaid sales and use taxes of a corporation in which they were officers, directors, and shareholders. Defendant Division of Taxation (Division) cross-appealed from that portion of the judgment determining that one plaintiff was not personally liable for the taxes. The court found that where plaintiffs were officers, directors and shareholders who supervised the store manager and were intimately involved in the day to day operations of the corporation, personal liability applied to them, and they had a duty to act for the corporation under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-2(w). The court affirmed the judgment, holding plaintiffs were personally liable for the unpaid sales and use taxes of a corporation in which they were officers, directors, and shareholders because they had a duty to act for the corporation. The court concluded that that both plaintiffs' and defendant's contentions were clearly without merit, and could perceive no basis to modify or otherwise interfere with the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court judgment that held plaintiffs were personally liable for the unpaid sales and use taxes of a corporation in which they were officers, directors, and shareholders because they had a statutory duty to act for the corporation. The court concluded that that both plaintiffs' appeal and defendant's cross-appeal were without merit.

Sherwood Court v. Borough of South River


A-004131-95T1, 004132-95T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


294 N.J. Super. 472; 683 A.2d 839; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 398


October 8, 1996, Argued  
October 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 28, 1996. As Corrected November 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant apartment owners challenged summary judgments from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, granted in favor of respondents, borough and its utility, against appellants' actions to restrain respondents from the sales of tax lien certificates on appellant's real property pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:62-14.


OVERVIEW: Appellant apartment owners brought actions against respondents, borough and its utility, to restrain respondents from selling, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:62-14, the tax lien certificates on appellants' real property. The court affirmed the order of the superior court, that granted summary judgments to respondents. The court found no grounds to depart from the clear statutory language allowing respondents to place the liens based on the tenants' unpaid bills because appellants gave implied consent to the electrical service from respondents, which created an implied contract. The court found that enforcement of the liens did not cause an absurd result. The court further ruled that the intent was evident in the statute's language and that a common sense reading would support the superior court decision. The superior court's interpretation of the statute recognized the common law doctrine of privity, which the court found to be a requirement to enforce these liens. The court determined that the statute was being enforced in accordance with the common law. The court held that no due process violation existed because appellants provided implicit consent to the electrical service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments granted by the superior court, law division, to respondents, borough and its utility, against the actions of appellant apartment owners to restrain respondents from the selling of the tax lien certificates upon appellants' real property pursuant to statute. The court found no basis to not follow the clear statutory language allowing respondents to place the liens because of appellants' implied consent.

Board of Educ. of Tp. of Neptune v. Neptune Tp. Educ. Ass'n


A-5612-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


293 N.J. Super. 1; 679 A.2d 669; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 309


February 21, 1996, Submitted  
July 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 22, 1996. As Corrected July 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, local board of education, sought review of the decision of the State Board of Education (New Jersey) that disposed of the matter on a motion for summary judgment. The lower court found that appellant's crediting method clearly advanced money to teaching staff members for services not yet rendered to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, local board of education, changed its method of paying over its employees' voluntary salary deductions for credit union and annuity plans. The effect of the change was to deprive the employees of the additional interest that had formerly accrued between the two paydays. The lower court found that appellant's crediting method advanced money to teaching staff members for services not yet rendered. The lower court's decision was affirmed. The court held that the test for public purpose was not who received the funds or even when, but rather the extent to which their expenditure was connected with valid governmental functions or policies. Because public funds could validly be used to achieve a variety of public purposes by a variety of means, there could be no constitutional bar against the reasonable use of public funds to provide benefits of public employment, whether direct or indirect, substantial or incidental.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision was affirmed. The court held that the test for public purpose was not who received the funds or even when, but rather the extent to which their expenditure was connected with valid governmental functions or policies.

Elco v. R.C. Maxwell Co.


A-6594-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


292 N.J. Super. 118; 678 A.2d 323; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 295


May 15, 1996, Argued  
July 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, which reversed the Absecon Zoning Board of Adjustment's decision to grant appellant's application for use variance relief under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-70d.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner applied for a use variance pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-70d and for site-plan approval to permit it to construct a billboard. The Absecon Zoning Board of Adjustment (Board) voted to grant the variance, but the decision was reversed. The court affirmed the lower court's decision to reverse the Board's decision to grant appellant's application for a use variance in order to construct a billboard. Appellant failed to satisfy its substantial burden of proof on the so-called positive and negative criteria in the New Jersey Municipal Land Use Law (MLUL), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-1 to -112. Appellant also failed to establish a special reason for a use variance. Appellant made no effort to develop the property except by applying for the use variance. Appellant could not prove that the billboard variance did not substantially impair the existing zoning scheme, which called for water-oriented business. No state policy was advanced by planting billboards in the wetlands, and a billboard was not compatible with a water-oriented business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision to reverse the Absecon Zoning Board of Adjustment's decision to grant appellant property owner's application for use variance relief because appellant failed to establish a special reason for a use variance and failed to prove that its proposed variance did not substantially impair the existing zoning scheme.

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of cocaine and heroin, possession of firearms, and stolen property, in the Atlantic County Superior Court of New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of multiple drug and firearm charges, and stolen property charges. Defendant claimed that his convictions should be reversed because the trial court denied his request to sever trials, to preclude character and conviction evidence, admitted evidence obtained involuntarily, and denied his motion for a new trial, and request for counsel under the U. S. Const. amend. VI. The court held that the trial court erred when it compelled defendant to proceed on appeal without counsel. It held that defendant had not knowingly, intelligently waived his right to counsel. It also held that the trial court should have engaged in a colloquy with defendant that would test his understanding of the implications of the waiver and will provide the appellate tribunal with an objective basis for review. The trial court did not follow this course, and no attempt was made to determine whether defendant understood the implications of waiving his right to an attorney.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause back to the trial court for further proceedings because it found that it had improperly denied defendant's right to counsel. The court reasoned that even though it said that the other issues presented on appeal were without merit, that was partially because defendant wrote his own brief, which was inexpertly written and very difficult to understand.

F.G. v. MacDonell


A-2055-95T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

April 15, 1996, Argued  
June 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parishioner appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which granted the motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by defendants, the former rector and present rector of Episcopalian churches, pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 4:6-2(e) in plaintiff's action for damages based on a sexual relationship between plaintiff and defendant former rector.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parishioner filed an action for damages based on a sexual relationship between plaintiff and defendant former church rector. The action against defendant present church rector was based on his disclosure of the relationship to the congregation. Defendants moved for judgment on the pleadings, pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 4:6-2(e). The trial court granted the motion on all counts against defendant former rector and on one of the counts against defendant current rector, holding that the actions for clergy malpractice could not be recognized. Plaintiff appealed and the court reversed the trial court's judgment. Noting that the case was one of first impression in New Jersey, the court held that the issues presented problems of proof and definition that should not have been addressed on a motion to dismiss under rule 4:6-2(e), but should have awaited resolution on a more fully informed record. The court concluded that the test to determine whether a cause of action against a cleric was cognizable was whether adjudication required an evaluation of dogma, ritual, or other matters of ecclesiastical concern.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment granting the motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by defendants, a former rector and present rector of two churches, in plaintiff parishioner's action for damages based on a sexual relationship and its disclosure to the congregation. The court held that the issues raised problems of proof that could not be addressed on a motion to dismiss, but required the resolution of a more informed record.

Mehlman v. Mobil Oil Corp.


A-438-94T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


291 N.J. Super. 98; 676 A.2d 1143; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 243


April 22, 1996, Argued  
June 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 13, 1996. As Corrected August 21, 1996.
Certification granted Mehlman v. Mobil Oil Corp., 147 N.J. 264, 686 A.2d 764, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 1611 (1996)
Affirmed by Mehlman v. Mobil Oil Corp., 153 N.J. 163, 707 A.2d 1000, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 242 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a prima facie tort award entered by the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey), in favor of cross-appellant ex-employee in a discharge action. Cross-appellant challenged the pretrial dismissal of his defamation claim and a judgment in favor of appellant on his claim under the Conscientious Employee Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:19-1 to -8.


OVERVIEW: Cross-appellant ex-employee was fired by appellant employer after telling appellant's employees in Japan to reduce benzene levels in gasoline because the chemical posed a serious threat to the public health and environment. Cross-appellant filed suit against appellant under the Conscientious Employee Protection Act (CEPA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:19-1 to -8, and for defamation. The jury ruled in favor of cross-appellant and awarded punitive damages, but the trial court entered judgment for appellant on the CEPA claim because cross-appellant failed to show a clear public policy violated by appellant. The trial court also amended to add a tort claim, entering judgment for cross-appellant, due to appellant's outrageous conduct. The trial court dismissed the defamation claim. On appeal the court reversed in part, as the tort claim was waived by filing a CEPA claim. The jury verdict and damage award was reinstated on the defamation claim, as it was independent of the CEPA claim. The judgment for appellant on the CEPA claim was improper as a CEPA claim could be based an employee's reasonable belief that a public policy was violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, reinstating the jury verdict and punitive damage award on the Conscientious Employee Protection Act (CEPA) claim. The trial court erred in dismissing the defamation claim against appellant employer, because it was independent of a CEPA claim. The court affirmed dismissal of a tort claim as barred by the CEPA waiver provision as it was based on the same retaliatory discharge as the CEPA claim.

Application of New Jersey Bell Telephone Co.


A-5013-92T2, A-5090-92T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

Related proceeding at In re Verizon New Jersey, Inc., 2016 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1526 (App.Div., June 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Board of Regulatory Commissioners.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, ratepayer advocate and cable company, challenged a decision of the Board of Regulatory Commissioners (New Jersey), which determined that the approved plan for a new regulation system provided for just and reasonable rates and met statutory criteria.

Ann. §§ 48:2-21.16 -21.21, did not require the maintenance of any previously approved plan as a prerequisite for effectuating any proposal pursuant to the new regulatory regime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board of Regulatory Commissioner's (Board) decision that the approved plan provided for just and reasonable rates and met the statutory criteria. The court found that the decision was a policy decision within the discretionary authority of the Board as conferred by the legislature and that it bespoke a reasoned conclusion.

N.J. Transit Pba Local 304 v. N.J. Transit Corp.

SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

May 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 21, 1996.
Certification granted New Jersey Transit PBA Local 304 v. New Jersey Transit Corp., 147 N.J. 259, 686 A.2d 761, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 1524 (1996)
Affirmed by New Jersey Transit PBA Local 304 v. New Jersey Transit Corp., 151 N.J. 531, 701 A.2d 1243, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 330 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, transit police officers' representative, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey Essex County, which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant state transit corporation upholding the constitutionality of the random drug and alcohol testing of plaintiff's policemen who carry firearms. The trial court denied plaintiff's application for an order to show cause to obtain a temporary and permanent restraining order.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, transit police officers' representative, filed a complaint against defendant state transit corporation arguing that those provisions of defendant's drug and alcohol policy that mandated the random testing of its policemen who carry firearms constituted an illegal search and seizure under N.J. Const. art. I, para. 7. The trial court entered summary judgment in defendant's favor and denied plaintiff's application for a restraining order. On review, the court affirmed, holding the proper balancing test, after determining whether a special need existed, was balancing the employees' privacy interests against those of the government employer in administering the drug-testing program. The court held defendant's need to conduct random, suspicionless searches outweighed the privacy interests of the officers represented by plaintiff to such a degree it was impractical to require either a warrant or individualized suspicion. The court held the special government need of protecting the public from the risk posed by officers who were impaired by drugs or alcohol could not be ignored. The court held the balancing test supported the constitutionality of defendant's drug-testing policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to uphold the constitutionality of defendant state transit corporation's drug and alcohol policy and to deny plaintiff, transit police officers' representative's, application for a restraining order. The court found that defendant's need to conduct random searches outweighed the privacy interests of those officers to whom the drug and alcohol regulation applied.

S. Jersey Catholic Sch. Teachers Ass'n v. St. Teresa of the Infant Jesus Church Elem. Sch.


A-2593-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


290 N.J. Super. 359; 675 A.2d 1155; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 206; 152 L.R.R.M. 2673


February 15, 1996, Argued  
May 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Catholic School Teachers Association appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey Camden County, which dismissed plaintiff's complaint that sought a mandatory injunction compelling defendant catholic elementary schools to recognize plaintiff as the representative of the parochial school lay teachers employed by defendant and to bargain over terms of employment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff Catholic School Teachers Association attempted to become the collective bargaining representative for lay teachers employed by defendant catholic elementary schools. Plaintiff refused to sign the minimum standards defendants required as a precondition for recognizing plaintiff as the union representative for lay teachers. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's suit, which sought a mandatory injunction compelling defendants to recognize plaintiff as the representative of the lay teachers and to bargain over terms of employment. On review, the court reversed, holding that the compelling state governmental interest expressed in the grant of the fundamental right to organize and bargain collectively by N.J. Const. art. The court held defendants' concerns regarding church autonomy were outweighed by the constitutional provision guaranteeing the rights of working men and women. The court remanded and directed the trial court to order an official representation election and to require defendants to bargain collectively with the chosen representative of the lay teachers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiff Catholic School Teachers Association suit. The court determined the fundamental state constitutional right to organize and bargain collectively outweighed the claimed burden on defendant catholic elementary schools' free exercise of religion rights. The court remanded and directed the trial court to order an official representation election and to order defendant to bargain collectively.

In re Return of Weapons of J.W.D.


A-6436-94T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


290 N.J. Super. 451; 676 A.2d 138; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 200


May 1, 1996, Submitted  
May 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Hunterdon County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hunterdon County, which denied the return of his weapons, and revoked his firearms purchaser's identification card, after domestic violence charges against him were dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Wife signed a domestic violence complaint against appellant husband, and a TRO was issued. Appellant filed a domestic complaint against wife. After a hearing on the merits, both complaints were dismissed, and the TRO was dissolved. The prosecutor filed an objection to the return of weapons, and sought their forfeiture pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:25-21d(3), 58-3f. The trial judge revoked appellant's firearms purchaser's identification card, and ordered that his weapons be forfeited to the state. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the record failed to support the finding that the appellant posed a threat to his wife or the public in general, or that the return of his identification card would not be in the interest of the public health, safety or welfare. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:58-3c(5). The court determined that appellant's weapons and firearm's identification card should be returned to him, because there was insufficient credible evidence to support the judge's order of forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying return of appellant husband's weapons, and firearms purchaser identification card, and remanded. The court held that the record failed to support the finding that the appellant posed a threat to his wife or the public in general, or that the return of his identification card would not be in the interest of the public health, safety or welfare.

 

890 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. B.H.


A-837-93T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


290 N.J. Super. 588; 676 A.2d 565; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 204


September 13, 1995, Argued  
May 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 15, 1996. As Corrected May 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Family Part, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions of violation of a permanent domestic violence retraining order, and harassment, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a), by the Superior Court of Atlantic County (New Jersey), contending that the trial judge erred in finding that his conduct constituted harassment, and that his contact was impermissible under the restraining order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of violating a permanent domestic violence restraining order, and two counts of harassment, under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a). On appeal, defendant contended that the trial judge erred in finding that his conduct constituted harassment, and that his contact was impermissible under the restraining order. The court-reversed defendant's convictions of harassment and held that defendant's mailing of a torn-up support order was not likely to alarm or seriously annoy a reasonable person. The court-reversed defendant's the contempt convictions based on the mailings and held that § 2C:33-4(a) only prohibited defendant from physically entering certain locations, but did not prevent him from sending mail. The court affirmed defendant's contempt conviction arising from an alarming gun-like gesture, which was prohibited conduct under the restraining order.


OUTCOME: The court-reversed defendant's convictions of harassment and held that defendant's mailing of a torn-up support order was not likely to alarm or seriously annoy a reasonable person. The court-reversed defendant's contempt convictions based on the mailing, because the restraining order did not prevent defendant from sending mail. The court affirmed defendant's contempt conviction for using a gun-like gesture.

 

891 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mastapeter


A-4741-94T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


290 N.J. Super. 56; 674 A.2d 1016; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 178


February 7, 1996, Argued; April 15, 1996, Reargued  
May 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence from the Superior Court of Union County (New Jersey), contending he was entitled to "jail time" credit, pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:21-8, for the time he was required to participate in an electronic monitoring wristlet program as a condition of his pretrial release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for attempted murder before the victim died, and was released on bail. After the victim died, defendant was charged with homicide. Pursuant to a negotiated disposition, defendant pled guilty to reckless manslaughter in exchange for a recommendation of a five-year sentence with a three-year parole disqualifier. On appeal, he sought jail time credits because he was placed in the "electronic monitoring program" as a condition of his pretrial release. The trial judge gave detailed reasons for accepting the negotiated disposition and the court found no basis for disturbing the sentence. At the time of plea defendant expressly acknowledged he understood that he did not receive jail credits for the time spent on the wristlet program. The court held defendant was not entitled to credits under N.J. Ct. R. 3:21-8 R. 3:21-8. The prosecutor's decision not to endorse an application for sentencing under the "escape valve" of the Graves Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6.2, was not arbitrary, capricious or unduly discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendant was not entitled to "jail time" credit, for the time he was required to participate in an electronic monitoring wristlet program as a condition of his pretrial release.

 

892 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Schulmann Realty Group v. Hazlet Twp. Rent Control Bd.


A-2763-94T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


290 N.J. Super. 176; 675 A.2d 645; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 182


February 6, 1996, Argued  
April 23, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, owner and operator of a mobile home park, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which dismissed its complaint challenging the decision of defendant rent control board with respect to a hardship rent increase.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, owner and operator of a mobile home park, filed an application with defendant rent control board, for a hardship rent increase. Defendant passed a resolution granting plaintiff a smaller increase than requested to be paid for five years, and determined that the increase would not constitute base rent in any future rent increase applications. The trial court upheld the decision of defendant, and dismissed plaintiff's complaint. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's decision limiting the duration of the rent increases to five years, and excluding the increase from base rent. The court held that, pursuant to the rent control ordinance, defendant was not authorized to make a hardship increase temporary, or exclude such an increase from base rent. The court held that a reviewing court may reject an interpretation of an ordinance by the governing body or rent control board, which conflicts with the plain language of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant rent control board's decision limiting the duration of plaintiff, owner and operator of a mobile home park's, rent increase to five years, and excluding the increase from base rent. The court held that, pursuant to the rent control ordinance, defendant was not authorized to make a hardship increase temporary, or exclude such an increase from base rent.

 

893 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State in Interest of J.G.


A-3585-94T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


289 N.J. Super. 575; 674 A.2d 625; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 163


October 31, 1995, Argued  
April 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 22, 1996.
Certification granted State ex rel. J.G., 146 N.J. 70, 679 A.2d 656, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 1701 (1996)
Modified by, Affirmed by State ex rel. J.G., 151 N.J. 565, 701 A.2d 1260, 1997 N.J. LEXIS 331 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hudson County, whose decision is reported at 283 N.J. Super. 32, 660 A.2d 1274.
State ex rel. J.G., 283 N.J. Super. 32, 660 A.2d 1274, 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 225 (Ch.Div., 1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which ruled that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-43.1 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-2.2 were unconstitutional facially and as applied to defendant juveniles, who were adjudicated delinquent for acts which, if committed by an adult, would constitute aggravated sexual assault, triggering the statutory requirement of mandatory AIDS and HIV testing on request of the victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juveniles were adjudicated delinquent for forcing a 10-year-old girl to engage in sodomy and fellatio, constituting aggravated sexual assault under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2a(1) if committed by an adult. The state requested an order compelling defendants to submit to HIV testing under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-43.1 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-2.2. The trial court denied the order and ruled that the statutes were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the trial court did not err in taking testimony, but did err in giving it more weight than the legislative determination that HIV testing was in the public interest. The court held that while the mandatory removal and analysis of blood to detect HIV constituted a search, the state's compelling interest in the health and welfare of its citizens outweighed defendants' reduced expectation of privacy afforded by their status as adjudicated delinquents, particularly as the intrusion was slight and disclosure of the results tightly controlled. The court held that the statutes did not violate either the federal constitution or N.J. Const. art. I, § 7, and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's determination that the statutes requiring mandatory HIV testing for juvenile sex offenders were unconstitutional, because the state's interest in the health and welfare of the victim and the public outweighed the defendants' interest in preventing a slight bodily intrusion and the risk of disclosure of HIV status, especially as they had a reduced expectation of privacy due to being adjudicated delinquents.

 

894 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roth


A-6767-93T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


289 N.J. Super. 152; 673 A.2d 285; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 144


February 26, 1996, Argued  
March 29, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County, for second-degree theft by extortion under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-5g.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the lower court's for second-degree theft by extortion under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-5g claiming, that his business tactics were not proscribed, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-5g was unconstitutionally vague, improper jury instructions, and denial of self-representation. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction and held that defendant's threat to file a motion to set aside a sheriff's sale unless the successful bidder paid him $ 2,000 constituted attempted theft by extortion. There was ample evidence that had defendant voided the initial sale, he would not have substantially benefitted from a resale because he did not have the financial wherewithal to bid in good faith, and thus it was not business tactics. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional and not vague, and that defendant lacked good cause for substituting counsel and continuing pro se. In light of the untimeliness of defendant's application, the lower court properly found that defendant presented no legitimate basis upon which to delay the proceedings and denied defendant's application on the ground that he sought a de facto co-counsel arrangement with the assistant deputy public defender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction for second-degree theft by extortion. The court held that defendant's threat to file a motion to set aside a sheriff's sale unless the successful bidder paid him $ 2,000 constituted attempted theft by extortion.

Rogan Equities, Inc. v. Santini


A-002605-94T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


289 N.J. Super. 95; 672 A.2d 1281; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 133


November 29, 1995, Argued  
March 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal From Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which denied defendants' motion to vacate the judgment of foreclosure entered in favor of plaintiff creditor that confirmed title in plaintiff who was the purchaser at the foreclosure sale.


OVERVIEW: Defendant property owners owned property upon which a savings & loan association held a first mortgage. Plaintiff creditor held a second mortgage on defendants' property. Plaintiff also held a first mortgage on two tracts of property owned exclusively by defendant mother. The savings & loan association commenced a foreclosure action on the property owned by defendants. Plaintiff purchased the property at the foreclosure sale. Plaintiff asserted that the corporation owned by defendant daughter had defaulted on its loan and instituted an action to foreclose on the two tracts of property. Defendants sought review or an order from the lower court that denied their motion to vacate the judgment of foreclosure entered in favor of plaintiff creditor. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court on the grounds of equitable estoppel, laches, and N.J. Ct. R. 4:50-2. The court found that the explanation for inaction by defendant daughter was inadequate. She had actual knowledge of the action and participated in it both as trustee and as an individual and nevertheless delayed more than two years before claiming that the judgment purporting to bind her and the ensuing sale were void.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that denied defendant property owners' motion to vacate the judgment of foreclosure entered in favor of plaintiff creditor. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment because of the intervening rights of plaintiff who had purchased defendants' property at foreclosure sale, and defendant daughter's delay of more than two years after learning of the foreclosure action to claim the sale was void.

Gennari v. Weichert Co. Realtors


A-5712-93T2F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


288 N.J. Super. 504; 672 A.2d 1190; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 128


January 10, 1996, Argued  
March 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant realtor challenged an interlocutory order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, which, after a bench trial, found defendant realtor liable under the Consumer Fraud Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-2, as the sole proximate cause of plaintiff purchasers' damages resulting from defective construction of their homes. Plaintiffs cross-appealed the dismissal of their fraud claims against defendant builder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant realtor appealed the trial court's interlocutory order finding it liable under the Consumer Fraud Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-2, for damages resulting from defendant realtor's affirmative misstatements to plaintiff purchasers regarding defendant builder's expertise, and plaintiffs cross-appealed the trial court's finding that defendant builder was not liable despite his affirmative misrepresentations. Defendant realtor argued that the trial court should have construed the Act to define misrepresentation according to its common law elements and that punitive damages were improper. The court affirmed the trial court's order as to defendant realtor's liability under the Act, holding that § 56:8-2 makes a New Jersey real-estate-broker defendant strictly liable for any material misrepresentation of fact made to a purchaser. The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiff's fraud claims against defendant builder, because defendant builder's misrepresentations directly caused plaintiff's losses. The court further concluded that defendant realtor's conduct did not justify punitive damages, but that the trial court could consider punitive damages against defendant builder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order holding defendant realtor liable for affirmative misrepresentations to plaintiff purchasers concerning defendant builder's homebuilding expertise, but reversed as to the punitive damage award against defendant realtor, finding its conduct insufficiently wanton or willful to justify the award. The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing plaintiffs' fraud claims against defendant builder.

Whitaker v. Devilla


A-3534-94T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 370; 671 A.2d 163; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 61


December 6, 1995, Argued  
February 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, driver and automobile owner, in a personal injury cause of action arising out of an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, driver and automobile owner, in appellants', husband and wife, cause of action for damages arising out of an automobile accident. The trial court ruled that appellants failed to meet the verbal threshold pursuant to the New Jersey Deemer Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4. Appellants were residents of Pennsylvania and covered by an insurance policy with full tort option, comparable to New Jersey's no threshold coverage. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees and ruled that, although appellants failed to meet the verbal threshold requirements, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1-4, appellants' claim was not barred because they elected a comparable no threshold coverage with a company licensed to do business in New Jersey. The court held that, under the New Jersey's Deemer Statute, a person insured under an automobile policy issued in another state by a company licensed to do business in New Jersey was deemed to have chosen and was subject to the tort option specified in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-8(a), the verbal threshold, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees, driver and automobile owner, and held that the New Jersey Deemer Statute did not bar the claim of appellants, husband and wife, because appellants elected comparable no threshold coverage with a company licensed to do business in New Jersey and the language employed by the legislature in the Deemer provision was not intended to restrict the rights of appellants.

 

898 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


A.F. v. Fauver


A-5695-94T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 354; 671 A.2d 155; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 59


January 31, 1996, Submitted  
February 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Final Determination of the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates challenged a decision of the Department of Corrections (New Jersey), which adopted an amendment to N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10A, § 4.41(a) that added the refusal to register as a sex offender to the list of acts punishable if committed by an inmate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmates challenged the Department of Corrections' adoption of "refusal to register as a sex offender" to N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10A, § 4.4.1(a), pursuant to Megan's Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:7-1 to 11, questioning the amendment's constitutionality. They were confined for sexual offenses previously committed by them and were covered by the requirements of Megan's Law. On appeal, the court affirmed the adoption of the amendment, finding that the amendment was constitutional. The court found the amendment was not vague because the amendment merely added the refusal to register as a sex offender to the list of prohibited acts for which inmates could be punished and the requirement was clear. Further, the court determined that the statutory provisions, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:7-2c(2) and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:7-4b, put all persons on notice of the requirements of registration and that they could be punished for refusing to comply with them. The court concluded that the amendment was valid because it was reasonably related to a legitimate penological interest, such as complying with the law requiring a system of registration for sex offenders or safeguarding the public at large.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Department of Corrections' adoption of an amendment. The court held the amendment was not vague as it added the refusal to register as a sex offender to the list of prohibited acts pursuant to Megan's Law, and the statutory provisions put persons on notice of the need to register or face punishment. The court ruled that the amendment was valid because it bore a reasonable relationship to a legitimate penological interest.

3085 Kennedy Realty Co. v. Tax Assessor of City of Jersey City


A-6452-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 318; 671 A.2d 137; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 55


January 10, 1996, Submitted  
February 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed plaintiff's complaint against defendants, tax assessor, city, and bank, and denied both relief and reconsideration for lack of jurisdiction. Plaintiff sought to enjoin defendant bank from foreclosing on two parcels of land that had been taken by defendant city due to unpaid taxes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer, by order to show cause and a verified complaint, filed an action against defendants, tax assessor, city, and bank, to stop actions to foreclose plaintiff's equity of redemption in two parcels of land. The trial court denied the requested relief on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction. By motion for reconsideration, plaintiff argued that N.J. Ct. R. 4:69-1 et seq., governing actions in lieu of prerogative writs, conferred jurisdiction on the trial court to grant the relief which it sought. The motion was denied and plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed the decision, holding that the order dismissing plaintiff's claim was properly entered with prejudice. The court held that plaintiff's claim should have been brought on direct appeal from the judgments of the county board of taxation and the tax court. Plaintiff contended that the trial court had jurisdiction as its claim was based on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court determined that plaintiff's § 1983 claim was barred by the statute of limitations because it accrued when plaintiff knew it was being taxed on the basis of an arbitrary and unfair assessment, which arose more than two years before filing the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's claim against defendants, tax assessor, city, and bank, holding that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations. The court held that plaintiff's claim accrued when plaintiff knew it was being taxed on the basis of an arbitrary and unfair assessment, which arose more than two years before plaintiff filed the claim.

State v. Robertson


A-5662-93T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 240; 670 A.2d 1096; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 50


December 4, 1995, Argued  
February 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 7, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court of Monmouth County (New Jersey), for the fourth degree crime of unlawful regulated activity in a freshwater wetlands area by willfully or negligently engaging in a regulated activity within such an area without a permit, contrary to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:9B-9a, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:9B-17a, and N.J. Stat. Ann. 13:9B-21f.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had wood chips brought in to help level part of his land. He was charged with unlawful regulated activity in a freshwater wetlands area by willfully or negligently engaging in a regulated activity within such an area without a permit, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:9B-9a, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:9B-17a, and N.J. Stat. Ann. 13:9B-21f. During deliberations, a juror asked the judge if defendant had a responsibility to investigate whether what he wished to do could be done either with or without a permit. The judge restated the elements of the crime and emphasized that the elements did not include a requirement that the state prove defendant knew the area in question was wetlands. The jury shortly returned with a conviction. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and remanded for a new trial or other action the prosecutor or commissioner deemed appropriate. The court found that the trial judge, by advising the jury that the state was not required to prove defendant knew the area in question was either a wetlands or a transition area, effectively made defendant strictly liable and, for practical purposes, directed the verdict against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for unlawful regulated activity in a freshwater wetlands area by willfully or negligently engaging in a regulated activity within such an area without a permit and remanded the case. The court held that the trial judge's advice to the jury that the state did not have to prove defendant knew the area was a wetlands area made defendant strictly liable and effectively directed the verdict against him.

State v. Malia


A-879-94T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 198; 670 A.2d 1075; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 47


December 12, 1995, Submitted  
February 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey which convicted him of possession of cocaine and sentenced him to three years probation with several conditions, including strict narcotic controls.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by the police because the rear lights of his car were out. As he was pulling over, the officer saw him bend down towards the floor, and, when he asked defendant for his license, he detected the odor of alcohol. He then searched the car and found cocaine in it. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to grant his motion to suppress and that a jury charge diluted the state's burden of proof and thus denied him due process of law. The state claimed that the trial court erred in not imposing mandatory penalties. In affirming the judgment, the court found the missing rear lights gave police had a reasonable suspicion of a motor violation. It also found that defendant's furtive movements and the odor of alcohol gave the officer probable cause to believe a crime had been committed; thus, the search of the car was justified. Therefore, the motion to suppress was properly denied. The court found that the jury charge which included the phrase "the law requires a moral certainty" with respect to a finding of guilt did not dilute the state's burden of proof. The court found that the fees for the statutory violation were mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because his initial stop by police for a traffic violation was clearly justified and his actions, together with the odor of alcohol, gave police probable cause to believe that a crime had been committed and to search defendant's car. The phrase "moral certainty" in the jury charge on reasonable doubt did not dilute the state's burden of proof. The case was remanded for imposition of statutory penalties.

 

902 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Dolan v. City of East Orange


A-2222-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


287 N.J. Super. 136; 670 A.2d 587; 1996 N.J. Super. LEXIS 44


November 6, 1995, Submitted  
January 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 30, 1996. As Corrected March 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a city administrator, appealed from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, an employee and his labor union representative, on their claims that plaintiff employee's termination was unconstitutional and directed defendant city to reinstate plaintiff employee pending a new hearing.


OVERVIEW: After a disciplinary hearing, plaintiff employee, was terminated from employment in connection with an altercation he had with a subordinate employee. After defendant city rejected plaintiff employee's request for a rehearing, plaintiff employee and plaintiff labor union representative filed a complaint against defendant city and defendant city administrator. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, directing defendant city to reinstate plaintiff employee. The court affirmed the summary judgment ruling, but reversed and dismissed the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. The court held that the trial court properly exercised jurisdiction to review the municipal action taken by defendant city in an action in lieu of prerogative writs under N.J. Ct. R. 4:69. The court held that although plaintiff employee's hearing passed constitutional muster, it was not fair because he did not have an opportunity to confront and cross-examine his employee. However, because plaintiff employee's right to confront and cross-examine the adverse witness was not of federal constitutional dimension, it did not provide a basis for § 1983 action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, an employee and his labor union representative, on its claim against defendant city because plaintiff employee was not given an opportunity to confront an adverse witness at his hearing. The court reversed and dismissed plaintiff employee's civil rights claim because his federal constitutional rights were not implicated.
