Merola v. Department of Corrections


A-6334-93T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


285 N.J. Super. 501; 667 A.2d 702; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 559


November 8, 1995, Argued  
December 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 1, 1995.
Certification denied by Merola v. Department of Corrections, 143 N.J. 519, 673 A.2d 277, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 304 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Decision of the Department of Corrections.
State v. Merola, 214 N.J. Super. 108, 518 A.2d 518, 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1491 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the calculation by respondent, Department of Corrections (New Jersey), of the end date of his term of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was sentenced to a 30-year mandatory minimum sentence for his conviction for murder, as well as other sentences to be served concurrently with this sentence for other convictions. Respondent, Department of Corrections, calculated appellant's end date of the term of his incarceration to be 30 years from the beginning of his incarceration. The court affirmed, holding that inmate's period of parole ineligibility could not be reduced, either through the application of commutation credits or through the compilation of inmate work credits, below the statutorily mandated term of imprisonment for murder. The court held that since the full sentence and the mandatory minimum term were of the same length, inmate simply could not reduce his 30-year sentence. The court further held that inmate could not establish that he had secured a federal constitutional right to reduce his mandatory minimum sentence. The court held there was nothing unconstitutional in distinguishing between inmates based on the severity of the crimes committed and reserving the strictest sentences for murderers.


OUTCOME: Calculation by respondent, Department of Corrections, of the end date of appellant inmate's term of incarceration affirmed because inmate's period of parole ineligibility could not be reduced below the statutorily mandated term of imprisonment for murder, and such restriction was not unconstitutional.

 

904 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Gough v. State


A-2074-93T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


285 N.J. Super. 516; 667 A.2d 1057; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 544


September 20, 1995, Argued  
November 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged the order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey), that denied appellant's motion for declaratory judgment to declare the oath of allegiance required of school teachers in New Jersey unconstitutional. Appellant alleged that said oath violated his rights of free speech, association, assembly, and to petition for redress of grievances.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teacher applied for a substitute teaching position in the public school system. As part of the application requirements, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:6-7 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:26-9, appellant was required to sign an oath of allegiance to support the constitutions of the United States and New Jersey and to bear allegiance to the same and to the governments established in the United States and the State of New Jersey. Prior to signing the oath, appellant added qualifying amendments to the oath. Appellant was interviewed and led to believe that he would be called to teach. Appellant was never called to substitute teach. Upon inquiry, appellant learned that he would not be called to substitute teach because of the qualifications he added to the oath. Appellant brought an action for declaratory judgment and alleged that the oath violated his U.S. Const. amend. I and U.S. Const. amend. XIV rights. The court held that the required oath did not violate appellant's constitutional rights and that the New Jersey oath was similar to the Colorado oath which was summarily affirmed by the United States Supreme Court as constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied appellant teacher's motion to declare unconstitutional the oath of allegiance required of New Jersey schoolteachers. The court concluded that the traditional statutory oath did not violate the state and federal constitutional rights of free speech, association, or assembly, or expression and did not inhibit political beliefs or activities.

 

905 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


City of Newark v. Townshp of Hardyston


A-672-94T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


285 N.J. Super. 385; 667 A.2d 193; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 536


September 20, 1995, Argued  
November 13, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final judgment of the Tax Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of the judgment of the Tax Court (New Jersey), which held in favor of appellee state that, in assessing the value of four parcels of watershed property, discounted the value because the moratorium from the Watershed Protection Act, 1988, c. 163 as amended by L. 1990, c.19, continued to be valid and was a factor to be considered in valuing watershed land for tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township contested appellee state's assessment of the value of watershed property which was discounted by the moratorium from the Watershed Protection Act, 1988, c. 163 as amended by l. 1990, c. 19 (Act). The tax court held the Act was valid and a factor in valuing watershed land. Appellant sought review and on appeal the court affirmed. The court held that the legislature intended the moratorium to continue, that it anticipated that watershed protection would go forward and although a final comprehensive bill had not yet passed, this did not mean that all prior activity should be vitiated. The court held an interpretation of the Act concluding that the moratorium expired would fly in the face of common sense, omit consideration of the breadth and importance of the legislative objectives, and render the 1990 amendment futile. The court held the legislature intended the limit on the transfer of watershed lands to continue until a statewide watershed system was in place, the moratorium was still in effect, the moratorium was not a temporary restraint that created a transitory absence of market, and thus, it was properly considered in determining true value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the value appellee state assessed appellant township's watershed property which was discounted by the moratorium from watershed protection legislation because the moratorium was still effective, it was not a temporary restraint creating only a transitory absence of market, and thus it was properly considered as a factor in valuing the watershed land.

State in Interest of S.M.


A-6415-93T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


284 N.J. Super. 611; 666 A.2d 177; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 517


September 28, 1995, Argued  
October 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 27, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Somerset County, New Jersey, which convicted him of two counts of juvenile delinquency for first-degree aggravated sexual assault under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2a(1), and second-degree aggravated sexual assault under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2b.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was convicted of two counts of juvenile delinquency, which, if committed by an adult would have constituted first-degree aggravated sexual assault under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2a(1) and second-degree aggravated sexual assault under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2b. Appellant was originally sentenced to 18 months of detention, but the trial court granted his motion to amend the sentence and appellant was placed on probation for two years. The court vacated appellant's sentence and remanded for resentencing because the 2-year probationary term exceeded his original sentence of 18 months of incarceration. R. Evid. 803(c)(27) because appellant failed to request a hearing under N.J. R. Evid. 104(a), and appellant failed to articulate any prejudice that resulted from the court's failure to hold such a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant juvenile's sentence and remanded for resentencing because the 2-year probationary term exceeded appellant's original sentence of 18 months of incarceration. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the aggravated sexual assault statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and the use of the victim's statements to his father and the police did not require reversal.

 

907 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Loftwich v. Fauver


A-1647-94T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


284 N.J. Super. 530; 665 A.2d 1133; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 495


October 3, 1995, Submitted  
October 19, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the New Jersey Department of Corrections that set his maximum total sentence expiration date on three convictions and two parole violations. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-5c provided that on a prison sentence for a crime committed while on parole, the new term and any term of re-imprisonment on the parole revocation were to run consecutively unless the trial court ordered otherwise.


OVERVIEW: New Jersey Department of Corrections set appellant's maximum aggregate sentence expiration date after appellant was convicted of three crimes and committed two parole violations by new crimes. Appellant sought review putting into issue the maximum aggregate sentence expiration. The court found that the issue presented centered on N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-5c. At the time, periods of imprisonment for a crime committed while on parole and periods of re-imprisonment for prior crimes committed were to run consecutively unless otherwise ordered by the trial court. Prior to 1984, they were to run concurrently unless otherwise ordered. Appellant was sentenced before the effective date of the amendment, but violated parole after that date. The court found that there was no violation of ex post facto law under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or N.J. Const. art. IV, § 7. The court did not see any disadvantage to appellant under the amendment because both before and after the 1984 amendment, P.L. 1983, c. 462, § 1, to § 2C:44-5c, it remained the responsibility of the trial court to determine whether or not sentences should run concurrently or consecutively. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination of the department of corrections. The court found that appellant was not disadvantaged by the application of the statutory amendment providing for consecutive sentences even though, prior to the amendment, the statute had provided for concurrent sentences, and appellant was sentenced before the effective date of that amendment but violated parole after that date.

State v. L.C.


A-6948-93T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


283 N.J. Super. 441; 662 A.2d 577; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 270


May 2, 1995, Argued  
August 8, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife appealed from the Superior Court, Law Division, of Hunterdon County (New Jersey), amended order of disposition finding her in contempt of court for violating domestic relations restraining orders issued under the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act of 1991, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 25-17 et seq. Defendant was convicted of violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 29-9.


OVERVIEW: In the course of defendant wife's separation and divorce, a temporary restraining order was issued under the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act of 1991, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 25-17 et seq., barring her from having contact with her husband except in matters related to their children. Defendant was convicted of violating the temporary restraining order and the final restraining order. The court affirmed the first conviction, reversed the second, and noted that the sentence was incorrect. The matter was remanded for correction and further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part, the order finding defendant wife in contempt of court for violating domestic relations restraining orders. Defendant's words did not constitute the "harassment" required for conviction under the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act for violating a restraining order. The court remanded for correction of the sentence and further proceedings.

New Jersey Hosp. Ass'n v. Fishman


A-898-94T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


283 N.J. Super. 253; 661 A.2d 842; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 266


March 28, 1995, Argued  
August 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 1, 1995. As Corrected September 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital association sought review of an order of the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health denying a tax assessment refund under the Health Care Cost Reduction Fund, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 26:2H-18.24-18.50, in favor of respondent attorney general and state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital association sought review of order by the state commissioner of the department of health (commissioner), which denied refund of tax assessments paid under the Health Care Cost Reduction Fund, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 26:2H-18.50, based on the contention that such over-collection of assessments paid following a court determination that such assessments were excessive entitled them to relief. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent attorney general and state and dismissed the appeal, concluding that appellant was not entitled to retroactive application of the decision declaring the assessments excessive, and that prospective relief of refund was also unavailable. The court explained appellant was not entitled to a refund because the payments made were voluntary and not a product of any duress exercised by the commissioner. The court further noted that where a tax was voluntarily paid on a demand not enforceable without fraud , duress, or mistake of fact, as here, such payments were not recoverable. The court concluded that no mistake of fact existed because appellant's mistake was one of law, where it paid based on belief the assessments were correct.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant hospital association's requested review and affirmed the state commissioner of the department of health's order denying appellant a refund for over-collected tax assessments under the Health Care Cost Reduction Fund because such payments were not recoverable when voluntarily paid without actual or threatened duress or while under a mistake of fact.

WHS Realty Co. v. Town of Morristown


A-6388-93T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


283 N.J. Super. 139; 661 A.2d 320; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 244


May 8, 1995, Argued  
July 10, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 10, 1995. As Corrected September 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants township and associated individuals challenged the order of the Superior Court, Morris County (New Jersey), granting appellee realty company partial summary judgment in its equal protection action against appellants. In this action, appellee filed suit against appellants, alleging that appellants' ordinance, which excluded a class of apartment-unit dwellers from garbage collection service, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee realty company filed suit against appellants township and associated individuals alleging that an ordinance that excluded a class of apartment-unit dwellers from garbage collections service violated due process and equal protection rights. The trial court granted appellee partial summary judgment and stated that the distinction made by the ordinance was not rationally related to any legitimate state interest. Accordingly, the trial court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it failed to satisfy federal equal protection requirements. Appellants challenged the trial court's order and claimed that providing garbage service to apartment buildings having less than four units promoted home ownership. The court rejected appellants' argument that the promotion of home ownership was a rational basis for the ordinance's classification and stated that equal protection of the laws was denied unless the service was made available to all apartment-unit dwellers in like circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order granting appellee realty company partial summary judgment against appellants township and associated individuals because appellants' ordinance, which excluded a class of apartment-unit dwellers from garbage collection service, was unconstitutional. The court held that appellee's equal protection rights were violated because there was no rational basis for any distinctions made by the ordinance.

Brown v. Port Authority Police Superior Officers Ass'n


A-3120-93T3, A-3123-93T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


283 N.J. Super. 122; 661 A.2d 312; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 240


May 10, 1995, Argued  
July 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs former employees challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County (New Jersey), which dismissed plaintiffs' labor dispute allegations against defendants Port Authority of New York and New Jersey and union with prejudice because it found federal law preempted state law. Defendant Port Authority of New York challenged the same trial court decision, which required the parties to participate in arbitration.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs former employees filed suit against defendants Port Authority of New York and New Jersey (Port Authority), union, and members based on a labor contract dispute. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' complaint against defendants with prejudice, because federal labor law governed, and ordered the parties to participate in binding arbitration. The parties challenged the trial court's order, and the court reversed the order insofar as it required arbitration because plaintiffs did not assert this relief. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint, but held that the trial court incorrectly surmised that federal labor law governed plaintiffs' claims because defendant Port Authority was exempt from the National Labor Relations Act (NLRA), 29 U.S.C.S. 152 § 2(2). The court held that plaintiffs' claims against defendant union should have been dismissed because they were based on federal labor law and that plaintiffs' claims against Port Authority should have been dismissed for failure to comply with the notice of claim requirements mandated by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 32:1-163. The court found no merit in any promissory or equitable estoppel arguments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order requiring the parties to participate in arbitration. The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs former employees' complaint against defendants Port Authority of New York and New Jersey and union with prejudice, but based its dismissal on plaintiffs' failure to comply with statutory provisions governing suits against state agencies, not federal law preemption.

State v. Piemontese


A-6713-93T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


282 N.J. Super. 307; 659 A.2d 1385; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 224


May 9, 1995, Submitted  
June 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 28, 1995.
Related proceeding at State v. Piemontese, 2017 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2871 (App.Div., Nov. 17, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an adjudication of guilt from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County, which held that appellant violated an ordinance that imposed upon property owners a requirement to prevent lawns, hedges, and bushes from becoming overgrown and unsightly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of violating an ordinance that required a property owner to prevent lawns, hedges, and bushes from becoming overgrown and unsightly. Appellant challenged the adjudication, claiming that the ordinance was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The court held that the phrase "overgrown and unsightly" was not sufficiently definite to give reasonable notice of the prohibited conduct to those who wished to avoid its penalties and to apprise the factfinder of standards of the determination of guilt. In addition, the ordinance was overly broad because it did not permit the enforcement officer acting in good faith to be able to point to objective facts that would have led a reasonable person to realize that his or her conduct was a violation of the ordinance. Therefore, the case was reversed and remanded for entry of a judgment of acquittal.


OUTCOME: Appellant's adjudication of guilt for violating an ordinance that imposed upon property owners a requirement that lawns, hedges, and bushes be kept from becoming overgrown and unsightly was reversed and remanded for entry of a judgment of acquittal because the ordinance was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, failing to provide a standard for the phrase "overgrown and unsightly."

 

913 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Yothers


A-3162-94T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


282 N.J. Super. 86; 659 A.2d 514; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 219


April 12, 1995, Argued  
June 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1995.
As Amended August 29, 1995.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Walsh v. Moore, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27069 (D.N.J., Nov. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which refused to instruct the jury that capital punishment could be imposed for purposely or knowingly causing serious bodily injury resulting in death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with killing two victims and was served at his arraignment with notice of aggravating factors weighing in favor of imposing the death penalty. At trial, the court refused to instruct the jury that capital punishment could be imposed for purposely or knowingly causing serious bodily injury (SBI) resulting in death. On appeal by the state, the court affirmed, holding that the death penalty could not be imposed for purposely or knowingly causing serious bodily injury resulting in death where the offense occurred after adoption of the state constitutional amendment declaring such punishment not cruel and unusual punishment, but before the amendment of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3 to expressly provide that SBI murder may support a death sentence. At the time the constitutional amendment was adopted, the statute did not clearly expose SBI murders to the death penalty. Once the constitutional amendment was approved, it was necessary for the legislature to implement the change. The purpose of placing the amendment before the voters was to remove the constitutional impediment, it did not in itself amount to legislative action amending the existing statute.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court refusing to instruct the jury that capital punishment could be imposed for purposely or knowingly causing serious bodily injury resulting in death was affirmed, because the statutory change allowing capital punishment for such offense did not become effective until three months after the offense occurred.

Matter of Estate of Post


A-917-92T1), A-4014-92T1) Consolidated


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


282 N.J. Super. 59; 659 A.2d 500; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 211


March 20, 1995, Argued  
June 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Probate Part, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both appellant widow and respondent estate sought review of a judgment, entered by the Superior Court of New Jersey, granting appellant an elective share of her late husband's assets, held by respondent estate, pursuant to N. J. Stat. Ann. § 3B:8-1, and denying either party an award of counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant widow elected against her late husband's will and sued respondent estate, demanding additional assets because property received from the decedent and otherwise acquired was less than one-third of the augmented estate under the elective share statute. The lower court rejected respondent's claim of marital disqualification, and awarded additional assets to appellant, while denying counsel fees to either. Both parties appealed, and the court reversed. The lower court's valuation of the "augmented estate" was incorrect, because it included the value of a trust interest which applicable law expressly excluded; because it excluded from the value of appellant's existing assets her interest in a trust settled by her father; and because it applied a "discount" factor to the value of appellant's interests in a decedent's closely held corporation. The court found that a discount was inappropriate in a liquidation sale situation; and that, based on correct valuations of the estate and of appellant's preexisting assets, appellant's share of assets had exceeded one-third of the estate, so that she was not entitled to additional assets. Nor was either party entitled to counsel fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a lower court ruling granting appellant widow additional assets from respondent estate, finding errors in the valuation of the "augmented" estate relating to the inclusion of certain trust assets and the exclusion of others, and finding that the value of appellant's minority interest in decedent's closely held corporation was improperly discounted. The court also held that neither party was entitled to counsel fees.

June 5, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Adoption of Regulations By The New Jersey Casino Control Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advocacy groups for the handicapped sought review of a decision of respondent New Jersey Casino Control Commission which promulgated regulations in N.J. Admin. Code tit.19, § 53 pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 5:12-134 and 135.


OVERVIEW: Appellant advocacy groups for the handicapped challenged regulations promulgated by respondent gaming commission on the grounds that the new regulations implemented only minimal affirmative action requirements for the handicapped. The court held that within the context of the commission's exercise of its interpretative and regulatory authority over N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-134 and -135, the removal of the handicapped from the scope of the commission's previous inclusive equal employment opportunity and affirmative action requirements was arbitrary, unreasonable and without sufficient basis. OUTCOME: The case was remanded to respondent Casino Control Commission on the grounds that the reduction of affirmative employment measures for the handicapped under the current regulations constituted an abuse of the commission's discretion.

State v. Kadelak


A-1243-93T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, after our remand, 258 N.J. Super. 599, 610 A.2d 916 (App. Div. 1992).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant drunk driver appealed after remand the decision upholding his conviction in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Burlington County for driving while intoxicated under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4.50 and upholding the constitutionality of random roadside inspections annually of at least one percent of motor vehicles under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:8-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50 when he was stopped at a random roadside inspection site. He also challenged the constitutionality of the roadside inspections required under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:8-2. The court affirmed defendant's conviction finding that the level-of-intrusion on motorists stopped briefly at mobile inspections teams vehicle safety checkpoints was minimal, usually not more than two to three minutes. The court found that the evidence disclosed that the safety checkpoints uncovered numerous violations that substantially advanced the state's interest in highway and vehicular safety and were an effective regulation and law enforcement technique in enforcing traffic safety. The court found that the state's obligation to the federal government under the Clean Air Act enhanced the safety inspection. The court refused to extend greater protection under the state's constitution than what was provided by the federal constitution. The court vacated the stay imposed on execution of defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and upheld the constitutionality of random roadside safety checkpoints because the intrusion of the stop was minimal lasting two to three minutes and advanced the state's interest in vehicle safety.

 

918 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


A-0714-92T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


279 N.J. Super. 131; 652 A.2d 241; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 56


December 7, 1994, Submitted  
February 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which convicted defendant of multiple charges including first degree kidnapping, attempted aggravated sexual assault, and attempted sexual assault. Pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:13-1c(2), the trial court merged the attempt convictions into the kidnapping conviction and imposed a life term with a 25 year period of parole ineligibility.


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial for kidnapping and sexual assault, the trial court denied defendant's request that the jury consider the preconditions required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:13-1c(2) for the imposition of a life term with a 25 year term of imprisonment without eligibility for parole. Following defendant's convictions for first degree kidnapping, attempted aggravated sexual assault, and attempted sexual assault, the trial court merged the attempt convictions into the kidnapping conviction and imposed § 2C:13-1c(2)'s enhanced sentence. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed the convictions but vacated the sentence. In vacating the sentence, the court found that the trial court was required to submit to the jury the question of whether defendant had committed a sexual assault upon a victim under the age of 16 during the course of the kidnapping in order to impose the enhanced sentence under § 2C:13-1c(2). Furthermore, the court found that defendant's attempt convictions had not provided the requisite foundation for imposing the enhanced sentence under § 2C:13-1c(2) because the attempts had not come within the preconditions required for enhancement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment convicting defendant of first degree kidnapping, attempted aggravated sexual assault, and attempted sexual assault and vacated the merger of the attempt convictions into the kidnapping conviction for sentencing purposes because the state, notwithstanding defendant's attempt convictions, had failed to prove the requisite elements for the imposition of an enhanced sentence under the New Jersey kidnapping statute.

General Motors Corp. v. City of Linden


A-5963-92T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


279 N.J. Super. 449; 653 A.2d 568; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 69


October 5, 1994, Argued  
February 3, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 3, 1995.
Certification granted by GMC v. City of Linden, 142 N.J. 454, 663 A.2d 1361, 1995 N.J. LEXIS 902 (1995)
Appeal granted by GMC v. City of Linden, 144 N.J. 371, 676 A.2d 1088, 1995 N.J. LEXIS 1158 (1995)
Reversed by, Remanded by GMC v. City of Linden, 143 N.J. 336, 671 A.2d 560, 1996 N.J. LEXIS 39 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.
GMC v. City of Linden, 1993 N.J. Tax LEXIS 47 (App.Div., July 7, 1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car manufacturer sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which granted summary judgment in favor or defendants city, tax assessor, and appraiser. Defendants cross-appealed from the denial of their applications for counsel fees and costs in an action claiming arbitrary, discriminatory, and excessive property tax assessment on plaintiff's automobile assembly plant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff car manufacturer brought an action under the Federal Civil Rights Act, against defendants city, tax assessor, and appraiser. The lower court, despite concluding that it lacked jurisdiction, ruled that the individual defendants had absolute immunity from suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and dismissed plaintiff's common law negligence claim. Plaintiff appealed from the summary judgment in defendants' favor. The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's common law negligence claim against defendant appraiser, but reversed the dismissal of plaintiff's § 1983 claims. The court dismissed defendants' cross appeals. The court remanded and directed that the case be assigned to the tax court judge. The court concluded that the trial court erred in holding that it lacked jurisdiction over the matter and in holding that defendants enjoyed absolute immunity from a suit. The court held that because defendant tax assessor's responsibilities were neither legislative nor judicial in nature, no immunity applied. The court held that defendants had not established immunity at common law required to support a claim of absolute immunity from suit under the Federal Civil Rights Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's common law negligence claim against defendant appraiser, but reversed the dismissal of plaintiff's claims under the Federal Civil Rights Act (act). Defendants', tax assessor, city and appraiser, cross appeals were dismissed and case was remanded to tax court judge because defendants had not established immunity at common law that was required to support a claim of absolute immunity under the act.

State v. Press


A-4893-92T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


278 N.J. Super. 589; 651 A.2d 1068; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 23


September 27, 1994, Argued  
January 26, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 26, 1995. As Corrected February 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sentence he received from the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which, after a guilty plea, sentenced him to one year in prison pursuant to the plea agreement. Appellant was charged with selling cocaine with in 1,000 feet of an elementary school. Appellant had accepted the plea agreement offered by the prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with selling cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school. He accepted a plea agreement that sentenced him to one year in prison. Appellant contended that he was treated unfairly because another prosecutor in another county would have given him a more lenient sentence. On appeal, the court agreed that appellant was properly sentenced. By statute, the Comprehensive Drug Reform Act of 1986, N.J.S.A. 2C:35-1 et seq., mandated a minimum sentence of three years without parole. However, prosecutors were allowed to lessen the sentence by plea agreement. The court remanded the case to the trial court because the record did not show that the prosecutor stated why the plea agreement waived the mandatory minimum sentence. This was the only error the court found.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case because it found that the prosecutor had not stated on the record why the plea agreement appellant accepted waived the mandatory minimum sentence of three years in prison for selling cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school. Otherwise, the court affirmed the conviction.

Taylor v. Rorke


A-5192-92T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


279 N.J. Super. 63; 652 A.2d 207; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 26


November 9, 1994, Argued  
January 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured driver and wife, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which dismissed their personal injury tort action against defendant driver pursuant to the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, injured driver and wife, residents of another state, filed a personal injury tort action against defendant driver. The trial court dismissed the action because plaintiffs failed to satisfy the verbal threshold requirements under the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-1 et seq., which limited certain plaintiffs' ability to recover non-economic damages. Plaintiffs argued that the Act's application to out-of-state motorists violated the privileges and immunities clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 1. The court affirmed. Under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17: 28-1.4, nonresidents whose insurer was authorized to transact motor vehicle insurance business in New Jersey were automatically assigned the verbal threshold tort option under N.J. Stat. Ann. 39:6A-8(a), which limited the right to sue for non-economic loss. The court held that the privileges and immunities clause protected only certain fundamental rights basic to the livelihood of the nation. Even if the right to sue for non-economic damages was protected, the legislation passed constitutional scrutiny because it was closely related to the advancement of a substantial state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed plaintiffs, injured driver and wife's, personal injury tort action against defendant driver, and held that the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act, pursuant to which the case was dismissed, did not violate the privileges and immunities clause of the United States Constitution.

 

922 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Jordan v. Dennison


A-3245-93T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


278 N.J. Super. 306; 650 A.2d 1041; 1995 N.J. Super. LEXIS 2


November 15, 1994, Submitted  
January 3, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which refused to apply the 1990 amendment of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-8 retroactively to plaintiff and the jury returned a verdict of no cause of action, in plaintiff's personal injury action against defendant driver.


OVERVIEW: The legislature amended N. J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-8, effective 1990, to afford an injured party, who had no automobile insurance, and was not part of the household of an immediate family member who did, the benefit of the no-threshold option. Plaintiff injured party brought a personal injury action against defendant driver. The trial court refused to apply the 1990 amendment to §39:6A-8 retroactively. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that intent to apply a statute retroactively was implied to give it the most sensible interpretation. There was no reason why the legislature would want to treat plaintiff, who was injured before the 1990 amendment cured an oversight in a 1988 revision of the statute, to be treated differently than those whose injuries occurred after the effective date in 1990. Another justification for retroactive application was that the 1990 amendment provided a change in the form of remedy. Applying the statute retroactively was not manifestly unjust because defendant did not rely on the prior law and his conduct was not motivated by expectations he had concerning the capability of people injured by his negligence to sue him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which refused to apply the relevant amendment retroactively to plaintiff injured party's personal injury action against defendant driver, because the court interpreted the statute retroactively to give it the most sensible interpretation. Applying the statute retroactively was not manifestly unjust because defendant did not rely on the prior law's protection.

F & W Associates v. County of Somerset


A-1104-93T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


276 N.J. Super. 519; 648 A.2d 482; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 416


September 19, 1994, Submitted  
October 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developers sought review of a judgment of defendant planning board (New Jersey) that assessed a contribution for future traffic improvements against plaintiff after defendant approved plaintiff's proposed subdivision plan, pursuant to the County Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:27-1 to -8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant planning board approved plaintiff developers proposed subdivision and reserved the necessity of off tract traffic improvements. A study was done and plaintiffs were assessed a contribution for future traffic improvements. Plaintiffs challenged the fee assessed by defendants. The appeals court affirmed, holding that defendant had the authority to assess the fees under the County Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:27-1 to -8. The court held that the assessment was made in accordance with the ordinance and that defendant had the independent power to impose the traffic fees. The argument that the New Jersey Transportation Development District Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 27:1C-1 to -18, was the exclusive means by which traffic impact fees could be assessed against developers was rejected, as the acts were not to be read in conflict. Defendant satisfied the "rational nexus" requirement and the assessment against plaintiffs was proper. As the ordinance was adopted after a comprehensive study and defendant engaged in a rigorous process designed to achieve a fair allocation of increased traffic costs, plaintiffs' objections were unavailing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of defendant planning board that assessed a contribution for future traffic improvements against plaintiff developers after defendant approved plaintiff's proposed subdivision plan, holding that defendant had the authority to assess the fees and that the assessment was made in accordance with the county ordinance and that defendant had the independent power to impose the traffic fees.

Matter of Comprehensive Investigation of School Dist. of Newark


A-704-93T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


276 N.J. Super. 354; 647 A.2d 1383; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 406


September 20, 1994, Submitted  
October 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a decision of the State Board of Education (New Jersey), which denied appellant's request to allow its counselor a stenographer to be present during compelled interviews of district personnel as part of the State Board of Education's comprehensive compliance investigation. Appellant maintained that due process requires that its attorney or stenographer be allowed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school district challenged a decision of the State Board of Education (Board), which denied appellant's request to allow its attorney/stenographer to be present during compelled interviews of district personnel, as part of the Board's comprehensive compliance investigation. Appellant maintained that due process requires that its attorney or stenographer be allowed. The Education Commissioner had responsibility of developing and administering a statewide system for evaluating school systems' performance under N.J. Stat. Ann. 18A:7A-2a. School districts that did not satisfy the basic criteria were to be subject to heightened scrutiny, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. 18A:7A-14a(1). Appellant was placed under heightened scrutiny. Because appellant did not cure deficiencies, it was subject to an independent investigation. On appeal, the court held that appellant was not entitled to have an attorney or stenographer present at the investigative interviews. The court held that no state constitutional right was violated by the denial of assistance of counsel in purely investigatory administrative proceedings, especially where there was no hint of criminal charges. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the State Board of Education, holding that appellant's argument had been rejected in precedent, both civil and criminal. The court held that no state constitutional right was violated by the denial of assistance of counsel in purely investigatory administrative proceedings, especially where there is no hint of criminal charges.

Southern New Jersey Newspapers, Inc. v. Township of Mount Laurel


A-4741-91T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


275 N.J. Super. 465; 646 A.2d 510; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 369


February 24, 1994, Argued  
August 18, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper appealed the decision from the Superior Court, Burlington County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant township in plaintiff's action under the Right to Know Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 47:1A-1 to -4, that sought access to records pertaining to applications for permits for the purchase of handguns and firearms purchaser identification cards.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff newspaper filed a complaint in lieu of prerogative writs, seeking access to records of permits for the sale and purchase of firearms. Plaintiff contended these records were subject to the Right to Know Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 47:1A-1 to -4. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendant township, primarily because an administrative regulation exempted background investigations related to firearm purchases from the Right to Know Law. The trial court utilized the common law public records balancing test to deny access to the permits and firearm purchaser identification cards. On appeal, the court first determined that some documents should not have been included within the category of statutory Right to Know Law documents. Next, the court found that the legislature did not delegate authority to the Superintendent of the Division of State Police to adopt a privacy regulation in connection with implementing the gun control legislation. However, the court upheld the trial court's decision because a strong public interest favored limited disclosure of the records that plaintiff sought. The court granted plaintiff leave to amend pleadings to make more limited inquiries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified the summary judgment in favor of defendant township in plaintiff newspaper's action that sought access to records pertaining to applications for permits for the purchase of handguns and firearms purchaser identification cards. While the court found no authority for an administrative regulation on privacy, it concluded that public interest required protection of the documents.

Saldana v. DiMedio


A-2453-93T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


275 N.J. Super. 488; 646 A.2d 522; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 371


June 7, 1994, Argued  
August 18, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a decision by the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey), that granted summary judgment to defendants, city, building inspector, and director of public works, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:4-2.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a summary judgment in favor of defendants, city, building inspector, and director of public works. Plaintiffs sought to recover damages sustained by their real property as a result of a series of fires. The fires were caused by unauthorized persons in vacant buildings owned by defendant city, and the fires eventually spread to plaintiffs' properties. The court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants on the ground that defendants could not be held liable for the fire damage to plaintiffs' properties under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:4-2. The trial court held that defendants were immune under any theory of liability based upon the failure to enforce the construction code regulations. Plaintiff appealed. The court found that defendant city, in its capacity as a landowner, negligently maintained its buildings in a dangerous condition. Therefore, while defendants were immune from any liability for failure to enforce construction codes, a genuine issue of material fact existed whether defendants negligently maintained their buildings in a dangerous condition. Therefore the case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The decision granting summary judgment was remanded. Although defendants, city, building inspector, and director of public works, were immune from any liability for failure to enforce construction codes, issues of material facts existed whether defendant city in its capacity as a landowner negligently maintained its buildings in a dangerous condition.

Taylor-Segan v. Rajagopal


No. A-387-93T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

August 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, which denied his motion for summary judgment and held that respondent insured did not have to satisfy the verbal threshold requirements set forth in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-8a in order to recover on an auto insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Respondent insured filed an action to recover non-economic losses sustained in an automobile accident. The trial court denied appellant insurer's motion for summary judgment and held that respondent did not have to satisfy the verbal threshold requirements set forth in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-8a. The court reversed the order denying appellant's motion for summary judgment, holding that he could renew the motion to determine if respondent had satisfied the verbal threshold requirements of the statute. The court held that the deemer statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4, was not unconstitutional simply because it treated out-of-state residents differently by requiring them to satisfy the verbal threshold requirements. The court reasoned that the equal protection clause did not require the government to treat all persons identically, and reducing auto insurance costs was a rational basis for the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying appellant insurer's motion for summary judgment, holding that reducing auto insurance costs was a rational basis for the deemer statute, and appellant could renew his motion to determine if respondent insured had satisfied the verbal threshold of the statute.

Baliko v. Stecker


A-1113-93T2F, A-1112-93T2F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

July 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 8, 1994. As Amended August 31, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a union and its members, and plaintiff construction workers challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Morris County (New Jersey), which denied defendants' summary judgment motion on plaintiffs' sexual harassment claims but dismissed all of plaintiffs' other claims.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, female construction workers, filed a lawsuit against defendants, a union and its members, to recover damages from defendants as compensation for defendants' conduct on a picket line. Plaintiffs' complaint alleged claims for intentional infliction of emotional distress, intentional interference with contractual relations and with prospective economic advantage, and sexual harassment. The trial judge dismissed all of plaintiffs' claims except those based on alleged sexual harassment in violation of the New Jersey Law Against Discrimination, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 10:5-1 to -42 (LAD). On appeal, the court held that the conduct plaintiffs alleged, if attributable to defendants, would violate LAD. The court further held that if plaintiffs' allegations were proved at trial, they would permit a trier of fact to find that the conduct was authorized, sanctioned, or ratified by defendant union. Therefore, the court concluded that the trial court was correct in declining to enter summary judgment dismissing plaintiffs' sexual harassment claims. The judgment was affirmed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that denied the summary judgment motion filed by defendants, a union and its members, on plaintiff construction workers' sexual harassment claims but dismissed all of plaintiffs' other claims was affirmed and remanded because plaintiffs' sexual harassment allegations involved a possible violation of state law.

Uncle v. New Jersey Pinelands Com'n


A-3267-92T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


275 N.J. Super. 82; 645 A.2d 788; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 336


May 24, 1994, Submitted  
July 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 22, 1994. As Amended October 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, General Equity Part, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner, in a case transferred from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Burlington County, challenged on due process grounds the validity of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 50-6.63, adopted pursuant to the Pinelands Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:18A-1 to -29, which prohibited appellant from extracting sand and gravel from her property for failure to register such use as a non-conforming use prior to a specified date.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner had operated a sand and gravel extraction operation on her land as a non-conforming use, but had ignored the various government regulations pertaining to such use, which led to its closure. Years later, appellant found a buyer whose purchase was contingent upon the use of the land for sand and gravel extraction. In the meantime, the Pinelands Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:18A-1 to -29, was enacted and, pursuant thereto, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 50-6.63 was adopted, which precluded appellant's former use of the land because she had not registered her non-conforming use by the date designated in the regulation. Appellant sought review of the regulation and the court sustained its validity, finding that it was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious, and it furthered the state interest in preserving sensitive land in its natural condition and promoted compatible agricultural, horticultural, and recreational uses. The court concluded appellant had abandoned her non-conforming use and failed to comply with a reasonable government regulation for its lawful continuance.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the validity of the regulation that prohibited appellant property owner from extracting sand and gravel from her property for failure to register such use as a non-conforming use prior to a specified date. Appellant failed to comply with a reasonable regulation for the lawful continuation of her non-conforming use, thereby rendering such use abandoned.

St. James v. Deparment of Environmental Protection and Energy


A-4077-93T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


275 N.J. Super. 342; 646 A.2d 447; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 361


June 8, 1994, Argued  
July 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Environmental Protection and Energy.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of defendant Department of Environmental Protection and Energy (New Jersey) determining that they were water polluters and refusing to grant a formal hearing unless they first posted the proposed penalty amount in the form of a surety bond, irrevocable letter of credit or trust agreement, or some other form of financial assurance approved by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant state environmental agency issued an order determining that plaintiffs were water polluters and imposing a $ 6,750 penalty. Plaintiffs requested a formal hearing. However, defendant refused to grant a hearing unless plaintiffs first posted the proposed penalty amount in the form of a surety bond, irrevocable letter of credit or trust agreement, or some other form of financial assurance approved by defendant. Plaintiffs appealed the refusal, and the court reversed. The court ruled that a provision requiring the posting of financial security in the amount of the proposed penalty in advance does not satisfy due process unless there is some interim procedure offering the putative violator an opportunity to be heard without posting security after he has received notice of the violation and before assessment of a final order and issuance of the penalty. Because there was no such statutory or administrative regulatory scheme for enforcement of the Water Pollution Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10A-1 et seq., the court ruled that the provision which required posting of financial assurance for payment of the penalty as a condition to obtaining a hearing was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order requiring plaintiffs to post the proposed penalty amount before receiving a formal hearing. The court ruled that the provision requiring prepayment of the proposed penalty was unconstitutional because it did not satisfy the minimum due process requirements that there be a forum where an order's validity can be challenged without penalty.

 

931 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Davidson Bros., Inc. v. D. Katz & Sons, Inc.


A-3718-92T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


274 N.J. Super. 159; 643 A.2d 642; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 278


February 24, 1994, Argued  
June 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, that held a covenant prohibiting the use of property as a supermarket was unenforceable against defendant city, who purchased the property for use as a supermarket in an effort to promote economic development in the downtown area.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation closed one of its supermarket's in the downtown area, and sold the property to a merchant, who then sold the property to defendant city. Defendant then leased the property to another company that operated a supermarket at the location in violation of a covenant prohibiting the operation of a supermarket at that location contained in the contract of sale from plaintiff. The court affirmed the judgment which held that plaintiff's covenant adversely impacted the public interest and therefore was unenforceable. Closing the supermarket caused difficulties and hardships on the downtown citizens, who lost the only opportunity to purchase food at a reasonably close location. Plaintiff's restriction impeded the relocation of another supermarket operation to the downtown area. This obstacle to remediation efforts by defendant city was so contrary to the public policies expressed in the New Jersey Urban Enterprise Zone Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 52:27H-60 to H89, and similar acts, that it represented a scorched earth policy that under the circumstances was unreasonable and unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held plaintiff corporation's covenant prohibiting the use of a property sold to defendant city for a supermarket was unenforceable. The covenant was so contrary to the public policy of promoting growth in the downtown area that the covenant was in these circumstances unreasonable and unenforceable.

 

932 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Craig v. Suburban Cablevision, Inc.


A-4693-92T5F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


274 N.J. Super. 303; 644 A.2d 112; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 299; 65 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 913


October 19, 1993, Submitted  
June 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff third party reprisal claimants appealed an order from the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County (New Jersey), that granted defendant employer's motion for failure to state a claim as to plaintiffs' claim for retaliatory discharge in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. 10:5-12d of the Law Against Discrimination Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff third party reprisal claimants filed suit against defendant employer, under the Law Against Discrimination Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 et seq., claiming that they were discharged in retaliation for their personal relationship with a co-employee who had filed a federal suit for discrimination. The state court dismissed these claims based upon defendant's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim under N.J. Ct. R. 4:6-2(e). The appellate court reversed. The appellate court liberally construed N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-12d, as protecting any person who sought to protect their own or someone else's rights under the Act. It reasoned that to fulfill the Act's broad objectives and overall design, even coworkers or co-employed relatives of an employee who assert rights under the Act have standing to litigate a claim of retaliation. Consequently, the court held that where plaintiffs filed a suit pleading retaliation under § 12d, and having alleged a palpable factual basis for that claim, including a personal relationship to a co-employee who asserted her rights under the Act, plaintiffs could not be nonsuited under rule 4:6-2(e).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that dismissed plaintiff third party reprisal claimants' retaliatory discharge claims under the Law Against Discrimination Act (Act). To fulfill the broad objectives of the Act to protect employees against retaliatory discharge for engaging in protected activities, plaintiffs alleged a palpable factual basis for retaliatory discharge sufficient to prevent a nonsuit for failure to state a claim.

Martin v. Home Ins. Co.


A-0856-92T1, A-1433-92T1, A-6209-91T1, A-6468-91T1 CONSOLIDATED


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


276 N.J. Super. 378; 648 A.2d 213; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 405


April 25, 1994, Argued  
June 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Burlington County and the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs insureds in consolidated actions against defendants multiple insurance companies, and Commissioner of Insurance, challenged an order by the Superior Court of New Jersey, which held that they were not entitled to payment for personal injury claims, because defendants' reimbursement from the Unsatisfied Claim and Judgment Fund denied reimbursement for medical expenses paid to its insured.


OVERVIEW: The court consolidated several actions to answer two questions. First whether defendants' insurance companies were allowed reimbursement from the Unsatisfied Claim and Judgment Fund (UCJF), for medical expenses they paid when their insureds' severely injured a third party in the state of New Jersey. Second, the court was to determine whether an out of state automobile insurer may obtain reimbursement directly from the tortfeasors. The court held that personal injury protection was available to plaintiff insureds, and as such they were also entitled to reimbursement under the UCJ fund. It held that the express language of the applicable statutes mandated that the UCJF reimburse an out-of-state insurer authorized to transact business in New Jersey for Personal Injury Protection benefits paid to an injured party as the result of a New Jersey automobile accident.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Unsatisfied Claim Judgment Fund (UCJF) applied to all in-state plaintiffs, and that they were entitled to benefits.

 

934 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


A-6538-91T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


274 N.J. Super. 137; 643 A.2d 631; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 266


May 3, 1994, Argued  
June 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 27, 1994.
Certification Denied by State v. Johnson, 138 N.J. 265; 649 A.2d 1285; 1994 N.J. LEXIS 1083


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for possession with intent to deliver cocaine, aggravated assault and resisting a police officer in the performance of his duties in the Bergen County Superior Court (New Jersey). He claimed that the trial court erred when it denied his request for a new attorney, it admitted improper evidence, and when it dismissed the case against the co-defendant but refused to sever the remaining cases against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine with the intent to deliver, aggravated assault, and resisting a police officer in the performance of his duties. He claimed that he was entitled to a new trial because the trial court refused to excuse his attorney, sever the trials, dismissed the case against the co-defendant and when it improperly admitted evidence which was obtained by unconstitutional means. The court reviewed defendants' several contentions and found his appeal to be without merit. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's request to permit his counsel to withdraw as trial date was close, and having counsel remain in the case would not in and of itself support an ineffective assistance of counsel claim. The court also held that pursuant to N. J. R. Crim. Proc. 3:15 § 2, the trial court properly balanced the potential prejudice to defendant's due process rights against prosecution's interest in not presenting two trials for the same facts and evidence. The court held that evidence seized from defendant was properly obtained, and the evidence against defendant was overwhelming, so a directed verdict was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession with intent to deliver cocaine, aggravated assault, and resisting a police officer. The court held that defendant's counsel was effective, evidence was properly obtained and admitted, severance was unnecessary and that dismissal of co-defendant was proper. The court also held that evidence was overwhelming so directed verdict was properly denied.

 

935 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Costello v. Bd. of Review


A-2703-92T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


273 N.J. Super. 536; 642 A.2d 1034; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 255


April 19, 1994, Submitted  
May 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1994.
As Corrected August 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Board of Review, Department of Labor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of a decision of appellee agency, which denied unemployment compensation benefits to appellant, holding that he failed to satisfy work requirements when he enrolled in a workfare program as a condition to his receipt of general assistance.


OVERVIEW: A person who received unemployment compensation benefits had to requalify in order to receive such benefits after the benefit year. To requalify, a person had to have engaged in four weeks of employment since the beginning of the immediately preceding benefit year and have earned at least six times his previous weekly benefit amount. Appellee Board of Review, Department of Labor, rejected appellant's argument that he satisfied these requirements through his service for more than four weeks in a workfare program. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that there was no systematic accumulation of funds during periods of employment under workfare programs to provide benefits for periods of unemployment. The court found that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-19(i)(1)(D)(v) excluded services performed in workfare programs from the definition of employment when determining whether the minimum employment requirement for requalification had been met. The court rejected appellant's argument that the exclusion unconstitutionally denied him equal protection of the unemployment compensation law because the law was rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee agency's holding that appellant claimant failed to satisfy work requirements for unemployment compensation when he enrolled in a workfare program as a condition to his receipt of general assistance. The court found that it was reasonable to exclude services performed in workfare programs from the definition of employment when determining whether the minimum employment requirement for requalification had been met.

 

936 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. Club Med Sales


A-6441-91T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


273 N.J. Super. 42; 640 A.2d 1194; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 216


April 12, 1994, Submitted  
May 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tourist sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court, Morris County, New Jersey, which granted the motion for summary judgment in favor of defendants, a Club Med facility, in a suit to recover damages for injuries plaintiff allegedly received after an incident that occurred while she was a guest at defendants' resort.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff tourist challenged a judgment that granted the motion for summary judgment in favor of defendants, a Club Med facility, in a suit to recover damages for injuries plaintiff allegedly received during an incident at defendants' resort. Plaintiff contended that the trial court erred in concluding that the law of the Turks and Caicos applied. The court held that no conflict having been established, the trial court should have applied the law of New Jersey on the issue of the innkeeper's duty. The court noted that defendants' motion remained one for summary judgment. As such, it should have been decided under the standards governing such motions, which required that all inferences of doubt be drawn against the moving party. Plaintiff also contended that the trial court erred in dismissing her claim for punitive damages. The court held that the evidence presented by plaintiff failed to establish that defendants' conduct reached the requisite threshold of wantonly reckless or malicious and that there was any factual issue pertaining to negligence. The court reversed the judgment in part and affirmed in part and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court remanded, affirmed the judgment in part, and reversed in part in favor of plaintiff tourist in a suit to recover damages for injuries plaintiff allegedly received as a guest at defendants, a Club Med facility's resort. The court held that no conflict was established and that the trial court should have applied New Jersey law on the issue of innkeeper's duty, and the evidence presented did not reach the threshold of wantonly reckless.

 

937 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Rinier v. State


A-1871-92T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


273 N.J. Super. 135; 641 A.2d 276; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 225


March 16, 1994, Submitted  
May 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Judgment of the Tax Court of New Jersey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, appealed a judgment of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which granted summary judgment for defendant state in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action, based on its determination that the New Jersey Gross Income Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54A:1-1-54:10-12, did not violate federal equal protection and due process rights by requiring plaintiffs to file a joint state income tax return when filing a joint federal return.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant state, alleging that the New Jersey Gross Income Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54A:1-1-54:10-12, was unconstitutional, as the requirements of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54A:8-31c and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54A:2-1 that married couples were to file joint state income tax returns when filing joint federal returns violated equal protection and due process. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendant, which the court affirmed on appeal. The court held that the rational basis standard applied, because government regulations affecting marriage were not subject to strict scrutiny unless they presented a direct obstacle to marriage. The court held that the tax law did not present a direct obstacle to marriage, but that it did have a rational basis, in that the administrative convenience of requiring the use of the same filing status for state and federal income tax returns made the auditing process for both federal and state taxing agencies more efficient. The court held that the tax law was therefore constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's summary judgment for defendant state in the declaratory judgment action filed by plaintiffs, husband and wife, over the constitutionality of the requirement to file a joint state income tax return when filing a joint federal return, because the administrative convenience of requiring the use of the same filing status for federal and state income taxes was a rational basis for the law.

In re Final Agency Decision by N.J. Dep't of Health


A-4132-92T3, A-342-93T3, A-778-93T3F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


273 N.J. Super. 205; 641 A.2d 1043; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 146


March 14, 1994, Argued  
April 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Department of Health; Superior Court, Chancery Division, Essex County, and Superior Court, Chancery Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospitals challenged orders from the New Jersey Department of Health, the Superior Court Essex County (New Jersey), and the Superior Court Morris County (New Jersey), which found in favor of respondent state-qualified utilization review organizations and held that appellants were required to permit respondents to conduct reviews during 1993.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Health (DOH) informed appellant hospitals how respondent state-qualified utilization review organizations were to function during 1993, and that appellants were expected to collect sufficient funds from payors to pay for respondents' services. Appellants challenged the interpretation of the DOH. The appeals focused on whether appellants were required to permit respondents to conduct reviews during the 1993 transition year and whether appellants were required to pay for those reviews. The court affirmed the interpretation of DOH that respondents were to be used to conduct limited reviews during 1993 only, and affirmed the lower court orders, vacating one order's stay of the payment provision. The court rejected the contentions that the DOH acted arbitrarily. The court found that respondents' system was free from payors' economic interests and that the DOH could use the review information in conjunction with its licensing powers to prevent abuses in the provision of medical services or health care costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgments, which affirmed the interpretation of the Department of Health that respondent state-qualified utilization review organizations were to be used to conduct limited reviews during 1993. The legislature entrusted the Department of Health with the responsibility of selecting the means of achieving statutory policy, so nexus between remedy and goal to be accomplished was peculiarly a matter for administrative competence.
