Dobron v. Board of Trustees, Police and Firemen's Retirement System


A-79-92T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


271 N.J. Super. 506; 638 A.2d 1357; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 94


February 8, 1994, Argued  
March 17, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of Pensions, Department of Treasury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a final decision from the Division of Pensions, Department of Treasury (New Jersey), which denied him retirement benefits through respondent Police and Firemen's Retirement System but ordered all his contributions returned to him. Appellant was a Senior Corrections Officer at a youth facility when he was indicted for several criminal acts arising from his employment.


OVERVIEW: In considering appellant former employee's challenge to the denial of retirement benefits through respondent Police and Firemen's Retirement System, the court rejected appellant's argument that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:16A-11.2 was unconstitutional facially and as applied, because it denied equal protection and due process by automatic forfeiture of pension benefits based on age. The court concluded that the alleged disparate treatment between appellant and another indicted employee was not based on age but on valid distinctions between public employees in service as of the date of retirement and those employees who left office prior to age 55 but sought a deferred retirement at age 55. The court asserted that the statute plainly required that an applicant be an active police officer over age 55 on the date of application for retirement and as of the date when actual retirement commenced, so appellant was not eligible. The court explained that the other indicted employee applied for retirement before his sentencing occurred, while appellant was terminated and applied for pension benefits after his sentence was affirmed on appeal. The court affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Board of Trustees of the Police and Fireman's Retirement System against appellant former employee, because he was plainly ineligible according to the statute, which was constitutional.

Manalapan Realty, L.P. v. Township Committee of Tp. of Manalapan


A-1228-92T1, A-1439-92T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


272 N.J. Super. 1; 639 A.2d 318; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 102


December 7, 1993, Argued  
March 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township planning board appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Monmouth County (New Jersey), which declared a zoning ordinance invalid that prohibited retail stores, like that operated by intervenor retail store, that sold materials outside the premises of plaintiff realty's shopping center, but on the same land as the shopping center. Defendant contended that it had a rational basis for the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff realty owned land on which a shopping center was located. Plaintiff sought approval from defendant township planning board for the expansion of the mall. The expansion included intervenor retail store's indoor and outdoor home improvement center. Defendant adopted a zoning ordinance, which excluded retail stores that sold lumber or building materials outside the premises from the regional commercial shopping center district, as intervenor would have done. Defendant appealed the trial court's judgment that declared the zoning ordinance invalid. Plaintiff and intervenor appealed the litigation expense award amount. The court reversed and found that the zoning ordinance was valid and that intervenor's use was impermissible. The court also reversed the awards of litigation expenses. The court found that the ordinance was presumably valid. Defendant had a rational basis for prohibiting retail stores, like intervenor, from selling materials outside a completely enclosed building because it could have been aesthetically displeasing and was more likely to create fire hazards, litter, and dust. The ordinance was also consistent with the municipality's land use laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that declared defendant township planning board's zoning ordinance invalid. The court found that the ordinance was valid because it was consistent with the municipality's land use laws and defendant had a rational basis for enacting it. Intervenor retail store's method of selling materials outside the indoor premises of plaintiff realty's shopping center was more likely to create fire hazards, litter, and dust.

Patzau v. New Jersey Dept. of Transp.


A-3243-92T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


271 N.J. Super. 294; 638 A.2d 866; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 89


December 14, 1993, Argued  
March 9, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 5, 1994. As Corrected April 19,1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, which found for defendants, department of transportation and municipalities, and denied a declaratory judgment that the Air Safety and Hazardous Zoning Act of 1983, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 6:1-80 to -88, and the New Jersey Airport Safety Act of 1983, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 6:1-89 to -97, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners' requested that the Air Safety and Hazardous Zoning Act of 1983 (Air Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 6:1-80 to -88, and the New Jersey Airport Safety Act of 1983 (Airport Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 6:1-89 to -97, be found unconstitutional regarding an airport construction. Plaintiffs' request was denied in favor of defendants, department of transportation and municipalities. The court affirmed and found the Air Act was not facially unconstitutional or unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs as a taking without just compensation because the lands' intended use did not substantially interfere with plaintiffs' use. There was no showing that plaintiffs were denied the economic use of the land or that their present uses were to be affected. To be unconstitutional as an expenditure of public funds for private purposes under the state constitution, the court had to determine whether the legislative provision of financial aid was for a public purpose and whether the means were consonant with that purpose. Because the legislature determined that an airport was for a public purpose, plaintiffs failed to show that the Airport Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for defendants, department of transportation and municipalities, and against plaintiff property owners, which held that the Air Safety and Hazardous Zoning Act of 1983 and the New Jersey Airport Safety Act of 1983 were not unconstitutional, because there was no showing of a loss of the economic use of the property, and the construction of the airport was for a public purpose.

County of Ocean v. Zekaria Realty, Inc.


A-825-93T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


271 N.J. Super. 280; 638 A.2d 859; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 81


January 7, 1994, Argued  
March 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County for plaintiff county in plaintiff's condemnation action under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 20:3-17 to 20:3-20 and 27:16-1 to 27:16-76.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county granted defendant property owner a variance in exchange for its grant of an easement over land to be used in the future. Defendant continued to use the land. Fourteen years later, plaintiff commenced a condemnation action under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 20:3-17 to 20:3-20 and 27:16-1 to 27:16-76 to obtain the easement without payment. The trial court denied found for plaintiff and denied compensation to defendant. The court affirmed and found that although the grant of the easement was constitutional because it had a rational nexus to the needs created by and benefits conferred upon defendant, the grant was unconstitutional because the easement as not to be used imminently. However, because defendant had not sought to void the transfer within 45 days of the transfer under N.J. Ct. R. 4:49-6, the claim to void the transfer was time-barred. There was no applicable exception under rule 4:49-6(c) because there was no novel constitutional issue and there was no important public, rather than private, clarification or adjudication involved. Because the transfer could not have been voided, the easement belonged to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for plaintiff county in plaintiff's condemnation action and held that defendant property owner's claim for compensation for the taking of an easement was time-barred, even though the initial taking was unconstitutional. Defendant failed to seek to void the transfer with 45 days of the transfer.

State in Interest of A.L.


A-501-93T1F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


271 N.J. Super. 192; 638 A.2d 814; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 79


November 17, 1993, Argued  
February 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Cumberland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Cumberland County, which denied his motion for reconsideration of the waiver under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-26 and N.J. R. Civ. P. 5:22-2, and held that the portion of the waiver that placed the burden on appellant to demonstrate the probability of rehabilitation prior to reaching the age of 19 was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was charged with first-degree attempted murder, third-degree aggravated assault, and fourth-degree criminal mischief. Respondent state moved for involuntary waiver, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-26 and N.J. R. Civ. P. 5:22-2. The trial court found granted the involuntary waiver. Appellant sought reconsideration of the waiver, which was denied by the Family Part judge who held that the portion of the waiver statute placing the burden on a juvenile to demonstrate the probability of rehabilitation prior to reaching the age of 19 was unconstitutional because it violated the right against self-incrimination. The court affirmed the grant of the waiver but held that the waiver statute was constitutional because it neither compelled a juvenile to testify at a waiver hearing nor required an admission of guilt by the juvenile and that the offer of more lenient treatment, remaining in the Family Part, in exchange for the juvenile's admission of guilt and remorse, especially where the admission has no adverse legal consequences because the juvenile is completely immunized, does not violate the juvenile's self-incrimination rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the involuntary waiver against appellant juvenile but held that the involuntary waiver statute was constitutional because it provided immunity fir any testimony and therefore, did not violate the Fifth Amendment's protection against compelled self-incrimination.

Slowinski v. County of Monmouth


A-6593-91T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


272 N.J. Super. 264; 639 A.2d 1112; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 140


December 15, 1993, Argued  
January 24, 1994, Decided; April 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Granted February 17, 1994. 1 Reargued March 2, 1994.


1 We granted plaintiffs' motion for reconsideration in which their counsel pointed out a mistake in our quoting of a portion of the Tinton Falls Turnpike Act and what constituted at least a lack of clarity in our description of where the "actual roads went" in colonial times. This opinion has been issued to replace our opinion of January 24, 1994, which we have directed the clerk of the court to withdraw.


PRIOR HISTORY: January 24, 1994, Decided. On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which granted summary judgment to defendant county, which recognized ownership by defendant of 33 feet on each side of the center lane of Route 537 that ran in front of plaintiffs' home.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owners filed an action to enjoin defendant county from implementing a road-widening of the street in front of plaintiffs' home. Defendant was granted summary judgment because a 66 foot right of way granted in 1765 on which plaintiffs' home encroached, was still in effect. Plaintiffs had asserted the need for a permit to encroach. The court affirmed and found that an unconstitutional taking of plaintiffs' property had not occurred, due to the fact that they were aware of the encroachment prior to their purchase of the home and adjusted the price accordingly. The court noted that due to the plaintiffs' adjustment in sales price they were equitably estopped to demand compensation for any alleged taking. The plaintiffs argued that the roadway was not where the recorded, legal description in the grant of the right of way described. However, the court rejected this issue because the roadway was an ancient road and followed the same pathway for 200 years, and its precise location would not affect the width of the right of way to which the public remained entitled. Further, the court found that the right of way was not lost by non-use or failure to pave its full width.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant county because the 66 foot right of way, which was granted in 1765 and upon which plaintiff owners' home encroached, was still in effect. No unconstitutional taking of plaintiffs' property occurred because they were aware of the encroachment prior to purchasing the home and adjusted the price accordingly.

State v. Baker


Nos. A-1550-91T4, A-824-92T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed post-conviction relief petitions relating to his convictions for second degree robbery, attempted kidnapping, and kidnapping, and the resentencing of his convictions on appeal, from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant were indicted for second degree robbery, attempted kidnapping, criminal restraint, kidnapping, and aggravated sexual assault. Defendant was convicted of all charges, except the trial court merged his conviction for aggravated sexual assault into his conviction for kidnapping. Defendant's convictions were affirmed, but remanded for reconsideration of the sentence. Defendant petitioned for post-conviction relief. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for second degree robbery, attempted kidnapping, and kidnapping, and the resentencing of his convictions on appeal, and denied post-conviction relief, because defendant received effective assistance of counsel, was not denied due process by his co-defendant's lower sentence, and defendant's lesser sentence was properly increased to the statutory minimum.

Macedonian Orthodox Church v. Planning Bd. of Tp. of Randolph


A-3314-92T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


269 N.J. Super. 562; 636 A.2d 96; 1994 N.J. Super. LEXIS 14


November 30, 1993, Argued  
January 13, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township planning board challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, which set aside the denial of a conditional use variance to respondent church.


OVERVIEW: Respondent church sought approval from appellant township planning board to construct on its property an all-purpose building that was larger than and in a different location from a proposed building that was approved 13 years earlier. Appellant denied the conditional use variance. The court held that not all legislation that impeded the exercise of religion was unconstitutional if no less restrictive means existed to achieve some overriding state interest. The court added that appellant had considerable latitude in reviewing the application and its decision was presumptively valid. The court held that appellant did not deny respondent an opportunity to engage in social and religious events, but merely placed constraints upon the building's size and location. The court held that the trial judge erred in determining that appellant's review of respondent's application should have been limited to site plan approval only. The court held that appellant acted within its discretion in reviewing the application anew under the conditional use ordinance. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the issue for reconsideration of the issue using the proper standard of review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that set aside appellant township planning board's denial of respondent church's conditional use variance and remanded the issue for reconsideration because appellant was within its discretion in requiring that respondent get conditional use approval as well as site plan approval.

Ballantyne House Associates v. City of Newark


A-1474-92T5, A-1485-92T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


269 N.J. Super. 322; 635 A.2d 551; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 893


September 28, 1993, Argued  
December 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city of Newark sought review from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County in which respondent housing corporations were awarded summary judgment in an action alleging appellant breached its tax abatement agreements with them by terminating garbage collection.


OVERVIEW: Respondents were limited dividend housing corporations and associations who entered into tax abatement agreements with appellant city of Newark relieving them of the obligation to pay property taxes but requiring them to pay an annual service charge for municipal services upon building of homes in blighted areas. When the agreements were executed, city was required by municipal ordinance to provide garbage collection services to respondents' facilities. However, the ordinance was repealed. Six years after city stopped collecting garbage respondents filed an action against city. The trial court granted partial summary judgment to respondents and ordered city to pick up their garbage within 30 days. The court affirmed holding that garbage collection was a municipal service which the city had contracted to provide for the duration of the tax abatement agreements. The court also reversed that portion granting garbage collection within 30 days without full consideration of all relevant facts and remanded for a complete record on the issue.


OUTCOME: Order granting partial judgment to respondents was affirmed, holding that the trial court properly construed the tax abatement agreements to require appellant city to provide garbage collection. Order stating that respondents were entitled to specific performance within 30 days notice without consideration of all relevant circumstances was reversed. Claims were timely and brought within contractual time limitations.

Rutgers, State University of New Jersey v. Grad Partnership


A-193-92T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


269 N.J. Super. 142; 634 A.2d 1053; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 874


November 8, 1993, Submitted  
December 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff university sought review of a judgment from the Middlesex County Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed its complaint against defendants on the ground that under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-1.1, plaintiff's suit was untimely.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff university sought review after the trial court dismissed its complaint against defendants pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-1.1. The issue on appeal was whether the ancient, and almost dead, doctrine of nullum tempus occurrit regi (no time runs against the state) barred defendants' reliance upon § 2A:14-1.1. The trial judge concluded that the doctrine applied only to statutes of limitations, that § 2A:14-1.1 was a statute of repose, and that, in any event, nullum tempus was no longer favored. The court agreed that the doctrine of nullum tempus was no longer favored. However, the court disagreed with the finding that the doctrine was not applicable to plaintiff at the time it filed its complaint. Specifically, there was no basis for limiting the doctrine to only what might be characterized as pure statutes of limitation. Moreover, the court found that the characterization of § 2A:14-1.1 as a statute of repose was not necessarily accurate. Therefore, the court held that defendants' reliance upon § 2A:14-1.1 was precluded. Accordingly, the judgment was reversed and the case remanded.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of plaintiff university's complaint was reversed and the case remanded because the doctrine of nullum tempus occurrit regi was applicable at the time plaintiff filed its complaint, therefore defendants' reliance upon the cited statute was precluded.

 

949 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Mc Garrah v. State, Dept. of Law and Public Safety, Div. of Motor Vehicles


A-5155-91T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


268 N.J. Super. 577; 634 A.2d 139; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 863


September 28, 1993, Argued  
December 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 27, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Decision of the Director of the Division of Motor Vehicles


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Director of the Division of Motor Vehicles (New Jersey) that refused to release the suspension on appellant's driver's license because he had not paid the insurance surcharge he was ordered to pay after being convicted of violating N.J. Stat. Ann. 39:4-50.4a.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of violating N.J. Stat. Ann. 39:4-50.4a. and as part of his sentence, he was required to pay a $ 3,000.00 insurance surcharge before his suspended driver's license would be reinstated. Appellant claimed this requirement was unconstitutional because he was poor and could not pay it. He claimed it violated his due process rights since it meant that his license would be suspended longer than a rich person's license would be suspended. The court disagreed and affirmed the decision not to release his license until after the surcharge was paid. The court found his due process rights were not violated and that a hearing was unnecessary because there were no material facts in dispute.


OUTCOME: A decision that appellant's driver's license would remain suspended until he paid the insurance surcharge he was ordered to pay as part of his sentence was affirmed. The court found that appellant's due process rights were not violated and that no hearing was required because there were no material facts in dispute.

Intek Auto Leasing, Inc. v. Zetes Microtech Corp.

Morgan v. Union County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders


A-2004-91T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


268 N.J. Super. 337; 633 A.2d 985; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 833; 10 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1676


October 12, 1993, Argued  
November 16, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 6, 1993. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, Law Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff director of buildings and grounds instituted an action in the Superior Court, Union County (New Jersey), and contended that he was wrongfully terminated by reason of his political affiliation. Following the completion of plaintiff's case, the court granted defendant county board's motion for an involuntary dismissal. Plaintiff appealed and defendants cross-appealed. At issue was also the question of punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff director of buildings and grounds contended that he was wrongfully terminated, via constructive discharge, from his position by reason of his political affiliation. Plaintiff sought punitive damages as well as injunctive and declaratory relief. Giving plaintiff the benefit of all favorable testimony and legitimate inferences, the jury could reasonably have found that defendants conspired to deprive plaintiff of his constitutional rights. The trial court committed error when it aborted trial and dismissed plaintiff's claim for punitive damages. The trial court acted correctly when it granted defendant's motion for an involuntary dismissal. Plaintiff presented a prima facie case against defendants. Accepting as true all evidence that supported plaintiff's claim, the court found that reasonable minds could have differed regarding whether defendants entered into an unlawful conspiracy to deprive plaintiff of his civil rights. The events created a substantial enough possibility of a conspiracy to have defeated defendants' motions for an involuntary dismissal. Therefore, sufficient evidence of an evil motive required submission of the question of punitive damages to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court acted correctly when it granted defendant county board's motion for an involuntary dismissal. There was sufficient evidence of an evil motive to have required submission of the question of punitive damages to the jury. The dismissal of plaintiff's claims for constitutional violations and for tortious interference was reversed and the matter remanded for retrial.

State v. Saez


A-4035-90T1, A-4189-90T1, A-4347-90T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


268 N.J. Super. 250; 633 A.2d 551; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 827


April 19, 1993, Argued  
November 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which convicted defendants for numerous drug-related offenses, which included maintaining or operating a controlled dangerous substance production facility, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-4, and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7.


OVERVIEW: Contending that a police officer's observations of illegal conduct through the common wall of a basement at the invitation of a tenant informant constituted an unconstitutional warrantless search, defendants appealed their convictions for various crimes related to the possession and manufacture of controlled substances in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-4, -10a(1), -10, -5b(2), -7, -5b(3). The court affirmed the judgments of conviction because even though defendants had a reasonable expectation of privacy in their premises, the officer's warrantless search did not violate either U.S. Const. amend. IV or N.J. Const. art. I., para. 7, because the invasion of privacy was occasioned by the private action of the informant. The court held that there was sufficient evidence that defendants operated a controlled dangerous substance production facility because "rerocking" cocaine fell within N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-2's definition of "manufacture." The court held that an uncertified school zone map was properly authenticated for the purpose of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 by reference to an ordinance which adopted the map.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction in all respects. The court held that the observation by a police officer of illegal conduct through a basement common wall at the invitation of a tenant informant was not an unconstitutional warrantless search because the officer's observations went no further than that of the informant's in infringing upon defendants' privacy.

State, Dept. of Environmental Protection and Energy v. Dopp


A-9-92T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


268 N.J. Super. 165; 632 A.2d 1270; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 817


September 21, 1993, Submitted  
November 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner's husband sought review of a decision by the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Somerset County (New Jersey), which ordered appellant to complete applications required by respondent Department of Environmental Protection and Energy and to pay a fine in connection with the Freshwater Wetlands Protection Act.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Environmental Protection and Energy issued a notice of violation to appellant landowner's husband for a "stream pond" that required a permit under the Freshwater Wetlands Protection Act (FWPA). When appellant failed to take any action, respondent issued an order and penalty assessment. Appellant did not request a hearing. Respondent sought injunctive relief and a monetary assessment. Defendant sought review of the lower court's order that defendant complete applications required by respondent's order and imposing a fine. The court affirmed the decision, holding that defendant lacked standing to assert that the FWPA was unconstitutional because appellant's outcome in the litigation did not depend on the constitutional question. The court held that the verification of the complaint could be made on information and belief. The court held defendant had a right to contest the validity of the order at an administrative hearing but, having failed to do so, was barred from challenging the factual predicates underlying it. The court held that neither equitable estoppel nor the doctrine of laches barred respondent from enforcing the order against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that appellant landowner's husband had to complete applications and pay a fine in connection with the Freshwater Wetlands Protection Act (FWPA) because appellant lacked standing to challenge the FWPA and neither equitable estoppel nor the doctrine of laches barred respondent Department of Environmental Protection and Energy from enforcing the order against appellant.

Buckwald v. Board of Review


A-6629-91T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


267 N.J. Super. 617; 632 A.2d 548; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 807


October 13, 1993, Argued  
November 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Board of Review, Department of Labor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of respondent Board of Review, Department of Labor (New Jersey), that affirmed a board decision that appellant was not eligible for unemployment compensation benefits pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-19(m)(1) because he was a corporate officer of his employer and owned more than 5 percent of the stock of his corporate employer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was a manager and vice president of his corporate employer. The property of the employer was extensively damaged by fire, and operations temporality stopped. Appellant applied for unemployment compensation benefits. Respondent Board of Review, Department of Labor, affirmed the denial of benefits. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed. The court found that appellant was ineligible for benefits by reason of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-19(m)(1). Under § 43:21-19(m)(1), an officer of a corporation or a person that owned more than 5 percent of the stock or debt interest of a corporate employer was ineligible during the term of office or ownership. Appellant was both an officer and an owner in excess of 5 percent. Appellant contended that § 43:21-19(m)(1) deprived him of equal protection of the laws because it treated him differently than other claimants without a reason. The court found that there was a rational basis for the disparate treatment and held that § 43:21-19(m)(1) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Board of Review, Department of Labor. The court found that appellant employee was not eligible for benefits because he was a corporate officer and owned more than 5 percent of the stock of his employer, and he had applied for benefits for weeks during his term of office or ownership in the corporation. The court rejected appellant's argument that he was unconstitutionally denied a property right.

Town of Secaucus v. Hackensack Meadowlands Development Com'n


A-2460-88T2, A-246-89T2, A-5430-90T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


267 N.J. Super. 361; 631 A.2d 959; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 773


June 15, 1993, Argued  
August 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Hackensack Meadowlands Development Commission (A-2460-88T2 and A246-89T2) and Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County (A-5430-90T2).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, municipalities, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, that dismissed plaintiffs' objections to a tax scheme based on res judicata.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, municipalities, filed suit challenging a tax system administered by defendant, a development commission. The tax system allocated equally among the various municipalities the burden of development of the Hackensack Meadowlands. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' complaint. The court reversed. The court held that res judicata did not bar plaintiffs' complaint. The court reviewed the merits of the complaint. The court held that the prospective application of the amendment of the Hackensack Meadowlands Reclamation and Development Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:17, which was designed to eliminate the compounding effect of the tax system, was proper and evidenced by legislative intent. The court held that the tax system was not arbitrary, but rather applied the same standards to all municipalities. The court held payments made in lieu of real property taxes were not required to be considered in calculating tax sharing obligations. The court also held that the involvement of federal agencies for the preservation of wetlands did not preempt regulatory authority from defendant. The court held the marshaled wetlands were of insignificant acreage in light of the whole project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that dismissed plaintiffs' claim because res judicata did not bar the action. The court reviewed the merits of plaintiffs' claim and held that the tax system was proper where the system was not arbitrary, but rather applied the same standards to all taxed municipalities.

State v. Ball


A-6040-88T1, A-6041-88T1, A-6043-88T1, A-6050-88T1, A-6051-88T1, A-6052-88T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


268 N.J. Super. 72; 632 A.2d 1222; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 798


March 10, 1993, Argued; March 10, 1993, Submitted  
August 6, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 4, 1993. As Corrected February 14, 1994.
As Corrected February 14, 1994.
Certification granted State v. Bassi, 135 N.J. 304, 639 A.2d 304, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 119 (1994)
Certification granted State v. Harvan, 135 N.J. 304, 639 A.2d 304, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 124 (1994)
Certification granted State v. Hurtuk, 135 N.J. 305, 639 A.2d 304, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 110 (1994)
Affirmed by State v. Ball, 141 N.J. 142, 661 A.2d 251, 1995 N.J. LEXIS 522 (1995)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendants sought review of their convictions by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, of conspiracy to commit racketeering and racketeering in violation of the New Jersey "Little RICO" statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:41-2(c), (d), bribery, theft of services, falsifying and tampering with public records, forgery, and the unlawful engagement in the business of solid waste collection and disposal.


OVERVIEW: Defendants bribed defendant public officials for "permission," via illegal licenses, to dump debris obtained in New York by defendant truck company at illegal dumping sites in New Jersey. An accident triggered an investigation, indictments, and a trial court conviction for violations of, among other charges, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2c:41-1, New Jersey's Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations (Little RICO) statute. The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences. The court found that, although not limited to legitimate enterprises, the "enterprise" element of Little RICO was satisfied if there existed a group of people that provided or implemented the common purpose to commit two or more predicate acts. The predicate acts did not have to be related. The court found that a conspirator did not need to know all aspects of the conspiracy or knowledge of all its participants. The court held that the "pattern of racketeering activity" as defined in Little RICO was not constitutionally vague, and that defendant's sentences were fair and comported with existing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions under New Jersey's Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations (RICO) statute. The court held that the defendants' purpose was to commit at least two predicate acts. The court found that the "enterprise" and "pattern of racketeering activity" elements found in the statute were not constitutionally vague, and that defendant's sentences were fair and comported with sentencing guidelines.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the tax court's award of counsel fees and costs to defendant township pursuant to N.J. Stat. State v. Jimenez


A-3679-92T1F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


266 N.J. Super. 560; 630 A.2d 348; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 730


June 15, 1993, Submitted  
July 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 10, 1993.
Certification denied by State v. Jimenez, 134 N.J. 559, 636 A.2d 518, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1390 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the Law Division's order granting defendant's petition for post-conviction relief is reversed and the mandatory term of parole ineligibility is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the order of the Superior Court, Hudson County (New Jersey), which granted defendant's petition for post-conviction relief and vacated the remainder of his parole ineligibility term imposed under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 after defendant was convicted of drug charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of drug charges and sought post-conviction relief. The trial court granted relief and vacated the remainder of defendant's parole ineligibility term imposed under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. The court reversed, finding that the prosecutor did not abuse his discretion when he refused to waive the mandatory minimum term and that the guidelines adopted by the attorney general satisfied constitutional standards because a prosecutor could generally condition a post-verdict waiver on a defendant's cooperation. The court held that the guideline which allowed the prosecution to waive the mandatory minimum if the defendant cooperated was facially constitutional and was constitutional as applied. The court found that the prosecutor's insistence on defendant's cooperation as a prerequisite to waiver of the mandatory sentence was not unreasonable. The court also held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-12 and the guidelines that were later adopted by the attorney general and the county prosecutors were not ex post facto.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting defendant's petition for post-conviction relief and reinstated the mandatory term of parole ineligibility because the prosecution's failure to waive the mandatory minimum where defendant did not cooperate was constitutional, was not unreasonable, and was not ex post facto as applied.

New Jersey Educ. Ass'n v. New Jersey Public Employment Relations Com'n


A-4412-91T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


266 N.J. Super. 66; 628 A.2d 789; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 699


June 14, 1993, Argued  
July 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Public Employment Relations Commission.



DISPOSITION: PERC's decision denying appellant's petition to amend is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state education association sought review of the decision of appellee Public Employment Relations Commission (New Jersey) which denied appellant's petition to amend. Appellant argued that appellee misinterpreted the leading case, and argued that the case did not dispense with the prerequisite that a nonmember object in order to obtain a deduction from his or her fee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state education association sought review of the decision by appellee Public Employment Relations Commission's (PERC) denial of appellant's demand that PERC amend regulations adopted in 1987. Appellant demanded an amendment requiring that political-activity deductions only be required for nonmembers who object. Under the existing regulation the representative body was required to deduct the political-activity portion of the fee as to all nonmembers, not just those nonmembers who affirmatively object. PERC denied the petition on the ground that the regulation was required under the leading case. The lower court decision was affirmed. The court held that the leading case was clear, and that appellee's regulation was a reasonable implementation of that holding. The regulations at issue departed from the literal language of the statute at issue. However, the statute must now be read as construed by the court. The legislature had not sought to amend the law to require nonmembers to object, despite the lapse of six years since the adoption of the regulation implementing the decision.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision that denied appellant state education association's petition to amend was affirmed. The court held that the leading case was clear, and appellee Public Employment Relations Commission's regulation at issue was a reasonable implementation of that holding.

C.I.C. Corp. v. Township of East Brunswick


A-6131-91T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


266 N.J. Super. 1; 628 A.2d 753; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 694


June 1, 1993, Argued  
July 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 28, 1993.
Certification granted C.I.C. Corp. v. Township of E. Brunswick, 134 N.J. 560, 636 A.2d 518, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1431 (1993)
Affirmed by C.I.C. Corp. v. Township of E. Brunswick, 135 N.J. 121, 638 A.2d 812, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 184 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners and operators of cigarette vending machines, sought review of the ordinance banning cigarette vending machines enacted by respondent township. Plaintiffs alleged that ban was unconstitutional in violation of equal protection and was preempted by state statute which prohibited sales of cigarettes to minors.


OVERVIEW: Respondent township enacted an ordinance banning cigarette vending machines. Plaintiffs, owners and operators of cigarette vending machines, challenged the legality of the ordinance on the grounds of preemption and equal protection. Plaintiffs claimed the area of law had been preempted by the legislature when it enacted N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:170-51 which prohibited the sale of cigarettes to minors and N.J. Stat. Ann. 18A:36-32 which prohibited vending machines on school property. Plaintiff further contended that a less restrictive means of preventing unrestricted access to vending machines could have been enacted. The court reversed and remanded for entry of a final judgment dismissing the complaint. The prohibition on the vending machines was rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest to satisfy equal protection and substantive due process concerns.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for the entry of a final judgment dismissing the complaint because preventing access to cigarettes on the part of minors was a legitimate governmental concern and a valid objective of respondent township. Whether the means chosen may be more encompassing than plaintiffs, owners and operators of cigarette vending machines, deemed necessary, was not a proper issue for the court.

Non-Profit Affordable Housing Network of New Jersey v. New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing


A-489-91T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


265 N.J. Super. 475; 627 A.2d 1153; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 701


April 5, 1993, Submitted  
June 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public advocate sought review of the regulations enacted by respondent Council on Affordable Housing (New Jersey), which governed the crediting of a region's low and moderate income housing.


OVERVIEW: Respondent council on affordable housing promulgated regulations under the Fair Housing Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:27D-301 et seq.(the Act) to determine the fair share of the region's low and moderate income housing. Appellant public advocate contended that regulations enacted to regulate credits were violative of the Act as they did not include affordability as part of the standard for determining whether a unit could be used for credit. The court examined the rule regarding the validity of an administrative agency's regulations and concluded that the regulations enacted were not ultra vires. Appellant also contended that amendments to the Act which took place in 1993 were unconstitutional. Because the record was not sufficient to permit the court to review the dilutionary effect of the amendments, the court remanded the matter to respondent to develop a complete and full record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the regulations enacted by respondent council on affordable housing because they were not ultra vires; however, the court remanded the case to respondent for further development of the record prior to determining whether amendments to housing statute were dilutionary.

 

964 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Commissioner of Insurance's Issuance of Orders A-92-189 and A-92-212


A-6126-91T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


274 N.J. Super. 385; 644 A.2d 616; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 941


April 7, 1993, Argued  
June 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Commissioner of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers sought to overturn a regulation, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 3-20.5, promulgated by respondent Commissioner of Insurance (New Jersey) under the Excess Profits Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:29A-5.6 to -5.16, which implemented a legislative mandate that insurers not pass through to insureds the cost of erasing an insurance association fund deficit.


OVERVIEW: The Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990 (the FAIR Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 et seq., imposed surtaxes and assessments on insurers to pay half the cost of erasing the deficit of an insurance association fund but required that insurers not pass these charges through to their insureds. Respondent Commissioner of Insurance promulgated a regulation, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 3-20.5, under the Excess Profit Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:29A-5.6 to -5.16, which excluded the surcharges from expenses that the insurers could deduct in calculating their profits. Appellant insurers challenged the regulation. The court affirmed, stating that it would not substitute its judgment regarding the wisdom of an administrative action for the agency's judgment as long as the action was statutorily authorized and reasonable. The court read the FAIR Act and the Excess Profit Law together and held that respondent clearly had both the mandate and the authority to pass the regulation, which was not a confiscatory taking because it allowed the surtaxes and assessments to be treated as expenses upon a showing that such treatment was necessary to earn a constitutionally adequate rate of return.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the validity of a regulation that respondent Commissioner of Insurance had promulgated under the Excess Profit Act in order to carry out the mandate of the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990 to prevent insurers from passing surtaxes and assessments through to their insureds, because the regulation was statutorily authorized.

State v. De Luzio


A-3076-88T4, A-3078-88T4, A-3079-88T4, A-3080-88T4, A-3295-88T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


274 N.J. Super. 101; 643 A.2d 609; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 945


January 13, 1993, Argued  
June 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 6, 1994.
Certification denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Sanders, 134 N.J. 564, 636 A.2d 521, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1376 (1993)
Certification granted State v. Sanders, 134 N.J. 564, 636 A.2d 521, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1381 (1993)
Certification denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Sanders, 134 N.J. 564, 636 A.2d 521, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1382 (1993)
Affirmed by State v. DeLuzio, 136 N.J. 363, 643 A.2d 535, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 511 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.
State v. Sanders, 107 N.J. 609, 527 A.2d 442, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 341 (1987)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions after a jury trial in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County. Defendants were convicted of numerous charges arising out of their involvement in a complex pyramid scheme. Defendant operators were convicted of promoting gambling, theft, conspiracy, and related offenses. Defendant police officers were convicted of promoting gambling and official misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operators ran an investment company. The state alleged that the company was a fraudulently operated pyramid scheme that constituted an illegal lottery in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:37-2. Defendants, operators and police officers, were convicted by a jury of offenses including promoting gambling, theft, conspiracy, and official misconduct. Defendants argued that their convictions for running an illegal lottery should be reversed and the court agreed, holding that a pyramid scheme, however fraudulently run, was not a "lottery" within the meaning of the statute. In reversing defendant operators' gambling related convictions, the court ruled that given the judge's instructions in the case, the court could not conclude that the jury found defendants guilty on any basis other than their wrongdoing in connection with a lottery. Defendant operators' other convictions were affirmed. The convictions of defendant police officers, who provided security for the investment company, were reversed because they could not be convicted of official misconduct in allowing and facilitating the conduct of an illegal lottery where a pyramid scheme did not constitute an illegal lottery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed each of defendants' gambling related convictions on the ground that a pyramid scheme did not constitute a lottery and that the indictments and jury instructions referred to running an illegal lottery The court affirmed most of the remaining convictions, but remanded with respect to one defendant for further proceedings relating to the claim that he was denied his right to counsel.

 

966 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Property Owners and Managers Ass'n v. Mayor and Town Council of Parsippany-Troy Hills


A-2287-91T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


264 N.J. Super. 538; 624 A.2d 1381; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 191


April 19, 1993, Argued  
May 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners and managers association sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Morris County, New Jersey, which upheld the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:66-1b giving municipalities discretionary power to limit solid waste collection service to curbside collection along public streets.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners and managers association requested that defendant township provide solid waste collection services at each apartment complex curbsides or from dumpsters inside the complexes. All of the streets within the complexes were privately owned and many did not meet municipal specifications. In an oral decision, the trial court required defendant to provide collection to plaintiffs and left the method of collection to the discretion of defendant. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:66-1b became effective the next day, and the trial court allowed plaintiffs to attack the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court upheld the statute, and the court affirmed. The court found that the statute did not exclude any class of residents from receiving municipal solid waste collection. The statute simply did not mandate the customized type of service requested by plaintiffs. The classification between collection on public and private streets was rationally related to the legitimate governmental objective of safety and cost containment, and the evidence failed to establish that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court, holding that the challenged statute giving municipalities discretionary power to limit solid waste collection service to curbside collection along public streets was constitutional because the statute did not exclude any class of residents from services and the restriction was rationally related to the legitimate governmental objectives of safety and cost containment.

 

967 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Property Owners and Managers Ass'n v. Town Council of Parsippany-Troy Hills


A-4815-91T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


264 N.J. Super. 523; 624 A.2d 1372; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 180


April 19, 1993, Argued  
May 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 27, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, township and mayor, challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, which declared unconstitutional Township of Parsippany-Troy Hills, N.J., Ordinance 91:10, a tax rebate ordinance requiring members of plaintiff property owners and managers association to pay their tenants a portion of any tax refunds or reductions received.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, township and mayor, enacted Township of Parsippany-Troy Hills, N.J., Ordinance 91:10 requiring members of plaintiff property owners and managers association to refund to residents any tax refunds or reductions received. The court affirmed the order declaring the ordinance unconstitutional. The purpose of the ordinance was the prevention of windfall profits to property owners, but there was no means of determining whether such profits existed. The ordinance took money belonging to property owners and distributed it to tenants without establishing a basis to support tenant's right to the funds. Without the structure of rent control, there was no way of knowing whether property owners were receiving sufficient rent to provide a profit. The court held that the ordinance standing without a rent control ordinance required a legislative or state constitutional source for the power. The statement that tenants paid property taxes through rent was merely an abstract principle, and it did not prove the foundation necessary for municipal action. The court was not shown why invoking such municipal police powers were reasonably required by local conditions in defendant township.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order declaring appellant township's tax rebate ordinance unconstitutional because without a rent control ordinance in place there was no other legislative or state constitutional source for the power exercised in the ordinance.

Adams v. Keystone Ins. Co.


A-3937-91T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


264 N.J. Super. 367; 624 A.2d 1008; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 182


February 17, 1993, Argued  
May 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which granted defendant's motion for summary judgment in an action seeking personal injury protection benefits under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured while traveling in a vehicle in New Jersey. The vehicle was registered and insured in Delaware. Plaintiff sought personal injury protection benefits from defendant over and above the amount provided in defendant's insurance policy issued to plaintiff. Under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4, any insurer authorized to do business in New Jersey was required to include New Jersey personal injury protection coverage in policies sold in another state whenever the vehicle insured under the policy was operated in New Jersey. The court held that the statute applied and provided additional personal injury protection benefits to plaintiff. The court cited the legitimate interest of New Jersey in its insurance scheme. There was no due process violation, because in a multistate transaction such as the one at issue, New Jersey had a legitimate interest in protecting its citizens, thus making N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:28-1.4 constitutional.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendants was reversed, because the New Jersey statutes required out-of-state insurers to provide personal injury protection benefits meeting the requirements of New Jersey statutes.

State v. Alexander


A-2951-90T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


264 N.J. Super. 102; 624 A.2d 48; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 149


February 10, 1993, Argued  
April 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 10, 1993.
Certification granted State v. Alexander, 134 N.J. 564, 636 A.2d 522, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1364 (1993)
Affirmed by, Modified by State v. Alexander, 136 N.J. 563, 643 A.2d 996, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 629 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey), which convicted him for the offenses of possession of cocaine, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-10a(1), possession of cocaine with intent to distribute it, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5a(1) and 5b(3)), and being the leader of a narcotics trafficking network, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of cocaine, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-10a(1), possession of cocaine with intent to distribute it, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5a(1) and 5b(3)), and being the leader of a narcotics trafficking network, a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-3. On appeal, the court reversed in part and held that the jury instruction regarding defendant's violation of the kingpin statute, § 2C:35-3, was improper because it did not permit the jury to determine whether defendant's status and activities warranted the punishment reserved for a leader of a narcotics trafficking network. The instruction given by the trial court permitted conviction under § 2C:35-3 merely if defendant initiated, supervised, financed, or managed a two-person conspiracy to produce or sell any quantity of the specified illegal drugs. The instruction failed to state, and further to define for the jury, that the prosecution was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was an "upper echelon member" of a drug organization, not just a street-level vendor. The court remanded and affirmed defendant's remaining convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction as the leader of a narcotics trafficking network. The court found that the jury instruction given by the trial court regarding the kingpin statute was improper because it failed to state, and further to define for the jury, that the prosecution had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was an "upper echelon member" of a drug organization, not just a street-level vendor.

 

970 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Murray v. Lawson


A-175-91T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


264 N.J. Super. 17; 624 A.2d 3; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 135


February 18, 1993, Submitted  
April 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Union County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant anti-abortionist protestors sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, which entered a permanent injunction against pickets or demonstrations by appellant and its cohorts within 300 feet of respondent physician's residence, and dismissed respondent's damages claim for picketing in front of his residence in an harassing manner.


OVERVIEW: Respondent physician filed suit against appellant anti-abortionist protestors, seeking damages and injunctive relief for picketing in an harassing manner outside respondent's residence. The trial court dismissed the damages claim but entered a permanent injunction against pickets or demonstrations by appellant and its cohorts within 300 feet of respondent's residence. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that there was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine because the trial court had the inherent equitable power to issue the injunction to protect the right to residential privacy under either state or federal concepts of police power without a finding that appellant had committed a crime or tort. The injunction was content-neutral in intent and was a proper regulation because there was a significant government interest at stake, despite the 300-foot restriction on expression of a particular viewpoint. The restriction preserved ample alternative channels of communication at the clinics where respondent performed abortions, and was narrowly tailored because the problem that was remedied, intrusion into residential tranquility, was created by the picketing itself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that entered a permanent injunction against pickets by appellant anti-abortionist protestors and its cohorts within 300 feet of respondent physician's residence. The court held that the trial court had inherent equitable power to issue the injunction, and that the restriction was narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest and preserved ample alternative channels of communication.

Resolution Trust Corp. v. Associated Gulf Contractors, Inc.


A-4259-91T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


263 N.J. Super. 332; 622 A.2d 1324; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 114


February 17, 1993, Argued  
March 31, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guarantor sought review of a default judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, that was entered when appellant failed to answer complaint in an action brought by appellee resolution trust corporation, and claimed that the judgment should be vacated because there were excusable neglect and meritorious defenses present in the matter.


OVERVIEW: Appellee resolution trust corporation, as assignee of mortgages and promissory notes, brought an action against appellant guarantor on the promissory notes. The trial court entered a default judgment in favor of appellee, and appellant moved to vacate on grounds that service of process was defective, and appellant had meritorious defenses to appellee's claims. The court affirmed the default judgment and held that appellant failed to meet his burden of clear and convincing evidence as to falsity of the sheriff's return and therefore personal service was valid and sufficient. The court further held that appellee qualified for status as "holder in due course" and was therefore guaranteed to be free of all personal defenses. The court noted that defenses to breach of contract and related matters were actually "claims" and thus barred from being heard in a trial court. The court also held that the proper forum for appellant's claims was not state court but in an administrative adjudication with appellee in its capacity as receiver according to mandatory and exclusive procedure of Financial Institutions Reform Recovery and Enforcement Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the default judgment against appellant guarantor and held that all issues of law raised were clearly without merit as service of process was valid and appellant raise no meritorious defenses to appellee resolution trust corporation's claims.

Horizon Health Center v. Felicissimo


A-1799-91T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


263 N.J. Super. 200; 622 A.2d 891; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 112


February 18, 1993, Argued  
March 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 19, 1993.
Certification granted Horizon Health Ctr. v. Felicissimo, 134 N.J. 480, 634 A.2d 527, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1070 (1993)
Modified by, Affirmed by, Remanded by Horizon Health Ctr. v. Felicissimo, 135 N.J. 126, 638 A.2d 1260, 1994 N.J. LEXIS 183 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Hudson County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant anti-abortion demonstrators sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, that made an order to restrain appellant's from demonstrating within 30 feet of respondent abortion clinic permanent. Appellant claimed the injunction violated appellant's constitutional right to free expression.


OVERVIEW: Respondent medical clinic sought to restrain appellant abortion protestors in the manner and place in which they could protest on the public ways outside of respondent's facility. The lower court made a temporary restraining order permanent and appellants sought review. The court affirmed the order and held that the injunction was content-neutral, noting that not all speech was immune from time, place and manner regulation. The court reasoned that the restraining order did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I because it protected respondents from loudness and physical intimidation, not from content of speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the permanent restraining order and held that it was not content-based regulation of free speech but focused specifically and exclusively on the location and manner of expression and therefore not a First Amendment violation.

 

973 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. American Banking Ins. Co. of Florida


A-705-91T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


263 N.J. Super. 124; 622 A.2d 261; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 100


December 15, 1992, Submitted  
March 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 5, 1993. As Corrected June 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Hudson County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent herewith. No costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a bail bondsman and insurer, sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Hudson County (New Jersey), that declared void a mortgage in which appellant had a security interest, and appellants argued that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-5 protected their security interest from forfeiture to appellee state.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state brought an action to settle the validity of a mortgage, held by appellant bail bondsman, on defendant's property that was seized by the government when defendant failed to appear for court. The trial court declared the mortgage void and appellant sought review on the basis that as holders of a perfected security interest in the property their interest was excepted from forfeiture by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-5. The court reversed and remanded the case and held that under the statute, a perfected security interest held by one with no knowledge of the proscribed activity was exempt from forfeiture, and that under the innocent owner's defense, those who took an interest in property that was not prima facie contraband, even after an illegal use, could still have their interest exempt from forfeiture. The court further held that the proper inquiry into whether an interest holder had knowledge of the act upon which the forfeiture was based should include whether the interest holder did what reasonably could have been expected to find out if the property had been illegally used.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for further proceedings and held that the forfeiture statute protected appellant bail bondsman who in good faith and without knowledge of wrongdoing took an interest in property and did what reasonably could have been expected to find out if property had been illegally used.

Hillsdale PBA Local 207 v. Borough of Hillsdale


A-2750-91T5, A-4855-91T2 Consolidated


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


263 N.J. Super. 163; 622 A.2d 872; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 95


February 1, 1993, Argued  
March 17, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 1, 1993. As Corrected June 16, 1993. As Corrected June 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Bergen County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boroughs challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which summarily confirmed the separate opinions and awards of the arbitrators appointed by the Public Employment Relations Commission in binding interest arbitration with respondent local unions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant boroughs and appellee local unions were unable to resolve disputed economic issues of salary increases for the police forces. The matter was presented for interest arbitration to resolve the dispute. The arbitrators chose the offer of the local unions. Interest arbitration was statutorily mandated in the public sector for impasse disputes between municipal employers and police and firemen pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:13A-16. Appellants argued that the awards should be vacated. The court agreed. It held that the interest arbitrators were required to consider the statutory factors outlined in N.J. Stat. Ann. 34:13A-16(g) and to issue a signed opinion based on a reasonable determination of those factors. The court held that neither of the arbitrators sufficiently considered the statutory factors. Where the award was not supported by substantial credible evidence in the record, the award could be vacated on judicial review. Finding the record not to contain substantial credible evidence, the court vacated the awards and remanded for new arbitration hearings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and vacated the arbitration awards. The court remanded the matters for new arbitration hearings.
