State v. Laws


A-6672-89T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


262 N.J. Super. 551; 621 A.2d 526; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 72


January 20, 1993, Argued  
March 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 23, 1993. As Corrected May 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County for possession of cocaine, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5a(1), distribution of cocaine, § 2C:35-5a(1), possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, § 2C:35-5b(3), possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, § 2C:35-7, and employing a juvenile in a drug distribution scheme, § 2C:35-6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for possession of cocaine, distribution of cocaine, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, and employing a juvenile in a drug distribution scheme. The court rejected defendant's claim that the state should have had to disclose the location of the surveillance point from which an officer witnessed defendant's involvement in a drug exchange. The court noted that defendant cross-examined the officer at trial regarding all of the factors which could have obscured his view and that any further examination would have pinpointed the location, thus jeopardizing ongoing operations as well as the public safety and personal safety of the officers. However, the court reversed defendant's conviction for employing a juvenile in a drug distribution scheme, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-6, because the trial court misstated the law with respect to determination of who controlled the drug transaction involving an adult and a juvenile. The court found defendant's claims regarding the sufficiency of the evidence and his presentment to the grand jury meritless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for employing a juvenile in a drug distribution scheme and remanded the charge for retrial. The court held that the trial court misstated the law regarding determination of whether the adult or juvenile controlled the drug transaction, requiring reversal. The court affirmed defendant's remaining convictions and remanded the matter for resentencing.

 

976 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Exxon Corp. v. Hunt


A-2044-91T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


262 N.J. Super. 264; 620 A.2d 1068; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 54


February 2, 1993, Submitted  
February 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 17, 1993. As Corrected March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporations sought review of an order of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which denied their petition of a modification of the remedy fashioned by the supreme court based upon a new ruling from the United States Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporations paid $ 8,142,094.00 in taxes to the New Jersey Spill Fund. During remand proceedings ordered by the supreme court, plaintiffs moved for an order mandating a full refund of those Spill Fund taxes which were pre-empted by CERCLA. Plaintiffs argued that a recent holding of the United States Supreme Court required a modification of the remedy fashioned by the supreme court. The lower court ruled that it was obliged to follow strictly the mandate of the state supreme court and refused to modify it in any way. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the lower court, holding that only portions of the Spill Fund were expressly pre-empted by CERCLA. Thus, the court held that the taxes paid by plaintiffs during the pre-emption period were valid as levies to fund those Spill Fund objectives that were determined not to have been pre-empted under federal law. Therefore, the court concluded that plaintiffs had no enforceable claim to a refund of any portion of the funds as long as all Spill Fund revenues expended for pre-empted purposes during the period of pre-emption were returned to the fund from general revenues within a reasonable time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court, holding that plaintiff corporations were not entitled to a refund of the invalid tax because other sections were valid. The court concluded that the tax itself was not invalid for any reason. Thus, plaintiffs had no enforceable claim to a refund as long as all revenues expended for pre-empted purposes were returned from general revenues within a reasonable time period.

 

977 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Disomma


A-6087-91T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


262 N.J. Super. 375; 621 A.2d 55; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 66


January 25, 1993, Submitted  
February 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 19, 1993. As Corrected May 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Criminal Part, Atlantic County.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the determination of the Law Division and reinstate the judgment of the Brigantine Municipal Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the state both challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Atlantic County (New Jersey), which affirmed defendant's conviction of driving while intoxicated, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50. The appellate court held that defendant's conviction for refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50.4a, could be considered in imposing second offender status but refused to impose the punishment for his second violation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was first convicted for refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50.4a. He was then convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50. At sentencing, the trial judge refused to impose second offender status under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50(a)(2) on defendant based on his refusal conviction. On appeal, the DWI conviction was affirmed. The appellate court held that while the refusal conviction could be considered for second offender status, a mandatory prison term could not be constitutionally imposed for the second violation. The defendant appealed and the state cross-appealed. The court held that the refusal conviction could not be a basis for imposing second offender status. The court held that an interpretation of § 39:4-50(a)(2) that treated a prior violation of the refusal statute as a first offense ignored the different burdens of proof of each one. Section 39:4-50 was quasi-criminal in nature and required guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, whereas § 39:4-50(a) was civil in nature and required proof by a preponderance of the evidence. Thus, the court reversed the lower court's decision and reinstated the original judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and reinstated the original judgment. The court held that defendant's prior conviction for refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test could not be the basis for imposing second offender status upon him for sentencing purposes for his later driving while intoxicated conviction, as to do so disregarded the different burdens of proof required for each offense.

 

978 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Cherry Hill Tp. v. Oxford House, Inc.


A-5572-91T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


263 N.J. Super. 25; 621 A.2d 952; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 80


December 9, 1992, Argued  
February 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residential program challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which ordered the residents of the home operated by appellant to be evicted because they did not satisfy the definition of family contained in respondent township's ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nonprofit organization established two independent, self-supporting, self-governing homes where recovering alcoholics and addicts could live together and provide mutual support. Respondent township filed a complaint alleging that the properties were occupied in violation of several ordinances, the Municipal Land Use Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7, and the drug-free school zone law. The trial court entered an order for the occupants to vacate the premises. The court reversed. The court held that the ordinance that restricted use of properties to single families must have a functional standard for determining whether a use qualified as a single housekeeping unit to satisfy due process. The court found that the ordinance, which on its face did not have a functional standard, was unconstitutional. The court held that if the residents were recovering alcoholics and addicts, they were protected as handicapped individuals under the Fair Housing Act but a plenary hearing was required to adjudicate that issue. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the eviction order entered by the trial court, affirmed the order denying summary judgment to appellant residential program in part, and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The court held that appellee township's ordinance concerning permissible domestic arrangements was unconstitutionally vague and a final plenary hearing was required to determine if residence had federal protections.

 

979 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Harper-Lawrence, Inc. v. United Merchants and Mfrs., Inc.


A-2394-90T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


261 N.J. Super. 554; 619 A.2d 623; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 28


October 8, 1992, Argued  
January 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment appealed from is vacated and the case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual appealed a summary judgment from the Bergen County Superior Court of New Jersey, dismissing his claim to a real estate commission. Defendant purchaser appealed from the judgment against her and from the judgment, which failed to award her full indemnification. Plaintiff corporation cross-appealed because the judgment entered in its favor was for the principal amount of $ 165,000, rather than for $ 330,000.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, corporation and individual, were Realtors who claimed that they were entitled to a real estate commission because they procured defendant tenant for a building that defendant purchaser bought from defendant company. Defendant purchaser appealed from a judgment against her; plaintiff individual appealed from the order for summary judgment, which dismissed his claim; and plaintiff corporation cross-appealed from the judgment in its favor because it was entered for the principal amount of $ 165,000 rather than for $ 330,000, the amount of the jury's verdict. On review, the court found that the summary judgment dismissing plaintiff individual's claim was correct because he was not authorized to sue to collect the commission. Further, because the necessary elements for tortious interference with a prospective advantage were not proved, the trial court should have granted defendant purchaser's request for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Finally, the court concluded that the trial court correctly reduced the award in favor of plaintiff corporation. Accordingly, the judgment was vacated and the case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered in favor of plaintiff corporation and against defendant purchaser was vacated and the case was remanded. Although the trial court correctly dismissed plaintiff individual's claims and reduced the judgment in favor of plaintiff corporation, the trial court erred in failing to grant defendant purchaser's motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict because plaintiff corporation failed to prove any wrongdoing.

 

980 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State, Dept. of Environmental Protection and Energy, Div. of Fish, Game and Wildlife v. Santomauro


A-2881-91T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


261 N.J. Super. 339; 618 A.2d 917; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 16


December 7, 1992, Submitted  
January 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Special Civil Part, Monmouth County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a civil penalty proceeding in the Superior Court of New Jersey, defendant was found to have violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:4-27 by offering for sale two stuffed deer heads, with antlers. He challenged the decision, arguing that it was barred by res judicata or collateral estoppel, that the heads were not covered by the statute, that he had been selectively prosecuted, and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower court's decision in a civil penalty proceeding that defendant had violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:4-27 by offering for sale two deer heads, with antlers. It rejected his claim that res judicata barred the instant action because he had been acquitted of similar charges in 1990, finding that the cases did not arise out of the same transaction. It held that collateral estoppel did not apply because one head used the same antlers involved in the 1990 action, adding that the clear language of the statute, the lack of legislative history and prior court decisions, and the concerns the statute addressed all militated against the application of collateral estoppel as well. Moreover, it noted, there was no indication of what grounds the 1990 court relied upon in acquitting defendant. It rejected defendant's argument that the statute did not apply to deer that were not native to New Jersey, finding that the modifying phrase in question referred only to birds, as well as his argument that the skin of a deer was not a body part under the statute. It found no merit to his claims that he had been selectively prosecuted or that the statute was overbroad and vague.


OUTCOME: Finding that the civil penalty proceeding against defendant, who was found to have illegally offered for sale two deer heads, was not barred by res judicata or collateral estoppel, the court affirmed the lower court's decision that he had violated the statute. It also found that the heads were covered under the statute, that defendant had not been selectively prosecuted, and that the statute was not vague or overbroad.

Matter of Assignment of Producers to Travelers Group


A-6511-91T1F, A-6512-91T1F, A-6513-91T1F, A-6600-91T1F, A-251-92T1F, A-546-92T1F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


261 N.J. Super. 292; 618 A.2d 894; 1993 N.J. Super. LEXIS 10


December 15, 1992, Argued  
January 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Order of the Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurers appealed orders from defendant Commissioner of Insurance (New Jersey), implementing and enforcing the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990, (FAIRA), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 to -63. At issue were the actions taken by defendant to effectuate the producer assignment program mandated by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-9c.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Commissioner of Insurance issued orders establishing a voluntary producer placement plan in implementation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-9b and a mandatory producer assignment program in implementation of § 17:33B-9c. Plaintiff insurers attacked N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11, § 3-42.12, which required them to enter into contractual relationships with assigned producers. The court held that this hybrid form of insurer representative, which lacked the element of binding authority, was of limited duration, and might be predicated on an enforceable scheme of indemnification of the insurer for other imputable acts of the representative, did not clearly implicate the basic constitutional and statutory considerations underlying plaintiffs' fundamental challenge. The constraints imposed upon plaintiffs' self-determination by having to contract with the producers in the manner prescribed was not an unconstitutional taking. Plaintiffs were bound by the "take all comers" requirement of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 to -63, thus they were necessarily required to accept the applications of all eligible persons. The court held that defendant's actions conformed to statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the general validity of orders of defendant Commissioner of Insurance appealed from on the ground that the clarified status of the producers imposed little more onus on plaintiff insurers than the "take all comers" provision itself of the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990. The court was satisfied that defendant's actions were in conformance with his statutory authority.

Limongelli v. N.J. State Bd. of Dentistry


A-811-91T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


260 N.J. Super. 346; 616 A.2d 945; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 403


October 19, 1992, Argued  
December 1, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 14, 1992.
Certification granted Limongelli v. New Jersey State Bd. of Dentistry, 133 N.J. 434, 627 A.2d 1140, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 661 (1993)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Limongelli v. New Jersey State Bd. of Dentistry, 137 N.J. 317, 645 A.2d 677, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 1583 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Final Decision of the New Jersey State Board of Dentistry.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the determination of the Board and remand for a plenary hearing in accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act and this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist challenged the final order of respondent New Jersey State Board of Dentistry (New Jersey), which denied his petition for relicensure and extended the suspension of his license to practice dentistry for an additional 10 years. The court considered appellant's argument that he had been denied due process by respondent's procedures.


OVERVIEW: Appellant dentist disputed a final order of respondent New Jersey State Board of Dentistry, which denied his petition for relicensure and extended the suspension of his license for ten years. The court held that, because appellant's license had been suspended, not revoked, he still had a property right in the license, which entitled him to due process. His license could be revived under the consent order to which he had agreed and also under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:6-7. Therefore, due process principles applied to respondent's proceedings. Although it was not directly applicable, under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14B-2 the proceedings were a contested case, to which the Administrative Procedure Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14B-1 et seq. (APA), applied. Appellant was entitled to various procedural rights under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14B-9. Respondent had not relied on appellant's own testimony in reaching in reaching its conclusions. Further, the statutes upon which it did rely did not apply. The court held that the lack of adequate notice, the lack of the opportunity to confront witnesses, and the failure to comply with the APA required a reversal and a remand for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a plenary hearing in accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act (APA) and the opinion. Because appellant dentist's license had been suspended, not revoked, he still had a property right, which entitled him to due process. The APA had not been followed. Appellant had not received adequate notice or an opportunity to confront the witnesses against him.

 

983 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Bussell v. Dewalt Products Corp.


A-2978-91T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


259 N.J. Super. 499; 614 A.2d 622; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 360


September 21, 1992, Argued  
October 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the successor in interest to the manufacturer of a radial arm saw, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, that held it liable for a judgment entered against the manufacturer in favor of respondent, who was injured while using the saw in the course of his employment.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was injured while using a radial arm saw and was awarded a jury verdict against the saw's manufacturer, on a finding that the saw was not reasonably safe for its intended purpose. He then sought to recover from appellant, the manufacturer's successor in interest, and the trial court held that appellant was liable for the judgment. Appellant contended that it was denied due process because no claim had been asserted against it, that Maryland law should control because it was domiciled therein, and that the theory of successor corporate liability was not viable and did not apply. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that where appellant had notice and an opportunity to be heard no due process rights were violated, and that New Jersey had the most significant interest in the litigation. It also held that appellant was strictly liable under the successor corporate liability theory, where in the transfer it received all assets and information related to the manufacture of radial arm saws. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting prejudgment interest where appellant was the real party in interest throughout the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that appellant's due process rights were not violated where it had notice of the suit from its inception as well as an opportunity to be heard, that New Jersey law controlled where that state had the most significant interest in the litigation, and that appellant was strictly liable under the successor corporate liability and product-line theories.

State v. Sette


A-5896-88T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


259 N.J. Super. 156; 611 A.2d 1129; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 311


April 15, 1992, Argued  
August 11, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.



DISPOSITION: The conviction on Count Three is reversed and remanded for a new trial; the convictions on the remaining counts are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, that convicted defendant of murder, attempted murder, aggravated assault, and possession of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, aggravated assault, and possession of a weapon. The court reversed the attempted murder conviction and remanded. The court held that the trial court gave the jury improper instructions on the attempted murder charge. The trial court erroneously informed the jury that defendant was guilty if they found defendant acted either purposely or knowingly. The court held that defendant could only be found guilty of attempted murder if he acted purposely. However, the court affirmed defendant's other convictions. The court held that the jury instruction on the defense of pathological intoxication was correct. The court held that the defense was only available if defendant was exposed to a pesticide and that alone altered defendant's mind. The court held involuntary intoxication did not occur if the pesticide was mixed with illegal drugs defendant voluntarily consumed prior to the crimes. The court held that the cross examination of defendant's expert about the jury verdict in a murder trial with a similar defense asserted of pesticide induced behavior was proper, as defendant's counsel misled the jury about that case's outcome.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's attempted murder conviction because improper jury instructions were given concerning the requisite mens rea for guilt. The court affirmed defendant's murder, aggravated assault, and possession of a weapon convictions, but remanded for overall resentencing.

State v. Kadelak


A-5944-90T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


258 N.J. Super. 599; 610 A.2d 916; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 306


April 28, 1992, Argued  
August 6, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. We do not retain jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his motion to suppress by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Burlington County, during his trial for driving while intoxicated. Defendant contended that the roadside safety check in which police stopped him violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 7.


OVERVIEW: A police department conducted a "roadside safety check" in which police stopped every fifth car, or any car with obvious safety problems. Police stopped defendant's truck because it was the fifth in line. Police found defendant intoxicated and charged him with driving while intoxicated (DWI). The municipal court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his intoxication. The trial court also denied the motion to suppress and found him guilty, but the trial court stayed the judgment pending appeal. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that police did not "randomly" stop vehicles at the unbridled discretion of police officers. The court found that the state presented no evidence to support the balance of legitimate governmental interests in its favor as opposed to the intrusion on defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV. However, because defendant did not give notice of his constitutional attack on N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:8-2, the court reversed and remanded for further consideration. The court ordered notice be given to the Attorney General of the attack on § 39:8-2, and permitted the state to supplement the record with appropriate evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his intoxication discovered during a police safety roadblock. The court found that the state did not prove a legitimate interest, as balanced against defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. However, because defendant failed to give notice about a constitutional attack on a statute, the court remanded for further proceedings.

E.I.B. by I.J. v. J.R.B.


A-1872-91T1F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


259 N.J. Super. 99; 611 A.2d 662; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 307


June 9, 1992, Submitted  
August 5, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] August 25, 1992, Approved for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hunterdon County.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse the order denying defendant's motion to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father challenged an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hunterdon County, that denied his motion to dismiss a paternity action brought by plaintiff grandmother on the child's behalf pursuant to the New Jersey Parentage Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:17-38 to -59 after finding that the action was not barred by res judicata.


OVERVIEW: A jury returned a verdict in favor of defendant putative father in a paternity action filed by the mother under prior N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:16-2 and 3 seeking child support. Plaintiff grandmother later filed an action on the child's behalf, this time under the New Jersey Parentage Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:17-38 to -59, for retroactive and prospective support, and defendant's motion to dismiss was denied when the trial court found that the action was not barred by res judicata. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that plaintiff was bound by the result of the first action by collateral estoppel. The paternity action by the mother made the same allegation (defendant was the child's father), sought essentially the same relief (an adjudication of paternity and the entry of a support order against defendant), and was actually litigated through trial and an appeal. The court determined that the child was in privity with her mother as required under collateral estoppel because although the child was not a named party in the first action, a proceeding under prior N.J. Stat. Ann. §9:16-3 was a representative action. Thus, the trial court improperly denied defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying defendant putative father's motion to dismiss a paternity action filed by plaintiff grandmother on behalf of the child because the action was barred by collateral estoppel, having been litigated under prior law by the child's mother.

N.J. State Bar Ass'n v. Berman


A-3457-90T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


259 N.J. Super. 137; 611 A.2d 1119; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 318


June 2, 1992, Argued  
August 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, whose opinion is reported at 11 N.J. Tax 433 (Tax Ct. 1991).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; modified in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the state bar association, appealed an order of the Tax Court of New Jersey (New Jersey) that upheld as constitutional Section 67 of the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-62, which assessed a fee on practicing attorneys.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assessed a fee, via Section 67 of the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act ("Act") of 1990, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-62, on attorneys practicing law in the state in order to pay off the debt created in the current insurance system so as to convert the citizens to a voluntary insurance market. Plaintiff, the state bar association, objected to the fee. The trial court affirmed the fee statute but exempted certain attorneys who the court held were not actively practicing law. The court affirmed, but included from exemption of the fee those attorneys barred from the practice of law by the constitution or statute, such as judges and judicial law clerks. The court held that the Act did not violate plaintiff's equal protection rights because the Act was rationally related to the state interest of insurance reform. The court found that assessing a fee on attorneys was rational because that profession benefited under the insurance system. However, the court found that certain attorneys were exempt from the fee because the statute required fee assessment only of those actively practicing law, and certain attorneys having a law license were not actively practicing law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, with modification, that permitted the assessment of a statutory fee on attorneys because the statute was rationally related to the state interest of insurance reform where the profession of law benefited under the insurance system. The court modified the order by exempting those attorneys not actively practicing law.

 

988 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jiminez


A-3266-90T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


257 N.J. Super. 567; 608 A.2d 996; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 267


March 17, 1992, Submitted  
July 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Essex County (New Jersey), convicting defendant of third-degree theft by receiving stolen property and two counts of second-degree reckless manslaughter. Defendant was sentenced on the theft charge to a term of five years, and he was sentenced to concurrent terms of ten years on the manslaughter convictions, consecutively served with the theft sentence.


OVERVIEW: Police officers chased a stolen vehicle driven by defendant. During the chase, the vehicle driven by defendant proceeded through a red light and collided into the driver's side of another vehicle. Both vehicles flew into the air on impact. Defendant's passenger and the driver of the other vehicle were both killed in the collision. Defendant argued that he was not the driver of the stolen vehicle. He also filed a motion for acquittal on the theft charge, but it was denied. Defendant was convicted of third-degree theft by receiving stolen property and second-degree reckless manslaughter. He was sentenced on the theft charge to a term of five years. On the manslaughter convictions, he was sentenced to concurrent terms of ten years, to be consecutively served with the theft sentence. The court held that the motion for acquittal was properly denied as to theft because the jury could infer from defendant's conduct that that he was seeking to elude police because of his knowledge that the vehicle was stolen. However, the manslaughter convictions were reversed and the case remanded for a new trial because the jury instructions did not accurately reflect the statutory law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's theft conviction and sentence were affirmed based on defendant's lack of permission to operate the movable property of another, and there was no trial court error because the evidence supported the findings of fact. However, the manslaughter convictions were reversed because the jury was not appropriately apprised of the quantitatively greater recklessness contemplated for manslaughter than that required for death by auto.

State v. Collette


A-5902-90T3, A-1032-91T3, A-6290-90T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


257 N.J. Super. 557; 608 A.2d 990; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 269


April 14, 1992, Argued  
July 1, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.



DISPOSITION: The appeals are dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, which entered acquittals in favor of appellees on charges of racketeering, bribery, official misconduct, and making gifts to public servants, in an action alleging that appellees, in return for money or other benefits, influenced the Atlantic City Zoning Board to act favorably upon certain commercial land use proposals.


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the judgment that granted acquittals in favor of appellees on charges of racketeering, bribery, official misconduct, and making gifts to public servants. The state alleged that appellees, in return for money, influenced the Atlantic City Zoning Board to act favorably on certain commercial land use proposals. The trial court held that because appellees were not members of the zoning board, they had no power to act in matters before the board. The state argued that the double jeopardy clause did not protect appellees because the trial court's determination was not based on factual insufficiencies in the state's case. The court dismissed the state's appeal and held that the Double Jeopardy Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. barred the retrial of appellees. The court held that the trial judge measured the state's evidence against its interpretation of the statutory elements and found the state's proofs to be inadequate. The court held that the disposition was an adjudication on the merits and was unappealable by the state.


OUTCOME: The state's appeal from the judgment acquitting appellees was dismissed because the acquittal of appellees by the trial court was an adjudication on the merits and was unappealable by the state.

New Jersey State League of Municipalities v. State


A-1936-90T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


257 N.J. Super. 509; 608 A.2d 965; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 259


March 10, 1992, Argued; May 26, 1992, Submitted  
June 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Briefs Requested on March 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County.

Supplemental briefs requested March 16, 1992 1


1 The supplemental briefs addressed the effect of the Legislature's enactment of L. 1991, c. 213 on July 23, 1991 after the original briefs of the parties had been filed with the court. The constitutionality of this later enactment was upheld by the Law Division and is the subject of a separate appeal. We decline to consider the possible conflict between these two enactments in this appeal.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Law Division is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state challenged the decision from the Superior Court, Burlington County (New Jersey), which ruled that N.J. Stat. Ann. 40:67-23.2 et seq. violated the Equal Protection Clause of both the state and federal constitution, and which therefore found the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, several municipalities and condominium dwellers, filed a lawsuit against defendant state challenging the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. 40:67-23.2 et seq. (the act), which excluded apartment complexes from those qualified private communities for which plaintiffs were required to provide certain municipal services. The trial court held that the act was underinclusive, and violative of equal-protection guarantees. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that the act's distinction between apartment owners and condominium owners was irrational because a significant percentage of condominium owners also rent their units, thus making them similarly situated to apartment owners. However, the court found that the act's main purpose, to relieve condominium owners of the burden of paying twice for municipal services, was a valid legislative purpose. Furthermore, even though the act grouped all condominium co-owners without distinguishing between resident and non-resident owners, most owners satisfied act's intended purpose. Therefore, there was a rational basis for the legislation. The trial court's judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision, that N.J. Stat. Ann. 40:67-23.2 et seq. (the act) violated the Equal Protection Clause of both the state and federal constitution and was therefore unconstitutional, was reversed. The act's main purpose, to relieve condominium owners of the burden of paying twice for municipal services, was a valid legislative purpose. Furthermore, there was a rational basis for the act's classifications.

Board of Educ. of Borough of Englewood Cliffs, Bergen County v. Board of Educ. of City of Englewood, Bergen County

Certification granted Board of Educ. of Englewood Cliffs v. Board of Educ. of Englewood, 130 N.J. 600, 617 A.2d 1222, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 1450 (1992)
Certification granted Board of Educ. of Englewood Cliffs v. Board of Educ. of Englewood, 130 N.J. 600, 617 A.2d 1222, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 1449 (1992)
Certification granted Board of Educ. of Englewood Cliffs v. Board of Educ. of Englewood, 130 N.J. 600, 617 A.2d 1222, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 1448 (1992)
Affirmed by Board of Educ. v. Board of Educ., 132 N.J. 327, 625 A.2d 483, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 106 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, board of education, sought review of a decision from the New Jersey State Board of Education that denied petitioner's request for severance of a sending-receiving relationship with respondent high school board under which petitioner had sent its high school students to respondent's high school.


OVERVIEW: Petition board of education sought to sever a sending-receiving agreement with respondent high school board wherein petitioner sent its students to respondent's high school. The New Jersey State Board of Education denied the request. On appeal, petitioner contended that the board erred in its determination that a grant of severance would result in substantial negative impact upon respondent, and that the board's decision violated U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court rejected petitioner's contentions, finding that the board's conclusion concerning negative impact was proper because of the long term effect upon the racial balance and educational quality at respondent's high school. The court noted that the relevant statute required denial of severance once a negative impact was found, and that it did not permit a balancing of negative and positive impacts. The court held that the denial of severance was not unconstitutional because the state was permitted to consider race in its educational decisions. The court noted that the board found the petition for severance was motivated by racial prejudice. Accordingly, the court affirmed the board's determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the New Jersey State Board of Education that found in favor of respondent high school board. The court held that once a substantial negative impact upon respondent's high school was determined, the relevant statute required the denial of petitioner board of education's request for severance from the sending-receiving agreement.

 

992 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stelzner


A-5963-89T3, A-6030-89T3, A-6036-89T3, A-6113-89T3, A-6157-89T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


257 N.J. Super. 219; 608 A.2d 386; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 239


April 1, 1992, Argued and Submitted  
June 11, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Atlantic County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were indicted with conspiracy, theft by deception, and swindling and cheating at casino gambling, collectively appealed from a decision of the Superior Court, Law Division, Atlantic County (New Jersey), which denied their motions for suppression of hotel billing records and other evidence arising out of an investigation into a card-shuffling scheme.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted with conspiracy, theft by deception, and swindling and cheating at casino gambling. The trial court denied defendants' motions for suppression of hotel billing records and other evidence arising out of an investigation into a card-shuffling scheme. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the hotel's telephone billing records were not illegally obtained by a police officer. Even if evidence of improper motive was present, subjective bad motive did not invalidate a warrantless seizure that was objectively reasonable. Further, the evidence demonstrated that a hotel clerk's actions were not sufficiently influenced by the police officer to require the conclusion that she was a state actor. The officer was neither present when the clerk printed out the telephone record nor did he direct or encourage her to do so. The court stated that swindlers could be prosecuted under the Casino Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-1 et seq., and face 18 months and a fine of up to $ 25,000, or they could be prevented from achieving economic windfall by prosecution for theft-by-deception under Title 2A. The two criminal prohibitions were not inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendants of conspiracy, theft by deception, and swindling and cheating at casino gambling. The court concluded that hotel billing records were not illegally obtained by police officer and that statutory criminal prohibitions were not inconsistent.

 

993 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Farmers' Mut. Fire Assur. Ass'n of New Jersey


A-3648-90T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


256 N.J. Super. 607; 607 A.2d 1019; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 200


April 28, 1992, Argued  
May 22, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State of New Jersey, Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance company sought review from the State of New Jersey, Department of Insurance, with regard to whether an insurer was entitled to a hearing on its request for an exemption, abatement, or deferral under the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 to17:33B-63.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner insurance company sought declaratory relief as to whether an insurer was entitled to a hearing on its request for an exemption, abatement, or deferral under the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990 (FAIR act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 to 17:33B-63. The Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990 (FAIR act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-1 to 17:33B-63, required the Property Liability Insurance Guaranty Association (PLIGA) to collect assessments from its members to be used to relieve the deficit of the New Jersey Full Insurance Underwriting Association (JUA). The act empowered the commissioner of insurance to exempt, abate or defer an assessment if an insurer is at risk because of its unsafe or unsound financial condition. The court found that the FAIR act afforded an insurer the right to a hearing on its claim for an exemption, that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and that administrative regulations were necessary to guide the commissioner of insurance in the exercise of his statutory powers.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded because the court concluded that agency rule making was reasonably required to fulfill the legislative purpose of the statutes as such action was consistent with the judicial recognition that agency rulemaking was necessary to inform the public and guide the agency in discharging its authorized functions.

 

994 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Patton


A-2053-90T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


256 N.J. Super. 413; 607 A.2d 191; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 187


February 13, 1992, Argued  
May 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment against him entered by the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey) in favor of the state. The superior court reinstated defendant's conviction for a disorderly persons offense after finding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-10c was constitutional when read to provide for use and fruits immunity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen removing something from his pocket which he dropped on the floor. An inspectors retrieved the object, which turned out to be a folded bill containing a white powdery substance, stipulated at trial to be cocaine. Defendant was indicted for third-degree possession of cocaine, but the state downgraded the charge to the disorderly persons offense. Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty. However, on defendant's motion, the judge arrested the judgment, concluding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-10c unconstitutionally infringed on the privilege against self-incrimination. The state appealed, and a second judge reinstated the conviction, finding that the statute was constitutional if read to provide for use and fruits immunity. Defendant appealed from that judgment arguing that plaintiff's appeal should have been dismissed because the court was the correct appellate venue. The judgment on appeal was reversed, and the earlier order for acquittal was reinstated as whatever route, the issue would have been before the court, and that the statute on the privilege against self-incrimination was a full defense to the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered on the appeal was reversed, and the earlier order for arrest of judgment and for judgment of acquittal was reinstated because a proper assertion of the privilege against self-incrimination was a full defense to the prosecution against defendant.

 

995 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomas


A-4540-89T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


256 N.J. Super. 563; 607 A.2d 997; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 198


April 28, 1992, Submitted  
May 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Approved for Publication June 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, contending that the evidence did not prove that the school building near the offense was used for school purposes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of, among other controlled substance offenses, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and possession of the same drug with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, and sought review. On appeal the court held that the conviction for possession with intent to distribute merged with that for possession near school property and reversed the former conviction. Defendant contended that the prosecution failed to prove that the school building within 1,000 feet of the offense was used for school purposes as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. The court affirmed the conviction for possession with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, holding that the map introduced into evidence that labelled the building as a school created a permissive inference from which the jury, absent evidence to the contrary, could properly find that it was used for school purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, but reversed his conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, which was merged with the previous conviction. The admission of a map showing a building labelled a school created a permissive inference from which the jury could find that the building was used for school purposes.

 

996 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Battle


A-4677-89T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


256 N.J. Super. 268; 606 A.2d 1119; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 180


January 7, 1992, Argued  
May 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which convicted defendant of aggravated assault upon a police officer and resisting arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for possession of marijuana, possession with the intent to distribute, aggravated assault upon a police officer, and second degree escape after a traffic stop. The court granted defendant's motion to suppress the marijuana evidence solely on the charges of possession and intent to distribute and the state's motion to dismiss the marijuana charges. Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault upon a police officer and resisting arrest. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that even though evidence was obtained in violation of U.S. Const. amend IV, it had been properly admitted as to the non-drug charges because defendant had admitted to attempting to escape police detention. The court held that although defendant had no notice before trial of the charge of resisting arrest, a valid waiver was found where defense counsel had participated in the decision and then expressed consent to the charge on the record. The court held that merger was improper because the offense of aggravated assault was concerned with physical protection of police officers and the offense of resisting arrest was to prevent persons from resisting police apprehension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated assault upon a police officer and resisting arrest because evidence of defendant's possession of marijuana, which was excluded with respect to defendant's drug charges upon a finding that the search was unlawful, was admissible in the trial of offenses that occurred after the stop and search were effected.

 

997 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Town of Secaucus v. Hudson County Bd. of Taxation


A-6663-89T5, A-311-90T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 665; 605 A.2d 1151; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 151


March 18, 1992, Argued  
April 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 7, 1992.
Certification granted by Secaucus v. Hudson County Bd. of Taxation, 130 N.J. 396, 614 A.2d 618, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 981 (1992)
Affirmed by, Modified by Town of Secaucus v. Hudson County Bd. of Taxation, 133 N.J. 482, 628 A.2d 288, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 746 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and county board sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, which held that a statute permitting the county board to exempt the city from assessment of taxes relating to the funding of a county vocational school district was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: New Jersey passed N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:54-37, which had the effect of exempting the taxpayers of only defendant city from contributing to the support of their county vocational school district. To accommodate the exemption, defendant county board adopted a two-tiered county tax rate, the higher rate for its municipalities, the lower rate for defendant city. Numerous municipalities filed suit and the trial court found the statute unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, noting that if the responsibility for the state function were assigned to local government, the local tax must fall uniformly upon all taxable property within the county or the municipality as per N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 1, paras. 1 and 2. The court noted that they were not dealing with an exemption of real property from taxation; they were dealing with a lack of uniformity caused by excusing defendant city from having to pay its proportionate share of the cost of a budget item. The court held that the statute that excused the city from funding the county vocational school district was unconstitutional because it permitted lack of uniformity in taxing taxpayers their proportional share of budget items.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, for different reasons than the trial judge, that exception of defendant city from taxes for that portion of the budget relating to county vocational school district was unconstitutional. The court found that the tax exemption was in violation of the state constitution's tax uniformity provisions.

 

998 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


N.J. v. Rosado


A-6678-89T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


256 N.J. Super. 126; 606 A.2d 835; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 154


March 24, 1992, Submitted  
April 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 7, 1992. As Corrected May 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey), which found that defendant had violated conditions of his probation and imposed the maximum base term and the mandatory minimum sentence for defendant's earlier conviction for violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. Defendant was not given credit for time spent on parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sentence that was imposed after his probation was revoked and the fact that he was not given credit for time spent on parole. The court ordered the trial court to vacate the mandatory minimum term, impose a four-year prison term in lieu of the maximum five-year base term imposed, and for provision that defendant be given credit for jail time and parole time served under the 364-day sentence originally imposed as a condition of his probation. The court held that on resentencing, defendant was entitled to the benefit of the state's waiver of the statutory minimum mandatory term because he was not told that the waiver was conditional. The court held that the record did not support imposition of the maximum base term. The pecuniary-incentive factor was inappropriately applied because it rested solely on the charge of possession with intent to distribute, and the deterrence factor did not sufficiently outweigh the mitigating factor of no prior criminal activity. Finally, the court held that parole was a continuation of custody and that both jail time and parole time counted toward service of the prison term imposed on the resentence.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for vacation of the mandatory minimum term, because defendant was not informed that the state's waiver at the original sentencing was conditional, and imposition of a four-year prison term, because the record did not support imposition of the maximum base term. Defendant was entitled to credit for time served on parole because parole was a continuation of custody, not a termination of imprisonment.

Mechanical Contractors Ass'n of New Jersey, Inc. v. State


A-3661-90T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 488; 605 A.2d 743; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 130


December 9, 1991, Argued  
April 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION APRIL 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractors' associations sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Union County (New Jersey), which denied its motion for summary judgment, granted summary judgment for defendant state agencies and officials and intervenor labor unions and other interested parties, and declared N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14C-2(g) unconstitutional, as its distinction between work inside and outside the property or curb line had no rational basis.


OVERVIEW: The definition of "plumbing" in the State Plumbing License Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14C-1 et seq., was amended to reserve installation or removal of pipes and plumbing fixtures between a building and a property line to licensed master plumbers. The attorney general issued an opinion that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14C-2(g) was unconstitutional. Plaintiff contractors' associations challenged the opinion. The trial court denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, granted summary judgment for defendant state agencies and officials and intervenors labor unions and other interested parties, and declared § 45:14C-2(g) unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the amended definition of "plumbing" was contrary both to traditional definitions and to the National Standard Plumbing Code, adopted by N.J. Admin. Code tit. 5, § 23-3.15(a)(1). The court held that plaintiffs had not alleged or proven that the unlicensed laborers who had historically performed the work were incompetent to do so, or that there was any danger to the public welfare. The court held that disenfranchisement of this labor force with no rational basis was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment for defendant state agencies and officials and intervenor labor unions and other interested parties, and affirmed the declaration that the statute defining "plumbing" was unconstitutional, as it was contrary both to traditional definitions and to the National Standard Plumbing Code and disenfranchised a labor force despite no evidence that the laborers were incompetent to perform the work.

 

1000 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 7:1e


A-921-91T2F


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 469; 605 A.2d 733; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 128


March 10, 1992, Argued  
April 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION APRIL 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection and Energy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trade association sought review of a decision of respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection and Energy, which adopted regulations that implemented amendments to the New Jersey Spill Compensation and Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11.


OVERVIEW: Respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection and Energy adopted regulations that implemented amendments to the New Jersey Spill Compensation and Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11. Specifically, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 1E-1.6, required that all discharges of hazardous substances into the water or onto the lands of the state be immediately reported. Appellant trade association sought review of respondent's adoption of the regulations. The court affirmed respondent's actions because it was clear that the regulations under N.J. Admin. Code. Tit. 7, § 1E did not exceed the enabling legislation that gave respondent the authority to implement the amendments. The court found that "discharge" and "hazardous substances" were described with adequate specificity in the regulations and the regulations were sufficiently definite to inform those subject to them as to what was required. The court also found that there were innumerable applications of the regulations that were clear and not in any sense vague or subject to doubt. Thus, even if the regulations were subject to question in some of their applications, they were not facially invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection and Energy's adoption of regulations designed to prevent discharge of hazardous substances because the regulations did not exceed the enabling legislation that authorized respondent to adopt the regulations, and the regulations were not constitutionally invalid.
